## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 15:08 UTC

I've read the core of it. Here's my honest read — diagnosis first, then where I'd take it.

## The headline

Nothing is "broken" in the sense of being amateurish — this is actually *sophisticated* code. That's the problem. You built a physically-motivated continuous-energy fracture model and then discovered that physics doesn't cooperate with a game where objects span five orders of magnitude in the energy term. So you've been patching the gap between "physical" and "fun" with magic numbers, and the patching is what's now unmaintainable. The energy model didn't fail because it's wrong; it failed because it's *physical*, and you don't actually want physical.

## Why the energy model is untunable (the real diagnosis)

The core is reduced-mass kinetic energy, [FractureService.cs:88-93](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L88-L93):

```
E = ½ · mRed · vRelN²,  mRed = m₁m₂/(m₁+m₂)
threshold = Toughness · (bodyMass · cellArea/totalArea)
```

Four structural reasons this can't be tuned to feel good:

**1. You're spanning ~5 orders of magnitude and papering over it with a fudge factor.** A bullet is light+fast (m≈0.2, v≈2500 → E≈625,000). An asteroid-on-asteroid hit is heavy+slow. The same formula can't serve both, so you bolted on `asteroidEnergyScale = 0.0002` ([game_config.json:586](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json#L586)) — a **5000× correction**. That number isn't physics; it's a confession that the model doesn't unify the two regimes. Every time you add an object with a new mass/speed profile, you'll need a new fudge.

**2. `Toughness` does two jobs at once.** It sets the *ignition threshold* (`Toughness · struckMass`, [FractureSimulator.cs:115](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs#L115)) **and** the *propagation cost* (bond strength = edgeLength × Toughness, spent in [FractureKernel.cs:95-98](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L95-L98)). One knob, two nonlinearly-coupled roles. You can't adjust "how hard to start a crack" without also changing "how far it spreads."

**3. Mass enters the break decision twice, with opposite signs.** A big asteroid couples *more* energy (bigger mRed) but also has a *higher* cell threshold (bigger struckMass). These partly cancel in a way nobody can predict by eye — so "does this shot crack this rock" depends on body size through two competing terms.

**4. The output is unpredictable by construction.** A continuous energy budget is spent breaking *discrete* bonds in descending-energy flood order, with directional weighting, transmission decay, `BoostCap`, `DirExponent`. "How big a chunk comes off for energy E" has no closed form — it's emergent from graph topology. You can *only* tune it by trial-and-error, and every material/weapon/size combination is a different trial.

There's also a tell that the model already gave up on physics in places: fragment fling is scaled to bullet **speed**, not momentum ([FractureService.cs:96-99](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L96-L99), "intuitive + visible, not physical"), and the weapon `energy: 1200` field ([game_config.json:84](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json#L84)) **isn't even used** for the player's own shots — the formula uses `bulletMass × bulletVel²`. `energy` only survives as a denominator for alien-bullet scaling ([PlayingState.cs:990](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs#L990)). So you have a config field named "energy" that doesn't set the energy. The model is already half-abandoned; it just hasn't been replaced.

### Where I'd take the model

Stop modeling energy. Model **damage in normalized, dimensionless units**, designed around the decision you actually care about ("did this chunk come off, and how big"):

- **One impact scalar, normalized to ≈1 for a baseline hit.** Define `S = penetration / cellToughness` where penetration is whatever you want gameplay-wise (a per-weapon constant × hit, plus a small velocity term). A cannon shot = S≈1, a piercing round = S≈3, asteroid bonk = S≈0.5. Now toughness means "needs S>1 to chip," which is *readable*.
- **Decouple the two toughness roles.** `IgnitionThreshold` (start a crack) and `BondCost` (propagation reach) become separate fields. Now "chips easily but cracks don't travel" (ductile) vs "hard to start but shatters fully" (brittle glass) are two independent sliders instead of one tangled one.
- **Kill `mRed`/KE entirely.** Mass/size effects come back as explicit, *bounded* multipliers you choose, not as a quadratic that explodes. No more per-regime EnergyScale.
- **Keep the bond-graph propagation** — that part is genuinely good and gives you the cool emergent shapes. Just feed it a normalized budget instead of joules.

The fling/visual velocities can stay speed-scaled exactly as they are; they were never the problem.

## Code organization — yes, it's a real problem

**[PlayingState.cs](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs) is a 2730-line god object.** It is, by my count, ~8 systems wearing a trenchcoat: wave spawning, procedural asteroid generation (incl. point-in-polygon and distribution sampling), player/alien/mothership spawning, *every* event handler (bullet hit, collision, pulverize, fracture-completed, fracture-split, grenade), the entire boss AI (shockwave/black-hole/ram/spawners), and the entire HUD + world rendering. Your own [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) says *"Semantic responses (damage, splits, score) live in game-layer systems subscribed to CollisionEvent."* They don't — they're private methods in PlayingState. **The architecture you documented is not the architecture you built.** That gap is most of your "badly organized" feeling.

**The demo is a divergent fork of the game.** [Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs](GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs) (2206 lines) re-implements `OnBulletHit`/`OnCollision`/asteroid-fracture/shotgun-cone almost verbatim from PlayingState — same `EmitFlash(0.5f·bulletMass·…)`, same asteroid `WeaponProfile`, same cone math. And [ConfigExtensions.cs](GameEngine/Game/ConfigExtensions.cs) is literally duplicated in both. Every fracture bug is now a two-file fix, and they've already drifted.

**Config has multiple sources of truth and dead entries:**
- The `materials` block in JSON is an exact copy of the hardcoded `Glass/Ice/Rock/Metal` presets in [FractureProperties.cs:76-86](GameEngine/Engine/Components/FractureProperties.cs#L76-L86). Two sources.
- `vortex` appears **twice** ([game_config.json:561](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json#L561) and [:789](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json#L789)) with different values — JSON silently keeps the second, so the first block is dead. That's drift you can't even see.
- Cell cap lives in both `maxLiveCells: 2000` and `waveSystem.maxCellCap: 2000`.
- A manual `waves[]` array *and* a procedural `waveSystem` block coexist — two wave systems.

## How I'd sequence the refactor

I would **not** rewrite the fracture engine first — it's the part that works. Order by leverage:

1. **Extract systems out of PlayingState** into the `ISystem`/`EventBus` pattern you already documented (`FractureResponseSystem`, `BossSystem`, `WaveSpawnSystem`, `HudDrawSystem`, …). This alone makes everything after it tractable, and it forces the demo and game to *share* those systems instead of forking. Biggest win, lowest risk.
2. **One config source of truth.** Delete the C# material presets (or generate JSON from them), de-dupe the `vortex`/cellcap/wave entries, pick one wave system. Mechanical, high-relief.
3. **Then** swap the energy model behind the now-single `FractureResponseSystem` boundary — replace `½mRed·v²` + EnergyScale with the normalized-damage scalar. Because step 1 made fracture-invocation live in *one* place, this becomes a contained change instead of a shotgun edit.

Steps 1–2 don't change behavior, so you can verify nothing regressed before you touch the thing you actually want to redesign.

Or if you'd rather, I can start with the highest-leverage piece — carving the event handlers out of PlayingState into real systems — and show you the shape on one of them first. Which way do you want to go?

Is it possible to have a physics realistic energy model that could adapt to both the bullet-asteroids collisions and the asteroids-asteroids / ship-asteroids collisions?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 15:24 UTC

Good — and this is the right thing to be unsure about, because there's a genuine physics fact hiding here that the current model walked into blind. Let me give you the honest version.

## The uncomfortable truth first

You asked: *can one physically-realistic model serve both bullet→asteroid and asteroid→asteroid?*

A single **dimensionally-consistent** model: yes, easily. A single **realistic** model where **bullets are still the dominant destruction tool**: no — and that's not a modelling failure, it's a physics fact. In reality:

- Two 5000-unit asteroids closing at 100 give dissipated energy ≈ ½·μ·v² ≈ **12 million**.
- Your 0.2-unit bullet at 2500 gives ≈ **0.6 million**, and its *momentum* (what actually drives penetration) is ~500 vs the asteroid contact's ~300,000.

So a real bullet is the puny object in the room. Your `asteroidEnergyScale = 0.0002` wasn't fixing a units bug — it was **forcing the anti-physical ordering you want for gameplay** (bullets shatter, bumps are gentle). Any fully-realistic model will fight you on this forever, because you're asking the pebble to beat the mountain.

The resolution isn't "more physics" or "less physics." It's recognizing you have **two energy *sources* that should share one *pipeline* but not one *formula*.**

## The model I'd build

**One fracture pipeline, one currency (impulse/energy in consistent units), two sources feeding it:**

### Source A — physical collisions (asteroid↔asteroid, ship↔asteroid): fully physical

Here realism is exactly what you want, and it captures mass + speed + spin *for free* through the standard rigid-body contact at point `p` with normal `n`:

```
r_A = p − com_A,  r_B = p − com_B
v_contact = (v_A + ω_A × r_A) − (v_B + ω_B × r_B)     // spin enters HERE, naturally
v_n       = v_contact · n                              // approach speed at the contact
1/m_eff   = 1/m_A + 1/m_B + cross(r_A,n)²/I_A + cross(r_B,n)²/I_B   // mass + rotational inertia
j         = (1+e) · m_eff · v_n                         // normal impulse
E_diss    = ½ · m_eff · v_n² · (1 − e²)                 // energy available to fracture
```

This is *the same number your collision solver already computes to resolve the bounce* — so fracture and collision response stop being two code paths. That alone kills a big chunk of your duplication. And note: **angular velocity enters in the place it physically belongs** — the contact-point velocity `ω × r` and the lever-arm term in `m_eff` — not as the bolted-on "tangential bond pre-stress" hack in [`ComputeEffStrengths`](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs#L156). Mass enters through `m_eff`, speed through `v_n`, spin through both. All three, correctly, one formula.

### Source B — weapons: authored, in the same units

Stop deriving bullet damage from ½·m·v². A bullet is not a kinetic pebble; gameplay-wise it's a directed energy/impulse delivery. So a weapon **injects an authored impulse `J` and energy `E` directly at the contact point** — and that's exactly what your unused `energy: 1200` field should *be*. Calibrate it in physical currency: *"a cannon shot ≈ a standard asteroid hitting at 400."* Now it lives in the same units as Source A, flows through the identical pipeline, but its magnitude is a **design choice, not a physics accident** — which is precisely why bullets can out-damage a mountain without a 5000× fudge.

The fudge disappears because you stopped asking physics to justify the un-physical.

## Why this is finally *tunable* — ignite on stress, not energy

This is the part that fixes "negligible collisions shouldn't fracture" without any threshold cap. **Fracture ignition is driven by stress (impulse per contact length), propagation by energy.** Two different jobs, two different quantities:

```
per-cell ignition:   σ_cell = j_cell / L_contact_cell   →  crack starts if σ_cell > cell.IgnitionToughness
propagation budget:  E_diss spent flooding the bond graph (your existing kernel, unchanged)
```

A bullet dumps its whole impulse into **one** cell over a tiny contact length → huge σ → ignites. An asteroid bump spreads a large impulse across **many** contact cells over a long edge → σ per cell stays low → no ignition, it just bounces. That's the real reason blunt slow contacts don't shatter and sharp fast ones do — and it gives you the natural threshold you wanted **for free**:

> **Drop the energy-threshold cap entirely.** "No cell reaches ignition stress" *is* the threshold, and it's physically meaningful instead of a magic 20. Keep optional sub-threshold accumulation (fatigue) if you like, but it's no longer load-bearing.

Your existing crack-propagation kernel stays — it's the good part. You only change *how the seed energy and the ignition decision are computed*.

## Spin: it's actually two effects, and conflating them is half your trouble

1. **Impact spin** — a spinning body hit on its rim has extra closing speed at the contact. Handled automatically by `ω × r` in `v_contact` above. One-time, per-hit.
2. **Centrifugal self-stress** — a fast spinner is under standing tensile load even with no impact (real rubble-pile asteroids have a spin-rate limit beyond which they fly apart). *This* is the "spinners are fragile / tear themselves apart when nudged" flavor, and it's legitimately separate. Keep it — but as a **standing stress added to `σ_cell`** in the same units, not as a bond-strength multiplier. Then a spinner near its limit ignites on a feather-touch, which is both physical and great gameplay.

Right now both are smeared into one `SpinPreStress` knob that weakens bonds, which is why spin is hard to reason about. Split them and each gets a clear, independent role.

## So, concretely

| Your requirement | How it's satisfied |
|---|---|
| Capture angular velocity | `ω × r` in contact velocity (impact) + centrifugal standing stress (self-load) |
| Take speed + mass into account | `v_n` and `m_eff` (incl. rotational inertia) in the physical collision |
| Adapt to both regimes | One pipeline, one currency; physical source for collisions, authored source for weapons |
| Drop the threshold cap | Replaced by per-cell stress ignition — negligible bumps simply never ignite |
| No more 5000× fudge | Gone; collisions are physical, weapons are authored, and they meet in common units |

The one honest caveat: you still hold **one** real lever — the conversion rate between "physical collision units" and "authored weapon units" (effectively, how hard asteroids hit relative to guns). But that's a single, meaningful, bounded number you set once, not a per-object regime correction that explodes every time you add an enemy. That's the whole difference between tunable and not.

---

Want me to write this up as the destruction-model spec — the field-by-field replacement for `FractureProperties`/`WeaponProfile`, the new `ContactImpact` struct the collision solver hands to the fracture pipeline, and the calibration recipe (pick σ₀ for a baseline cannon shot, derive everything relative to it)? That becomes step 3 of the refactor, and I can fold it into the plan alongside the PlayingState/demo de-duplication.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 16:07 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 16:08 UTC

Good instinct to check — but here the implementation doesn't actually do what you're picturing. Let me correct that, then explain σ, because the two are the same idea.

## What accumulation currently does (and why it's not what you want)

There *is* accumulation, but it's [`FractureState.AbsorbedEnergy`](GameEngine/Engine/Components/FractureState.cs#L13) — **one float for the whole body**, combined with the next hit before the threshold check:

```csharp
float combined = energyTotal + body.State.AbsorbedEnergy;   // FractureSimulator.cs:116
if (combined < threshold) { /* absorb, no fracture */ }
```

So it's three things you don't want:

1. **Body-global, not per-cell.** A light tap on the *left* edge and a light tap on the *right* edge of a huge asteroid pool into the same bucket. Physically and visually wrong — chipping one spot should weaken *that spot*, not the whole rock.
2. **Energy, not stress.** It accumulates the wrong quantity (see below — energy doesn't predict whether something cracks).
3. **No decay.** It only resets *on* fracture. So infinitely many infinitesimal taps eventually break anything, with no notion of "you have to hit the same place repeatedly *before it relaxes*."

So "already supported" is half-true: there's a global energy bucket, not per-cell stress fatigue. The good news is that per-cell accumulation falls straight out of the σ model — it's barely any extra machinery.

## What σ represents, intuitively

**σ is how *concentrated* a hit is — load per unit of contact, i.e. pressure.** Not how much energy or force, but how *focused* it is.

The canonical intuition: **push a wall with your thumb, then with a needle, using the exact same force.** Same force, same energy — but the needle punctures and the thumb doesn't. The only difference is contact area: the needle concentrates that force into a tiny spot, so the *local* load (force ÷ area) is enormous. That local concentration is σ. Materials don't break when you put a lot of *energy* into them; they break when the *local concentration* exceeds their strength.

```
σ_cell = impulse delivered to the cell  ÷  contact length it's spread over
```

(Strictly it's an impulse-density rather than a textbook stress in pascals — we use impulse not instantaneous force because the game never resolves contact duration — but it plays exactly the role of stress: peak local load.)

This is *precisely* why your bullet-vs-asteroid problem dissolves without a fudge:

- **Bullet** = needle. Tiny contact length, all impulse into one cell → **huge σ** → cracks.
- **Slow asteroid bump** = leaning your whole back against a wall. Large total impulse, but spread over a long contact edge across many cells → **small σ per cell** → no crack, just a bounce.

Energy gets this backwards (the slow asteroid carries *more* energy yet should do *less* damage). σ gets it right because it asks the question that actually decides fracture: *how focused was the load, here, on this cell?*

## Per-cell accumulation = fatigue, and it's natural with σ

Once ignition is decided per-cell by σ, accumulation is just **fatigue**: real materials fail under repeated *sub-yield* loads because each one deposits microscopic damage that adds up (this is genuinely how metal fatigue works). Each cell carries its own accumulator:

```
per hit, for each contact cell:
    if σ_cell ≥ cell.IgnitionToughness:        // big enough alone → crack now
        ignite a crack front at this cell
    else:                                       // too light alone → deposit fatigue
        cell.Damage += σ_cell
        if cell.Damage ≥ cell.IgnitionToughness:
            ignite a crack front at this cell

each frame:
    cell.Damage -= relaxRate * dt               // decay, clamped at 0
```

Three properties this buys you, all of which the current global bucket lacks:

- **Local.** Damage lives on the cell that got hit. Chip the same spot ten times and *that* spot fails — exactly the behavior you described — while the far side stays pristine.
- **Decay (the important addition).** Without `relaxRate`, any object dies from infinite tiny taps over a long match. With it, you must concentrate hits *in a window* before the cell relaxes — physically it's anelastic relaxation, gameplay-wise it's a per-material "toughness regen." It's also your single knob for "how much does chipping matter."
- **Same currency.** `Damage` and `IgnitionToughness` are both in σ-units, so accumulation, single-hit ignition, and the threshold are one consistent scale — no separate magic numbers.

Note this also kills the old global-threshold-cap question entirely: there's no body-level cap anymore. A cell ignites either because one hit was concentrated enough, or because enough concentrated-enough hits stacked before it relaxed. That *is* the threshold, per-cell, in meaningful units.

So: not currently supported the way you want (it's a global energy bucket), but it becomes almost free once stress-ignition is per-cell. Want me to roll this — per-cell `Damage` + `relaxRate`, replacing `FractureState.AbsorbedEnergy` — into the model spec I offered to write?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 16:24 UTC

The plan is written. Here's the shape of it:

**Structural de-dup first (Phases 0–5, behavior-preserving):**
- **Phase 0** — fix `game_config.json` drift (duplicate `vortex`, two wave systems, material presets duplicated in C#).
- **Phase 1** — new `AsteroidsGameplay` library both exes reference; move shared components/events/`ConfigExtensions` into it (one copy).

- **Phase 5** — parity gate: both build and run identically before touching physics.

**New physics behind the now-single boundary (Phases 6–7):**
- **Phase 6** — `CollisionSystem` emits a `ContactImpact` (effective mass + contact-point velocity incl. ω×r); ignite per-cell by stress σ, propagate by dissipated energy through the existing kernel; weapons inject authored impulse in the same currency; remove `asteroidEnergyScale`; split `Toughness` into `IgnitionToughness` + `BondCost`.
- **Phase 7** — replace body-global `AbsorbedEnergy` with per-cell `Damage[]` + `relaxRate` decay (fatigue); drop the global threshold cap.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 17:07 UTC

This is an important discovery that the plan under-specified — and it has behavior implications, so I want your call before proceeding.

The demo systems aren't movable verbatim because they're written against **demo-local infra that diverges from the game's**:

1. **Collision layers differ in their bit values.** Demo `Layers`: `Ghost=4, Alien=8`. Game `GameLayers`: `Alien=4, Bullet=8, Ghost=16`. (The values are arbitrary — only *internal consistency per exe* matters — so unifying is safe **if** every reference in each exe switches together. But it's not a no-op edit.)
2. **There are two different `Camera` classes with different APIs.** The demo defines its own `Camera` (with `.Offset`, used by the demo's `PlayerControlSystem`); the game uses the engine's PAL `Camera` (with `Position`/`ScreenToWorld`, no `.Offset`). A shared `PlayerControlSystem` can only depend on one of them.

So "demo systems are canonical" holds for the *logic*, but moving them into shared code forces a choice of canonical Camera + Layers, and one exe has to adapt. Here's the fork:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 17:34 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 17:35 UTC

I need to correct something, because the evidence now clearly contradicts the "demo canonical" assumption — and I'd rather flag it than quietly build the wrong thing.

Having read both sides, **the game's systems aren't inlined and aren't worse — they're in a clean `_systems[]` array too, and they're consistently *richer* than the demo's:**

| System | Demo | Game |
|---|---|---|
| `PlayerControlSystem` | fires starting weapon only | + skills (Q/E/R), multi-weapon, propeller-thrust degradation, piercing |
| `VortexSystem` | (simpler) | per-entity `VortexResponse` multipliers |
| `BorderDampSystem` | no-arg | configurable world bounds + position clamp |
| `GhostSystem` | restores to Asteroid only | distinct Player/Alien/Asteroid layer restore |
| `TimeToLiveSystem` | allocates each frame | cached dead-list |
| `FractureGroupSystem`, `EventFlushSystem` | identical | identical |
| `GrenadeSystem`, `BlackHoleSystem`, boss | — | game-only |

So the demo's systems are *simpler*, not *better* — they looked "more coherent" only because the demo is a smaller game. What was genuinely demo-canonical is the **fracture-response handlers and spawning** (Phase 3), not the systems. Taking the demo's systems verbatim would regress the game's skills/weapons/boss.

Crucially: the **game's systems already use the engine `Camera` + `GameLayers`** we just picked as canonical — so taking *them* needs zero infra adaptation, and only the demo adapts. That's both more correct and less work.

This reverses the canonical rule you chose, so I want your explicit sign-off rather than flipping it silently:

## On your end-goal: demo == game + tuning

You're right, and the player bug was a symptom of it — I'd wired the shared *system* but left the demo *spawning* its own divergent player. To get the demo to be exactly the game plus tuning, the remaining divergences to fold into shared code are:

| Concern | Status |
|---|---|
| Player spawn | ✅ now shared (`PlayerPrefab`) |
| Systems (control, vortex, AI, weapons…) | ✅ shared (Phase 2) |
| **Asteroid spawn** | ❌ each exe has its own `SpawnAsteroid`/procedural builder |
| **Alien / mothership spawn** | ❌ duplicated |
| **Rendering** (bodies, HUD, debris) | ❌ game `DrawBodies` vs demo `DemoRenderer` diverge |
| **Wave system** | ❌ both have their own wave logic |
| **VFX** (flash/dust) | ❌ diverge (`EnergyRef` vs config) |

So the path to true parity is to extract shared **prefabs** (`AsteroidPrefab`, `AlienPrefab`, `MothershipPrefab`), a shared **world renderer**, and a shared **wave spawner** into the lib, leaving each exe as: *compose shared gameplay + its own shell* (the game adds states/HUD; the demo adds the editor/shape-tools/tuning overlay).

That's a meaningful chunk of work but it's the right target. Two questions of sequencing:

## Let me be honest about the pattern

This is the third "demo is missing X" (shooting/skills → grenade/piercing). They're all the same root cause: **the demo keeps its own thinner copies of the fracture-response handlers**, which is exactly the "keep thin handlers" approach you picked back in Phase 3. That choice made sense for "preserve both behaviors," but it's now directly fighting your actual goal — *demo == game + tuning*. As long as the handlers are per-exe copies, the demo will keep drifting behind the game.

The demo's handlers still differ from the game's in more places you haven't hit yet:
- `OnBulletHit`/`OnCollision`: game applies dash-invincibility + player/alien impact-coefficient; demo doesn't.
- `OnCellPulverized`: game does scoring + cockpit→game-over; demo doesn't.
- `OnFractureCompleted`/`OnFractureSplit`: game does cockpit/player-transfer + mothership tracking; demo's are simpler.

Since you want the demo to *be* the game (just with tuning tools layered on), the demo actually wants **all** of that behavior identically — there's no real "demo is simpler" anymore. So the clean fix is to **stop keeping thin handlers and share the real ones**: extract the game's fracture-response handlers (+ asteroid/alien spawn, + the world renderer) into shared lib code that *both* run identically. The demo then = shared gameplay + its editor/shape/wave overlay, and this whole class of "demo missing X" bugs disappears at once.

That reverses the Phase 3 "thin handlers" decision — which is why I'm flagging it rather than just doing it. My recommendation: **converge the handlers + spawn + renderer into shared code next**, before the energy model (so the model only has one fracture path + one renderer to touch).

Want me to proceed with that convergence (the demo becomes game-gameplay + tuning overlay)? Or would you rather I keep patching the demo piecemeal and move to the energy model sooner?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 19:41 UTC

All four projects build clean. Here are the three fixes:

## 1. Player/aliens dying on the first split — *engine bug, now fixed*

Your instinct was right that it's a tag-transfer problem, but the root cause was one level deeper: the engine's fragment builder ([FractureSimulator.cs:338](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs#L338)) constructed each fragment cell **without copying `Role`**. So the moment any body fractured, every fragment cell's `Role` reset to `null` — the cockpit/propeller/cannon roles vanished. That's why `Cells.Any(c => c.Role == "cockpit")` was always false → the cockpit fragment was never recognized → instant "death."

Fixed by carrying `Role = src.Role` into the fragment cell. This also fixes a second latent bug you'd have hit next: **weapons and thrust would stop working after any fracture** (those gate on `cannon`/`propeller` roles too). This was a pre-existing engine bug affecting the **game as well** — the convergence just surfaced it because the demo now runs the same cockpit-transfer logic.

## 2. Piercing round instantly killing the player

The piercing round's collision mask was `Asteroid | Alien | Player` — so the round the player just fired (spawned right on top of the ship) immediately collided with the player and fractured it. Removed `Player` from the mask ([PiercingPrefab.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/PiercingPrefab.cs)) — a player's own weapon shouldn't hit the player. It now flies out and fractures asteroids/aliens as intended.

## 3. Slow-mo vs respawn key conflict

The demo's respawn was on `R`, which is also the slow-mo skill. Moved demo respawn to **Backspace** so `R` works as slow-mo (and updated the on-screen key legend).

All four build clean. These should let you fully exercise the demo now — the ship survives partial fracture (keeps firing/thrusting from surviving roled cells), piercing works, and slow-mo is testable. Worth a run to confirm, especially the role-preservation fix since it changes fracture behavior in **both** the game and demo.

Want me to continue with **Convergence C (shared spawn prefabs)** next, or verify these first?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 09:19 UTC

Found it — a pre-existing bug. The arrow keys validate the scheme (`1073741824 + scancode`): Up = scancode 82 → `1073741906` ✓. But Control is mapped to `1073741724`/`1073741728`, which are *below* the `1073741824` base — invalid values that never match. The real SDL keycodes are LCTRL `1073742048` (scancode 224) and RCTRL `1073742052` (228). So `KeyCode.Control` was never registered → Ctrl+S/Ctrl+Z never fired. Fixing it (and adding Shift/Alt correctly while here):

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 13:23 UTC

I have the full picture. Here's the Phase 6 design (implementing what we discussed), then I'll build it:

**Unified model — one formula, physical for collisions, sharpness-authored for weapons:**
- **Effective mass at contact:** `1/m_eff = 1/m_imp + 1/m_body + (r×n)²/I_body` — captures mass *and* rotational inertia/lever-arm (spin).
- **Contact-normal speed** `v_n` (callers already fold ω×r into the relative velocity).
- **Normal impulse** `J = (1+e)·m_eff·v_n`; **dissipated energy** `E = ½·m_eff·v_n²·(1−e²)`.
- **Ignite on stress:** `σ = (J / √cellArea)·Concentration ≥ IgnitionToughness` — *Concentration* is the impactor's sharpness (bullets high, blunt asteroid contact low). This replaces the `asteroidEnergyScale` fudge with a meaningful knob, and **decouples** ignition (`IgnitionToughness`) from propagation (`Toughness`/bond cost).
- **Propagate on `E`** (the existing bond-graph kernel, unchanged). Global threshold cap **removed**.

New knobs: material `ignitionToughness` + `restitution`; weapon `concentration`. Let me re-read the exact current `BeginFracture` to rewrite it.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 13:35 UTC

## Phase 6 — what changed

All in `FractureService.ComputeImpact` (the new core), `FractureSimulator`, and `FractureProperties`/`WeaponProfile` + config:

- **Effective mass at contact** — `1/m_eff = 1/m_imp + 1/m_body + (r×n)²/I_body`. Mass *and* spin now enter the impulse properly (the lever-arm term), on top of the contact velocity already carrying `ω×r`.
- **Dissipated energy** `E = ½·m_eff·v_n²·(1−e²)` drives propagation (existing bond-graph kernel, unchanged). Restitution `e` is the bounce-vs-fracture split.
- **Stress ignition** `σ = (J/√cellArea)·Concentration ≥ IgnitionToughness` decides *whether* a crack starts. `Toughness` (bond cost) and `IgnitionToughness` (ignition) are now **decoupled**.
- **Gone:** the global energy threshold and the `asteroidEnergyScale = 0.0002` fudge. The asteroid contact is now `asteroidConcentration = 0.02` — a *blunt-stress* factor with physical meaning, not a mystery energy scale.

New knobs (all live-tunable in the demo): material `ignitionToughness` + `restitution`, weapon `concentration`, fracture `asteroidConcentration`. And **`ForceLog` (press L) now prints `J / eDiss / σ vs ignite`** on every hit — exactly what you need to tune.

## Important: these constants are *starting estimates*, not calibrated

I picked the absolute numbers (concentration 80, rock ignition 600, asteroidConcentration 0.02) by rough arithmetic — they will need a tuning pass in the demo. Expect to adjust:
- **Bullets don't fracture** → lower material `ignitionToughness` or raise weapon `concentration`.
- **Asteroid collisions too violent/gentle** → adjust `asteroidConcentration` (and watch `σ vs ignite` in the force log).
- **Cracks too small/big once started** → that's `Toughness`/`surfaceEfficiency` (propagation), independent of ignition now.

The `σ vs ignite` readout tells you exactly why any hit did or didn't start a crack, so tuning is now a readable feedback loop rather than guesswork.

Please **run the demo, press L to enable the force log, and fire at a few asteroids** to see the new numbers — then tell me what feels off and we'll calibrate. Once it's in the right ballpark, **Phase 7** adds the per-cell stress accumulation (fatigue) so repeated light hits to the same spot eventually crack it.

Want to tune Phase 6 together now, or go straight to implementing Phase 7 and tune both at once?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 14:47 UTC

Now I have precise answers. Here's the full picture:

## 1. Bond & density multipliers

**Bond multipliers — working.** Each cell carries a `BondMult` (from a shape seed's `bondMult`, or a procedural `bondMultDistribution`). When bonds are built ([VoronoiTessellator.cs:350](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L350)):
```
bond.Strength = sharedEdgeLength × material.Toughness × √(multA × multB)
```
So a high-`bondMult` region (e.g. an armored asteroid's `surfaceValue: 3.5` shell) gets stronger bonds → cracks spend their energy budget faster crossing them → that region resists shattering. It's a **propagation** modifier (geometric mean of the two cells' mults).

**Density multipliers — currently dead.** `Cell.DensityMult` is *intended* to weight mass/inertia (denser core). `VoronoiTessellator.TotalMass`/`ComputeInertia` honor it (`mass = Density × Σ(area × densityMult)`)... **but nothing calls those anymore.** The convergence routed all spawns through `FractureBodyFactory.SpawnFromDensity`, which uses `Density × TotalArea` — ignoring per-cell `DensityMult`. The fragment mass-split also splits by area only. So `densityMultDistribution` (boulder's dense core, etc.) is set on cells but **has no effect** right now. That's a regression I introduced in Convergence C — worth fixing (switch `SpawnFromDensity` to `TotalMass` and weight fragment mass by `DensityMult`).

## 2. Mothership state

- **Components** (shared lib): `MothershpId { Id, InitialCockpitCount }`, `SpawnerAccumulator`.
- **Spawn**: `SpawnMothership()` — **game-only** (in `PlayingState`, not shared); the demo never spawns it.
- **Boss skills**: `UpdateBossSkills()` — **game-only** in `PlayingState`: shockwave, black-hole, ram-charge, drone-spawning, half-health "overdrive". ~150 lines, all in the state.
- **Fracture response** (shared, `FractureGameplay`): when a mothership breaks, **only cockpit-bearing fragments** become alien-tagged motherships; the rest are inert debris. This is the correct pattern.
- **AI** (`AlienAiSystem`): explicitly **skips** `mothership` ("drift handled by boss skill system").

So the mothership is functional but **entirely game-side** (spawn + skills in `PlayingState`); only its fracture-tagging is shared. To get it in the demo it'd need a `MothershipPrefab` + a shared `BossSystem`.

## 3. Material specs in a `.cs` file

You're right, and it's already safe: the `FractureProperties.Rock/Glass/Ice/Metal` presets are **completely unused** (every spawn path reads from config via `ToFractureProperties`). I can delete them outright — materials then live *only* in `game_config.json`. ✅ (clear win, I'll do it)

## 4. Material ownership — shape vs config

Here's the key find: **`ShapeData` already has a `Material` field** ([ShapeData.cs:10](GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/ShapeData.cs#L10), default `"metal"`) — but **nothing reads it.** Aliens use `EntityConfig.Material`, the player uses `PlayerConfig.Material`, and piercing hardcodes `"metal"`.

My recommendation: **the shape owns the material for authored shapes** (player_ship, drone, bruiser, mothership, piercing_round) — it's the natural single source, and it kills the piercing hardcode and the redundant `material` on every entity config. **Procedural asteroids keep material in the asteroid config** (they have no `ShapeData`). The config `material` becomes an optional *override* (empty = use the shape's). This directly matches your instinct and uses a field that already exists.

The one caveat: if you ever want the *same* shape in different materials, shape-owned material blocks that — but you'd just clone the shape. I think shape-owned is right. **Do you agree?**

## 5. Titanium not shattering

Expected, and diagnosable: titanium `ignitionToughness = 3000`, but a single cannon shot produces `σ ≈ (J/√grainArea)·concentration ≈ (600/70)·80 ≈ 685` — far below 3000 (press **L**, you'll see `σ=685 vs ignite=3000`). Two fixes, and I think you want **both**:
- **Phase 7 fatigue** is the realistic fix — one bullet can't crack titanium, but *sustained fire* accumulates stress past 3000. (This is exactly the case you flagged.)
- Optionally lower titanium `ignitionToughness` to ~800–1200 so it takes a few solid hits even without sustained fire.

## 6. Alien tag / movement / shooting tied to roles

Confirmed bug: `CopyTags` blindly copies `AlienTag` + `AlienVariant` to **every** alien fragment — so a severed wing becomes a free-floating "alien." It should mirror the mothership: **only cockpit-bearing fragments stay alien**, the rest become inert debris. The movement/shooting gates *already exist* in `AlienAiSystem` (`AlivePropellerFraction` → thrust, `AliveWeaponFraction` → fire), so once tagging is fixed, a cockpit fragment with no propeller won't move and with no weapon won't shoot — exactly what you want. ✅ (clear fix, I'll do it)

**Proposed action set** (pending your call on #4):
1. Delete the `.cs` material presets (#3).
2. Move material to shape-owned (#4) — *if you agree* — removing the piercing hardcode + entity-config redundancy.
3. Fix alien fragment tagging to cockpit-only (#6).
4. Restore `DensityMult`'s effect on mass (#1).
5. Tune/clarify titanium (#5) — defer to Phase 7, optionally nudge the value now.

Want me to proceed with 1, 3, 4 now (unambiguous), confirm shape-owned material for 2, and handle 5 as part of Phase 7?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 14:59 UTC

I've got the context I need (the procedural builder, shotgun/shrapnel, and bullet plumbing are all fresh from the Phase 6 work). Here's my assessment of your two designs, then a few clarifications before I write the plan.

## My take on the cluster rework

**I like it — it's a real improvement.** The current system ties heterogeneity to *position* via `radialGradient`/`noiseClusters` distributions, which is rigid. Your model cleanly separates two concerns: **seed placement** (uniform, count from material grain) and **material heterogeneity** (clusters of strong/dense cells grown by BFS). That gives organic dense cores, tough nodules, weak veins — more interesting and more physical than concentric gradients. The "BFS budget that decays with inter-cell distance" is a good spread mechanism.

Three things I'd pin down: (a) clusters naturally make *localized blobs*, so the current **"armored" surface-shell** pattern (tough all around the rim) can't be expressed by central clusters — that needs a decision; (b) cluster contributions should be **additive on a base of 1.0** so overlapping clusters stack and you can have several; (c) one `clusterStrength` driving *both* bond and density (at a fixed ratio) is simpler than two budgets — I'd start there.

Note one bug this surfaces: per-cell **`DensityMult` is currently ignored** (the converged spawn uses `Density × area`, not `TotalMass`), so density clusters won't affect mass until we fix that — which is already in our action set (#1).

## My take on the shotgun/grenade rework

**Strongly agree, and it synergizes beautifully with the new model.** Drag → lower velocity at range → lower `v_n` → lower stress `σ` → less (or no) ignition far away. So "shotgun is lethal point-blank, weak at range" becomes *emergent* from the physics rather than a special case. Per-pellet TTL/speed variance + a **stratified** spread (evenly spaced slots + per-slot jitter — structured but not gridded, not pure random) gives the organic cone you want.

One implementation note: shotgun pellets and grenade shrapnel are **raycast bullets with no `RigidBody`**, so they don't go through `PhysicsSystem`'s drag — they integrate in `MovementSystem` with no damping. So drag needs a small addition (a `Drag` field on `BulletData`, applied to velocity for bullet entities). The grenade *projectile* already has drag; it's the pellets/shrapnel that need it.

A few clarifications before I finalize the plan:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 22:14 UTC

Good feedback — all incorporated. First, to answer your blastResist question directly:

**`BlastResist` (per-cell, [0,1])** controls *vaporization*, which is separate from cracking. When a cell absorbs enough crack energy, it can **pulverize** — turn into dust/debris instead of becoming a solid fragment, which is what carves the impact crater. `BlastResist` is that cell's resistance to vaporizing: `0` = vaporizes at the normal blast threshold, `1` = needs the *full* impact energy to vaporize. So an armored shell with high blastResist cracks and sheds chunks but doesn't disintegrate into dust. My "folded into clusters" remark just meant: cluster cells get higher blastResist too (via the now-separate `blastGain`), so a surface-cluster shell resists both cracking *and* vaporizing. The full write-up of this (and everything else) is now a deliverable (Part E).

Let me update the plan with your changes.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-25 22:26 UTC

This is the right question to ask before tuning — and the audit gives clear answers. Here's the full picture: how each parameter actually moves the simulation, then what's dead or redundant.

## The pipeline & what each parameter does

**Stage 1 — Impact → impulse, energy, stress** (`FractureService.ComputeImpact`)
A hit produces three numbers from the contact:
- **`Restitution`** (material `e`): splits contact energy into bounce vs fracture. `J = (1+e)·m_eff·v_n`, `E = ½·m_eff·v_n²·(1−e²)`. High `e` → bouncier → less `E` into the crack.
- **`Concentration`** (weapon): ignition stress `σ = (J/√cellArea)·Concentration`. Pure sharpness multiplier — sharp bullet high, blunt asteroid low.
- **`IgnitionToughness`** (material): the gate. `σ ≥ IgnitionToughness` or nothing happens.

**Stage 2 — Energy split** (`ComputeBudget`)
`E` is divided three ways using **two** knobs:
- **`KineticFraction`** (shaped by `Brittleness`): `kFrac = lerp(KF, KF·0.3, Brittleness)`. `kinetic = kFrac·E` → fragment fling.
- **`SurfaceEfficiency`**: `surface = SurfEff·(1−kFrac)·E` → the crack budget. The remainder `(1−SurfEff)·(1−kFrac)·E` is **lost** (heat/sound, invisible).

**Stage 3 — Bond strengths** (`ComputeEffStrengths`)
- **`Toughness`**: `bond.Strength = EdgeLength · Toughness · √(bondMultA·bondMultB)` (set at tessellation; this is the **propagation** cost). Per-cell `bondMult` (clusters) scales it.
- **`SpinPreStress`** × body ω²: pre-weakens tangentially-oriented bonds, more at the rim — the centrifugal "fast spinners are fragile" channel.

**Stage 4 — Crack propagation** (`FractureKernel.StepFront`)
A descending-energy flood from the struck cell, spending the surface budget on bond strengths:
- **`Brittleness`** → `transmission = lerp(0.18, 0.96, Brittleness)`: how much surplus energy passes to the next cell. Brittle = travels far (shatter); ductile = dies locally (chip). **This is the single biggest "shatter vs chip" lever.**
- **`CrackDirectionality`** (material) + **`Directionality`** (weapon), averaged: steer the crack into a forward cone vs an omni splash (`align^DirExponent`, capped by `BoostCap`).
- The **surface budget** caps total bonds broken; each broken bond costs its `Strength`.

**Stage 5 — Vaporization** (blast crater)
- **`BlastFraction`** (weapon): `blastBase = (1−blast)·E`. 0 = nothing vaporizes; 1 = everything the crack reached turns to dust.
- per-cell **`BlastResist`**: `cellThresh = blastBase + BlastResist·(E − blastBase)`. High resist → needs near-full `E` to vaporize → survives as a chunk instead of dust.

**Stage 6 — Fragments + motion**
- **`MinFragmentArea`**: below this a piece is visual debris, not a body.
- **`Density`** (+ per-cell `DensityMult`): mass.
- Fling: `EjectFraction` (scatter speed, scaled by `√(GrainArea/area)` so small = fast), `ImpactSpin` (shear spin), `MomentumTransfer` (recoil on the body), `DetachCellScale/Jitter` (single-cell shrink). `Brittleness` also adds fling-spin variety.

**Stage 7 — Pacing** (multi-frame)
- Global **`CrackSteps`/`CrackFrames`**: frontier-pops per iteration / frames between. `DetachOnSplit`: detach as cracks arrive vs at the end.

## Redundancy verdict

**Dead — remove now:**
- **`CrackSpeed`** (material) — stored, config-mapped, passed through `AsteroidPrefab`… but **never read**. Pacing comes entirely from the global `CrackSteps`/`CrackFrames`. Pure noise.
- **`EnergyScale`** (global `fracture`) — only ever used as `BulletMass × EnergyScale`. A redundant multiplier; fold into `BulletMass`.

**Redundant — merge:**
- **`KineticFraction` + `SurfaceEfficiency`** → one **`SurfaceFraction`**. Today two knobs carve a 3-way split where the third slice ("lost") is invisible. Collapse to `surface = SurfaceFraction·E`, `kinetic = (1−SurfaceFraction)·E`. One fewer param, and you lose nothing you can see. (`Brittleness` already biases the split, so it stays the brittle/ductile master.)

**Vestigial — flag (game-layer, lower priority):**
- Per-weapon **`Energy`** — after Phase 6 the player's damage is `BulletMass × velocity × Concentration`; the weapon `Energy` field now only survives to (a) scale **alien** bullet mass relative to the player's reference weapon and (b) seed shrapnel/per-ray energy. It's confusing to keep a "damage" number that no longer drives player damage. Cleaner: give aliens a per-weapon `concentration`/`mass` like everything else and delete `Energy`. Worth doing but it's a separate cleanup.

**Keep but reconsider later:**
- **`SpinPreStress`** — it works, but it's the bond-weakening *hack*; the cleaner form is a centrifugal term added to the ignition stress `σ`. It's the only centrifugal channel, so not removable — just a future rework (was in the original Phase 6 intent, deferred).
- The "feel" knobs (`MomentumTransfer`, `EjectFraction`, `ImpactSpin`, detach scale, `AsteroidDirSpin`) are fine per-weapon; they're not redundant, just cosmetic.

**Net:** material params drop from 14 → 11 (remove `CrackSpeed`, merge `KineticFraction`+`SurfaceEfficiency`); global `fracture` drops `EnergyScale`. That's a real reduction in tuning surface with zero capability loss.

Let me fold these into the plan (the trims + a properly-outlined `info/fracture_model.md` that *is* the detail above, cross-checked against the code).

## Part A + D2 — cleanup & trims
- **Material presets deleted** from `FractureProperties.cs`; materials live only in JSON.
- **Params trimmed:** `CrackSpeed` (was never read) and global `EnergyScale` removed; `KineticFraction`+`SurfaceEfficiency` merged into one **`SurfaceFraction`** (recalibrated per material, no more invisible "lost" energy). *(Found & fixed a latent Phase-6 bug: the asteroid builder's manual material construction was silently dropping `IgnitionToughness`/`Restitution` — asteroids had ignition=0.)*
- **Shape-owned material** via `ResolveMaterial` (config = optional override); piercing no longer hardcodes `metal`.
- **Alien tagging cockpit-only:** severed wings are now inert debris; only cockpit fragments stay steerable/shooting aliens (movement/fire already self-gate on propeller/weapon cells).
- **`DensityMult` mass restored** (`SpawnFromDensity`→`TotalMass`; fragment split weighted), so dense cores actually weigh more.

## Part B — procedural clusters
Uniform seeds (count from grain) + **`ClusterCount`/`ClusterCentrality`/`ClusterSpread[range]`/`BondGain`/`DensityGain`/`BlastGain`**, grown by a Dijkstra over cell distances. Re-expressed every asteroid type (boulder = dense core, armored = surface shell, etc.). Added `Bond.StrengthMult` so live `Toughness` edits in the demo don't wipe clusters. Editor sliders + JSON updated.

## Part C + D — shotgun/grenade + self-hit
Shared **`WeaponEffects.SpawnBullet`/`SpawnCone`** (stratified spread + per-pellet speed/TTL jitter + drag) now drive player shotgun, alien shotgun, and grenade shrapnel. Per-bullet **drag** applied in `RaycastBulletSystem` (close-range lethal, long-range chips — emergent from `σ ∝ v_n`). **Projectile self-hit fixed**: `BulletData.Owner`/`OwnerGrace` make a bullet ignore its firer for ~0.1s (covers aliens, player cannon, grenade).

## Part E — docs
`info/fracture_model.md` — the full pipeline (cell/bond state, contact-impulse math, ignition, graph propagation, vaporization, fragments, spin, multi-frame) with every parameter's formula and the deprecation notes.

I can't run it here (SDL needs a display), so please **run the demo** to verify: spawn each asteroid type (clusters → cores/shells/veins, force-log shows stronger cluster bonds), fire shotgun/grenade (organic spread, point-blank shreds vs long-range chips), confirm aliens don't shoot themselves and break into one cockpit piece + debris. All the new knobs are live in the editor for tuning. After that, **Phase 7** (per-cell stress fatigue) is the last piece — what finally lets sustained fire crack titanium.

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The overarching project is a major refactor of "Asteroids on Steroids" — a C#/.NET 8.0 game with a custom ECS engine and physics-based destruction. Earlier phases (0-6, already complete) created a shared `AsteroidsGameplay` library, converged the demo and game to share all gameplay code, and implemented a unified contact-impulse fracture model. The MOST RECENT explicit requests (this segment) were:
   - **Answer questions** about how bond/density multipliers work and the mothership AI/prefab state.
   - **Design points**: materials should live only in game config (not a `.cs` file); a body's material should come from its shape, not hardcoded/entity-config; titanium doesn't shatter from bullets; alien-tag should only follow cockpit-bearing fragments (movement tied to propeller cells, shooting to cannon/shotgun cells).
   - **Rework #1 — procedural asteroid builder**: remove `seedClusterCenter`, uniform seeds with count from material grain, introduce `clusterCount`, `clusterStrength`→`clusterSpread` (range of % radius), `clusterCentrality`. Clusters = chosen cells with higher density+bond multiplier spread to neighbors via BFS. Separate `bondGain`/`densityGain`/`blastGain` params (user feedback).
   - **Rework #2 — shotgun/grenade**: per-pellet variation (different TTLs, speeds), stratified (not random, not gridded) angular spread, drag so they do more damage at close range. Drag must live in `RaycastBulletSystem` (user feedback: "isn't really a separate concern, so no new system needed").
   - **NEW bug fix (user feedback)**: alien bullets instantly collide with their own body on spawn — need a grace period like the piercing round.
   - **Documentation**: a detailed file in `info/` explaining all parameters influencing fracturing/vaporization/energy-spread (how computed, how they change, what's stored in cells, how energy traverses the graph and why), PLUS a trimming analysis of redundant/obsolete/irrelevant parameters.
   - **Phase 7 (most recent "Let's go with the last phase")**: per-cell stress accumulation/fatigue — replace body-global `FractureState.AbsorbedEnergy` with per-cell `Cell.Damage`; on sub-ignition hit accumulate `Damage += σ`, ignite when `Damage ≥ IgnitionToughness`, decay each frame by per-material `RelaxRate`. This is what lets sustained fire crack titanium.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - ECS engine: structs in SparseSet, `ref`-based mutation, deferred destruction, `World.ForEach`, EventBus.
   - Shared `AsteroidsGameplay` class library referenced by both Game.exe and Demo.exe.
   - Contact-impulse fracture model: effective mass `1/m_eff = 1/m_imp + 1/m_body + (r×n)²/I_body`, normal impulse `J=(1+e)·m_eff·v_n`, dissipated energy `E=½·m_eff·v_n²·(1−e²)`, ignition stress `σ=(J/√cellArea)·Concentration ≥ IgnitionToughness`.
   - Crack propagation: descending-energy flood (`FractureKernel.StepFront`), `transmission=lerp(0.18,0.96,Brittleness)`, directionality cone (`DirExponent=1.6`, `BoostCap=3`).
   - Voronoi tessellation; bonds with `Strength = EdgeLength·Toughness·StrengthMult` (`StrengthMult = √(bondMultA·bondMultB)`).
   - Cluster BFS via Dijkstra over inter-centroid distances; contribution `c=(reach−graphDist)/reach`.
   - Stratified cone spawning; per-bullet drag for raycast bullets; owner-grace.
   - Plan mode workflow (AskUserQuestion / ExitPlanMode); plan file editing.
   - Build command (CWD resets between calls): `cd /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine && dotnet build <proj> -v q --nologo`. SDL needs a display so runtime verification is the user's responsibility.

3. Files and Code Sections:

   **Engine/Destruction/Cell.cs** (Phase 7 — DONE):
   - Added `Damage` field for per-cell fatigue:
   ```csharp
   public float     DensityMult = 1f;
   public float     BlastResist = 0f;
   public float     Damage      = 0f;  // accumulated sub-ignition contact stress (fatigue); decays over
                                       // time and ignites a crack once it reaches IgnitionToughness
   ```

   **Engine/Components/FractureProperties.cs** (Phase 7 — DONE; also earlier param trims):
   - Removed presets (Glass/Ice/Rock/Metal), removed `CrackSpeed`, merged `KineticFraction`+`SurfaceEfficiency`→`SurfaceFraction`. Added `IgnitionToughness`, `Restitution` (Phase 6), and now `RelaxRate`:
   ```csharp
   public float RelaxRate;  // Rate (stress/sec) at which a cell's accumulated fatigue Damage relaxes
   ```

   **Engine/Components/FractureState.cs** (Phase 7 — DONE): Removed `AbsorbedEnergy` field; only `RngSeed` remains with note "Per-cell fatigue now lives on Cell.Damage, not here."

   **Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs** (Phase 7 — DONE for both paths):
   - `ComputeImpact` helper (Phase 6) computes eDiss/sigma/J via effective mass.
   - `BeginFracture` now accumulates fatigue:
   ```csharp
   fb.Cells[cell].Damage += sigma;
   float accumulated = fb.Cells[cell].Damage;
   ForceLog.CurrentBody = body.Id;
   if (ForceLog.On(ForceCat.Energy, body.Id))
       ForceLog.Write(... $"J={J:0.#} eDiss={eDiss:0.#} σ={sigma:0.#} dmg={accumulated:0.#} vs ignite={fb.Material.IgnitionToughness:0.#} ...");
   if (accumulated < fb.Material.IgnitionToughness) return;   // fatigue building, no crack yet
   fb.Cells[cell].Damage = 0f;                                // ignited — fatigue consumed
   ```
   - `TryFracture` same: `fb.Cells[cell].Damage += sigma; if (fb.Cells[cell].Damage < fb.Material.IgnitionToughness) return false; fb.Cells[cell].Damage = 0f;`
   - TryFracture tail simplified to `result = FractureSimulator.Simulate(fb, input, rng); return result.Fractured;`

   **Engine/Destruction/Bond.cs** (Part B — DONE): Added `public float StrengthMult;` (geometric mean of cluster bondMults) so live Toughness edits preserve clusters. `Strength = EdgeLength·Toughness·StrengthMult`.

   **Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs** (Parts A4, B, D2 — DONE):
   - `ComputeBudget` merged: `surf = Clamp(mat.SurfaceFraction,0,1); return new FractureBudget(surf*energyDiss, (1f-surf)*energyDiss, totalArea);` (FractureBudget struct lost Fractured/Absorbed).
   - Fragment mass weighted by DensityMult: BuildComponentSpec sums `weighted += cells[ci].Area*cells[ci].DensityMult`, computes `totalWeighted`, mass `= input.BodyMass*(weighted/totalWeighted)`. Debris path similarly weighted.
   - Fragment bond copy includes `StrengthMult = b.StrengthMult`.

   **Gameplay/Prefabs/AsteroidPrefab.cs** (Parts A1, B — DONE):
   - Material now `var mat = mc.ToFractureProperties(); mat.Density *= ac.DensityMult;` (was brittle manual construction that silently dropped IgnitionToughness/Restitution).
   - `BuildProceduralAsteroid`: uniform seeds (`ScatterSeedsUniform` with `r=maxR·√u`), tessellate with uniform bondMults=1, then `ApplyClusters`. `ApplyClusters` picks ClusterCount centers at radius `(1−Centrality)·maxR`, runs Dijkstra to `budget=U(spread)·maxR`, accumulates `c=(budget−dist)/budget`, applies `bondMult=1+A·BondGain`, `DensityMult=1+A·DensityGain`, `BlastResist=clamp(A·BlastGain,0,1)`, recomputes bond Strength+StrengthMult. Helpers: `NearestCellIndex`, `ProcPointInPolygon`.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-26 15:53 UTC

Ok, let's see if I got the fracture model correctly, please correct me where I'm wrong and be precise.
At impact, 3 things are computed:
Impulse J, which decides how much the two objects get pushed in the opposite direction of the impact.
energy E, the budget of the fracture front that traverses the graphs.
stress that decides whether a crack starts. It depends on the impulse relative to the area of the impacted *cell*, not the whole body, and on the concentration.

The budget of the crack depends purely on the SurfaceFraction and the Energy. 

Propagation is the trickiest part. There's CrackSteps each CrackFrames frames (global fracture config), and each step only one cell (the highest-energy) propagates its energy to its neighbors. If the amount of energy passed to the neighbors is greater than the bondStrength (with the spin-prestress included) the bond breaks and the bondStrength is subtracted to the passed energy. The energy isn't distributed among the neighbors, each neighbor gets the full amount.

Vaporisation, during the fracture step, if the energy delivered to a cell is greater than its threshold (which depends on its BlastResist and BlastFraction of the crack, set by the weapon) it gets vaporised.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-26 15:53 UTC

Let me read the actual code to check each claim precisely.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-26 15:55 UTC

I read the impact model ([FractureService.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs)), the propagation kernel ([FractureKernel.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs)), the budget/vaporization ([FractureSimulator.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs)), and the multi-frame driver ([FractureCrackSystem.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureCrackSystem.cs)). You've got the shape of it right, but there are several precise corrections — and one is a genuine surprise.

## Stage 1 — Impact (`ComputeImpact`)

Three values, yes: `J`, `eDiss`, `σ`. But your role for **J is wrong**.

- **J = (1+e)·m_eff·v_n** is the normal contact impulse. It does **not** push the two bodies apart. Grep it: `J` is used in exactly two places — computing `σ` and the `ForceLog` line. Nothing applies it as a Δv. The body's recoil is a *separate* thing: `kick = dir · (bulletSpeed · MomentumTransfer)` ([FractureService.cs:189](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L189)), applied along the impact direction (not opposite). And the bullet is a raycast bullet — consumed, not pushed. So there's no Newton's-third-law pair here at all. **J's only job is to feed the ignition stress.**
- **eDiss = ½·m_eff·v_n²·(1−e²)** — correct, this is the dissipated energy that propagates. Note `m_eff` folds in the body's spin via the lever-arm term `(r×n)²/I`.
- **σ = J / √(cellArea) · Concentration** — correct, and note it's the **√** of the cell area (a characteristic contact length), not the area itself. And since Phase 7, σ no longer decides ignition directly: it's *added* to `cell.Damage`, and a crack ignites only once the **accumulated** Damage ≥ `IgnitionToughness`.

## Stage 2 — Budget

✓ Correct: `Surface = SurfaceFraction · eDiss`, and that's the whole story.

But watch the distinction you blurred in your "energy E is the budget" line: **two separate quantities flow downstream.**
- The **per-cell energy field** seeds the struck cell with the *full* `eDiss` (not the surface budget) and decays as it transmits.
- The **budget** (`SurfaceFraction·eDiss`) is a separate global accumulator that caps total bond-breaking.

## Stage 3 — Propagation

Mostly right, with three refinements:

- ✓ Pacing is `StepsPerIteration` pops every `FramesPerIteration` frames (the *multi-frame* path — the only one the game uses; the single-frame `Simulate` drains the whole front in one `while` loop). ✓ Each `StepFront` pops exactly the **highest-energy** frontier cell. (Caveat: there can be several fronts co-propagating, one per hit — each pops its own max.)
- The energy handed toward a neighbor is **not** a flat `e`. It's `deliver = e · min(w·norm, BoostCap)` where `w` is the directional alignment weight and `BoostCap = 3`. Mean weight is 1, so omnidirectionally each neighbor does get ≈`e` (you're right it's **not divided among neighbors**), but with directionality the aligned neighbor gets up to 3× and the others less.
- Bond breaks when `deliver > eff[bk]` (effective strength *with* spin pre-stress ✓). But the child's energy isn't just `deliver − strength`: it's **`(deliver − eff) · Transmission`, capped at the parent's energy**. You omitted the `Transmission` factor — and that's the important one: `Transmission = lerp(0.18, 0.96, Brittleness)` is the *main reach lever*. Also, the bond strength is subtracted from **two** things: the child's transmitted energy *and* the global budget (`f.Budget -= eff[bk]`). When budget hits 0, propagation stops regardless of remaining energy.

## Stage 4 — Vaporization

Here's the real correction. Your description — threshold depends on **BlastResist** and BlastFraction — describes the **single-frame `Simulate` path, which the game never calls** ([FractureGameplay.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs) only ever calls `BeginFracture`).

The path the game actually runs ([FractureCrackSystem.cs:108](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureCrackSystem.cs#L108)) vaporizes a cell when `en[i] > f.BlastThresh`, and `BlastThresh = (1 − BlastFraction) · eDiss` — a **single flat scalar set once at seed time** ([FractureService.cs:205](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L205)). It does **not** read `cell.BlastResist` at all.

So in the live game, **`BlastResist` currently has no effect on vaporization** — your clusters' armor only resists via bond strength / density, not blast. Only the unused atomic `Simulate` honors `cellThresh = blastBase + BlastResist·(E − blastBase)`. That's almost certainly a bug worth fixing — want me to thread `BlastResist` into the multi-frame blast check so the per-cell armor actually resists pulverization?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-26 16:03 UTC

So there may be more energy transmitted from a cell than the energy delivered to it?
Why only one cell propagates its energy per step and not all of them? 
How does energy dissipate during the energy propagation?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-26 16:04 UTC

Good questions — they get at the heart of why this is a *flood*, not a conserved-energy simulation.

## 1. Yes — more energy can leave a cell than entered it

This is the key thing to internalize: **energy is not conserved and not divided among neighbors.** Each surviving neighbor independently gets its own copy derived from the parent's *full* energy `e`:

```
deliver = e · min(w·norm, BoostCap)      // per bond, BoostCap = 3
tr      = (deliver − eff) · Transmission // capped at e
```

A cell with energy `e` and 4 break-through neighbors radiates up to 4 separate `tr` values. So the **total** energy leaving a cell can far exceed what arrived. What stops this from being a runaway chain reaction is **not** energy bookkeeping — it's the global `Budget`: every broken bond subtracts its strength (`f.Budget -= eff[bk]`, [FractureKernel.cs:98](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L98)), and when `Budget ≤ 0` the whole front dies.

One bound *does* hold though: the energy a child cell ends up *storing* (`tr`) is **capped at the parent's `e`** ([FractureKernel.cs:100](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L100)). So no cell's energy ever exceeds the struck cell's — the field is monotonically non-increasing along any path, even though the aggregate radiated outward isn't.

## 2. Why one cell per step (highest-energy first)

Because that cap-at-parent rule makes energy **monotonically non-increasing** along every path — which makes this exactly Dijkstra's shortest-path situation. Popping the **maximum-energy** frontier cell guarantees that when a cell is processed, it's at its *true peak* energy: no later path can ever deliver more (every other source has `e ≤` the current max, and transmission only shrinks it). That's what makes the `if (e <= processed[i]) return` guard ([FractureKernel.cs:68](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L68)) sound — each cell is processed **once, at its strongest**.

If you instead fired *all* frontier cells every step, a cell could be processed early at low energy (wasting budget on weak breaks), then have a stronger path arrive later forcing reprocessing — order-dependent, non-deterministic, and it'd burn the budget wrong. Highest-first is both correct and cheap.

It also buys two practical things: **determinism** (seeded + ordered ⇒ replayable fractures), and **controllable pacing** — "advance N frontier-pops per frame" is a meaningful dial precisely because each pop is one discrete crack-tip advance. A crack visibly creeps outward from the hottest point instead of detonating everywhere at once.

## 3. How energy dissipates along the way

Four mechanisms, all in that one `tr` line plus the break test:

1. **Bond cost** — crossing a bond subtracts its effective strength: `(deliver − eff)`. Tougher bonds eat more.
2. **Transmission decay** — the per-hop multiplier `Transmission = lerp(0.18, 0.96, Brittleness)`. This is the dominant reach lever. Brittle (0.96) loses ~4% per hop → cracks race across the body; ductile/tough (0.18) loses ~82% per hop → the crack dies after a cell or two.
3. **Directional falloff** — `deliver = e·min(w·norm, BoostCap)`. Off-axis neighbors get `w < 1`, so they receive less; if it drops below the bond strength, **nothing transmits that way at all** — energy is preferentially funneled along the impact axis and starved off-axis.
4. **Hard stop at strong bonds** — if `deliver ≤ eff`, the bond doesn't break and *no* energy passes; it's fully absorbed by the intact joint.

So there are really two independent "dissipation" accountings, and it's worth keeping them separate in your head:
- **Per-cell energy decay** (subtraction + Transmission + directional weighting) shapes the crack's *reach and silhouette*.
- **Global Budget** (decremented by each broken bond's strength) caps the *total extent* — how many bonds can break before the front simply runs out of money, regardless of how much energy the cells still hold.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-26 16:09 UTC

So only bond traversal absorbs energy, the cells do not? 
Also, does it physically make sense for a single cell to deliver 4x the energy delivered to it?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-26 16:10 UTC

## Cells don't absorb — correct, with one asterisk

Right. In the propagation field a cell is a pure **node**: it holds a scalar `energy[i]` that records the *peak* energy that reached it, and that's it. When a cell pops and radiates, its own `energy[i]` is **not decremented** — it isn't a conserved flow being drained, it's a "what's the highest driving energy that got here" field. All the loss is **edge-local**, applied during the hop:

```
tr = (deliver − eff) · Transmission
       └ bond cost    └ material reach factor
```

`eff` is the bond's strength; `Transmission` is a material (Brittleness) constant applied at the crossing. Neither is a per-cell term. So yes — cells neither absorb nor lose; bonds (edges) account for all dissipation.

The asterisk: a cell *can* be **consumed** by vaporization if its energy clears the blast threshold, and a cell's geometry feeds the model indirectly (bond `eff = EdgeLength·Toughness·…`, and centroids drive the directional weight). But there's no "this cell soaked up X joules" term. Cells are relays; bonds are resistors.

## Does 4× outflow make physical sense? No — and that's deliberate

It is **not** energy-conserving, on purpose. The thing to realize is that the per-cell `energy[]` field is **not a packet of joules being transported** like heat through a bar. It's better read as a **stress-intensity / crack-driving field** — "how hard is something pushing a crack at this point." The actual energy accounting lives in the global `Budget`, which is the conserved-ish quantity: it's spent creating new crack surface (`Budget -= eff` per broken bond), which is essentially Griffith's energy-release criterion — a crack advances while released energy ≥ the energy to make new surface. *That's* the conservation law in this model, and it's never violated.

Given that framing, "one cell drives cracks in 4 directions" is fine: each direction independently asks "is the local stress here greater than this bond's resistance?" — and high stress at a point genuinely can drive cracks several ways at once. Two parts of the 4× are even physically motivated:

- **The directional boost** (`BoostCap = 3`, aligned bonds get up to 3×) is a stylized **stress concentration at the crack tip** — real fracture mechanics: the stress-intensity factor is highest directly ahead of an advancing crack.

The part that's frankly **non-physical-but-intentional** is *not dividing* `e` among the neighbors. A conservation-respecting model would split it (`Σ deliver = e`). They explicitly don't — the comment says *"mean weight 1: **steer, don't attenuate**"* ([FractureKernel.cs:89](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L89)). The rationale is mesh-independence: if you divided by neighbor count, a crack would die faster in a finely-tessellated region simply because cells have more neighbors there — an artifact of mesh resolution, not material. Giving each neighbor the full intensity makes crack **reach independent of cell count**, which is what you want for a tessellation that varies in granularity.

So the honest summary: the node field is a stress proxy, not conserved energy; the 4× represents "stress high enough to drive cracks every adjacent way"; physical conservation is enforced where it matters (the `Budget`, ≈ Griffith surface energy), so the *visible consequence* — how many bonds actually break — stays bounded and tunable even though the intensity field over-radiates by design.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-26 19:25 UTC

I'm considering a major refactor of this model. This doesn't make sense to me, it's very counter-intuitive. The brittleness as it is now doesn't shift the energy from vaporizing to breaking bonds, it just means how much of the energy is lost at each edge traversal, it doesn't redirect it anywhere else, the energy just disappears. Since the edges don't accumulate stress, an edge either breaks completely or isn't affected at all. There are also too many different ultra-specific parameters that only marginally change the fracture behaviour but have become a hell to understand and to tune. Do you agree?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-26 19:26 UTC

Largely yes — but let me separate the parts I think are genuinely broken from the parts that are defensible-but-badly-explained, because the refactor should keep what works.

## Where you're flatly right

**The vanishing energy is the real problem.** You've correctly diagnosed it: `tr = (deliver − eff)·Transmission` discards the `(1 − Transmission)` fraction into nothing. It doesn't become vaporization, fling, or heat — it's gone. So `Brittleness` isn't a *partition* knob (shatter-vs-fling), it's a *decay* knob (reach), and the energy it "saves" by being brittle isn't redirected anywhere. Worse, the actual surface/kinetic partition is a *different* parameter (`SurfaceFraction`) computed *upstream* in `ComputeBudget`, so the two levers you'd expect to interact ("how brittle" and "how much energy goes to cracking") are wired to completely separate mechanisms that don't talk to each other. That's the core unintuitiveness, and it's not just cosmetic — it means you genuinely *can't* reason about where energy goes, which is why tuning feels like whack-a-mole.

**Binary bonds are now inconsistent with your own model.** `if (deliver > eff) break; else nothing` — no accumulation, no arrest, no partial weakening. This was *already* a simplification, but Phase 7 made it actively incoherent: you just gave **cells** a `Damage` accumulator that builds across hits, while **bonds** remain all-or-nothing within a single propagation. Two different damage philosophies in the same system. A crack also can't "run out of steam and stop halfway through a bond," which is exactly the behavior that would make sustained-fire-cracks-titanium feel physical.

**Parameter sprawl is real and some of it is non-functional.** Count the overlaps:
- Three toughness-like things: `Toughness` (bond cost), `IgnitionToughness` (start gate), `Concentration` (stress multiplier).
- Two directionality inputs (`weapon.Directionality` + material `CrackDirectionality`, averaged) plus two *hidden* globals (`DirExponent`, `BoostCap`) that no one can tune because they're consts.
- `BlastFraction` + `BlastResist` — and we established `BlastResist` **does nothing** in the live multi-frame path.
- `SurfaceFraction` and `Brittleness` both claim to be "the shatter lever."

That's ~13 material params, ~6 weapon params, several dead or redundant. You're right that most move the needle marginally while costing enormous cognitive load.

## Where I'd push back

**Don't throw out the core.** The highest-energy-first flood with a global `Budget` is actually a sound skeleton — the `Budget` is essentially Griffith's surface-energy criterion (a crack grows while released energy ≥ energy to make new surface), and the Dijkstra ordering gives you determinism and mesh-independence cheaply. The disease isn't the propagation order; it's that energy isn't *accounted* as it flows.

**"Non-physical" isn't the indictment — "un-reasoned-about" is.** A game fracture model doesn't need to be conservative to be good. But your actual complaint is that you can't predict it, and *that's* the thing worth fixing. Intuitive tunability is a more important design goal here than physical fidelity, and a conservative model happens to be the easiest way to get intuitive tunability — because every joule is visibly accounted for.

## The shape of a cleaner model

The unifying move: make the propagation **conservative**, so at each cell the incoming energy splits into named, summing channels — `break` (spent on bonds) + `vaporize` (local pulverization) + `transmit` (onward) + `fling` (fragment KE) = input. Then:

- **Brittleness becomes a real partition**: brittle → most energy transmits onward (long thin cracks); ductile → most dumps locally into vaporize+fling (blunt craters, short cracks). One parameter, visible meaning, and it *replaces* both today's `Transmission` decay and a chunk of `SurfaceFraction`/`BlastFraction`.
- **Bonds accumulate stress** like cells do — one unified `Damage` concept for both, breaking when accumulated stress ≥ strength, with cracks that arrest when the front's energy drops below the local resistance. This makes Phase-7 fatigue fall out naturally instead of being bolted on, and it's what lets a crack stop mid-body.
- **Collapse the param set**: one `toughness` (resistance to breaking), one `brittleness` (transmit-vs-dump partition), one `directionality` (merge weapon+material, fold the exponent/cap into it or derive them). Vaporization stops being a separate `BlastFraction`/`BlastResist` system and becomes "a cell whose local dumped energy exceeds its mass-threshold pulverizes."

The one decision that drives everything: **do you want full energy conservation** (every joule accounted across break/vaporize/transmit/fling), or a **looser stress-field with conservation only at the `Budget` level** (what you have)? Your whole critique points at the former, and I agree it's the right call — it's the thing that makes the model legible.

I do agree this is worth a major refactor. If you want, I can work up an actual design — the conserved-channel propagation, the unified bond/cell stress model, and the consolidated parameter list with a migration map from the current ~19 knobs — in plan mode, before any code changes. Want me to do that?
