5. Problem Solving:
   - Diagnosed the collision-energy bug definitively: CollisionSystem publishes CollisionEvent in narrow-phase (line 121) but applies impulses in Phase 4 (125-132); the deferred EventBus means OnCollision (via EventFlushSystem, which runs after CollisionSystem) reads POST-bounce velocities → tiny vRel → ~100 energy → ricochet. The ω×r/lever math was correct; only the timing was wrong. Fix: capture pre-solve ApproachSpeed on the event; BeginFracture takes normalSpeed; ComputeEnergy uses it directly.
   - Confirmed Task 7 (pulverized-cell phantom hits) is real: body collider is a CompoundShape never rebuilt on pulverize; same-frame raycasts run pre-fracture. Planned fix: per-part disabled flag on CompoundShape.
   - Confirmed Task 8: recoil `vKick.Linear += kick` is a raw velocity add, mass-independent. Planned fix: mass-scaled impulse.
   - 0c coupling analysis: body-body coupled to FractureGameplay (_activeCollisions cleared by fracture-result handlers, live Player, dash-invincibility, effects). User chose **pragmatic split** (extract grenade + piercing only; keep body-body in FractureGameplay).
   - Piercing pass-through: restitution alone insufficient (min-rule kills bounce-back but normal impulse still arrests at surface); needs Collider.Sensor + ProjectileSystem speed-bleed (Task 3).

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 14:29 UTC

**Task 1 complete** — all four projects build clean. Here's what changed:

**AI behaviour rework** ([GameSystems.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/GameSystems.cs)):
- **Propeller gate fix** — `AlivePropellerFraction` now returns `0` (was `1`) when a fragment has no propeller cells, so cockpit-only pieces can't thrust and just drift.
- **Aggro range** — beyond `AggroRadius` the alien ignores the player and **wanders** on a slow per-alien heading (`WanderDir`, cruising at 45% speed); within it, it engages.
- **Drone = kite** — `KiteGoal` holds `PreferredRange`: closes in when far, backs off when close, strafes/orbits in the band. Fed into the existing danger-avoidance steering (`DroneSteering` now takes a goal dir).
- **Bruiser = ram** — direct pursuit straight at the player (unchanged), now finished by the dash.
- Rotation/firing are gated on `aggro` (no spinning-to-face or shooting while wandering).

**Alien skill framework + bruiser dash**:
- `AlienDashConfig` ({ `Cooldown`, `TriggerRange`, `Speed` }) on `EntityConfig`; `AlienSkillState { DashCd }` component.
- Cooldown ticks in the AI loop; when the bruiser is within `TriggerRange`, ready, and can thrust, it adds a velocity spike toward the player and resets the cooldown — a periodic lunge to close the final gap.
- `AlienSkillState` is attached wherever the alien role is (shared `AlienPrefab.Spawn` → game + demo, plus `TagAlienFragment` so a surviving cockpit fragment keeps its dash).

**Config** ([game_config.json](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json)): drone `aggroRadius: 1500`, `preferredRange: 450`; bruiser `aggroRadius: 2000` + dash (`cooldown 7`, `triggerRange 480`, `speed 1600`). All tunable.

Please playtest and confirm: cockpit-only fragments drift (don't chase), drones hang back and shoot from a standoff, bruisers ram and periodically dash-lunge when close, and aliens past their aggro range wander instead of homing. ## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 14:48 UTC

Done. Both the dash and alien fire now go along the ship's nose (`facingDir`) rather than straight at the player's position. Since the alien still rotates to face the player while engaged, the net effect is that aim/dash track the player but are gated by turn rate — so a bruiser only lands its dash (and drones only hit) when actually pointed at you, and a player who jukes sideways can slip the lunge. ## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 17:06 UTC

There's a slight problem now, the kiting ai makes drones circle around the player so they continuously rotate to face the player and if the player stays still their shots are never accurate because their rotation always lags behind their movement.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:07 UTC

Good catch — that's the steady-state lag of the rotation controller. Let me look at the rotation controller and the alien firing path to fix it properly.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:07 UTC

Two fixes. First, replace the laggy PD+damping angular controller with a kinematic proportional turn — directly driving angular velocity toward the bearing eliminates the steady-state lag that an orbiting drone accumulates:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:07 UTC

Now gate firing on alignment — only loose a shot when the nose is actually pointed at the player (within ~14°), so an orbiting drone doesn't spray off-target:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:08 UTC

Builds clean. Two changes address the lag:

1. **Kinematic turn (root fix).** The old controller `vel.Angular += diff·rotSpeed·fdt` followed by `vel.Angular *= exp(-5·fdt)` leaves a large *steady-state lag* whenever the bearing keeps rotating — exactly the orbiting-drone case. To hold a constant tracking rate the damping forced a persistent error of roughly `ω_orbit·5/rotSpeed` (tens of degrees). Now, while engaged, angular velocity is driven **directly** at the bearing (`Clamp(diff·12, ±maxTurn)`), so the nose tracks the player with only a few degrees of lag. Damping is kept only for the wander state.

2. **Fire-when-aligned gate.** Since shots go along the nose, the drone now holds fire until `facing · dirToPlayer > 0.97` (~14°). The cooldown stays ready while it waits, so it fires the instant it lines up — no wasted off-axis shots at a stationary player.

Bruisers are unaffected in practice (they ram radially, so their bearing barely rotates), but they benefit from the same tighter tracking for their dash/fire. Worth a playtest to confirm drones now land hits on a still player and the turning still looks natural rather than snappy — if the kinematic turn feels too robotic, I can dial `maxTurn`/the `12` gain down.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:48 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 17:51 UTC

Good — I've now confirmed exactly how it behaves. Answering your three questions in order:

## 1. What CollisionSystem does for a sensor↔non-sensor pair

It skips **both** objects, not just the sensor. The relevant code ([CollisionSystem.cs:116-128](GameEngine/Engine/Systems/CollisionSystem.cs#L116)):

```csharp
bool sensor = cA.Sensor || cB.Sensor;
if (ResolveOverlap && !sensor)
{
    TrySeparate(...);                 // positional correction — SKIPPED
    for (...) GatherContact(...);     // builds the Contact for the solver — SKIPPED
}
... _bus.Publish(new CollisionEvent(...));   // always happens
```

If either collider is a sensor: no `TrySeparate` (no positional push on **either** body) and no `GatherContact` (so Phase 4's velocity solve has no contact for this pair → **zero impulse on either body**). The event is still published. So neither the round nor the asteroid gets any position/velocity change *from the collision system* — the round flies straight through, and the asteroid feels nothing from the contact. Any reaction has to come from the gameplay layer.

## 2. Is ProjectileSystem the sole consumer?

In effect, yes — though technically all three `CollisionEvent` subscribers receive every event:
- **`FractureGameplay.OnCollision`** early-returns on any piercing pair ([:202](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs#L202)).
- **`GrenadeSystem.OnContact`** only acts when a side is a grenade, so a piercing↔asteroid pair does nothing there.
- **`ProjectileSystem.OnContact`** is the only one that actually handles it.

One important fact: **the round isn't a sensor yet.** `PiercingPrefab` ([:42](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/PiercingPrefab.cs#L42)) never sets `Collider.Sensor`, so today it's a normal collider with `restitution 0` — which is exactly why it arrests at the surface instead of penetrating. Flipping it to a sensor is the core of Task 3.

## 3. Solver-coefficients vs. sensor + gameplay knobs

I'd **not** scale the impulses inside the solver. Your two-coefficient instinct is right — but apply them at the gameplay layer, not in `CollisionSystem`. Reasons the in-solver version fights you:

- The sequential-impulse solver applies one equal-and-opposite impulse `P` (`+P/mA` to A, `−P/mB` to B). Scaling the two sides by different coefficients **breaks Newton's third law inside the generic engine solver** and bakes a piercing-specific concept into code that shouldn't know about it.
- `TrySeparate` would still **eject** the round back out of the surface it's trying to enter — so you'd have to disable separation for it anyway (i.e. it's already half a sensor).
- Even with `restitution 0`, the normal impulse drives closing speed to 0 (*arrests* it). Scaled over 6 iterations × several overlap frames it still bleeds a lot unless the coefficient is tiny — and a tiny coefficient also kills the target-push you wanted independent. The two effects end up coupled, and it's iteration/framerate-dependent.

The cleaner design gives you the **same two knobs, decoupled and explicit**, on top of the sensor:

| Goal | Mechanism (gameplay layer, in `ProjectileSystem`) |
|---|---|
| Round barely slows | explicit per-pierce **speed bleed** knob (`penetrationSpeedLoss`), optionally scaled by target mass/toughness |
| Round pushes target only a little | explicit small **mass-scaled impulse** on the target (`targetPushCoeff`) — heavy asteroids barely move (also lines up with Task 8) |
| Heavy/tough asteroid stops it | **already there, physically:** the round's reciprocal self-fracture uses the *target's real mass* as the impactor ([:876](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/GameSystems.cs#L876)), so a big tough rock dumps lots of energy into the round → it shatters fast → stops |
| Round dies | natural: self-fracture shatters it, or TTL |

So the engine stays generic ("sensors report, don't resolve"), and the feel is tuned with clear, independent coefficients instead of a solver hack.

**Concrete Task 3 plan:**
1. `PiercingPrefab` → set `Collider.Sensor = true`.
2. `ProjectileSystem.OnContact`: dedup so each **target cell** is pierced once (use `ev.Contact.PartIndex` and fracture *that cell* instead of the current `-1`), with a short re-pierce cooldown fallback — otherwise the per-frame overlap re-fractures the same spot every frame.
3. Add the speed-bleed and target-push, plus the two new `weapons.piercing` knobs.
4. Self-fracture already handles the heavy-asteroid stop; just tune.

Want me to implement it this way, or would you rather prototype the scaled-impulse version first to compare feel?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 18:01 UTC

All four build clean. **Task 3 implemented** the way we agreed:

**The round is now a sensor** ([PiercingPrefab.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/PiercingPrefab.cs#L44)) — `CollisionSystem` reports the contact but applies no separation/impulse, so it physically passes through. All reaction is modelled explicitly in `ProjectileSystem`:

- **Per-cell dedup** — since a sensor never separates, the same contact re-fires every frame; a pierce is only deposited once the round has advanced `PierceSpacing` (20px) past the last one, so it carves a tunnel (one fracture per cell crossed) instead of grinding a single spot.
- **Speed bleed, sub-linear in target mass** — `bleed = penetrationSpeedLoss · √targetMass`, subtracted from forward speed (clamped ≥ 0). The √ gives you the "less than linear" you asked for: it slows a lot more in heavy rock than in light fragments, but a big asteroid doesn't bleed it proportionally to its full mass.
- **Mass-scaled target push** — `targetPushCoeff · roundMass · speed / targetMass`: heavy asteroids barely budge, light fragments get a real nudge (same shape as the Task 8 recoil fix).
- **"Can't pierce a heavy/tough rock" comes for free** — the reciprocal self-fracture on the round uses the *target's real mass* as impactor, so a heavy/tough asteroid dumps enough energy back to shatter the round.
- Lateral clamp is preserved (folded into the bleed step, now clamped against the post-bleed forward speed).

New `weapons.piercing` knobs, both tunable: `penetrationSpeedLoss: 4`, `targetPushCoeff: 0.15`.

**Two things to watch when you playtest:**
1. The per-pierce bleed total scales with how many pierces happen, which depends on `PierceSpacing` (20px, a const). If the bleed feels coupled to that in a weird way, I can switch to a continuous distance-based bleed — but per-pierce should feel fine.
2. Because it's a sensor, the round also passes *through* the player once `PlayerGrace` expires (fracturing the player via `PlayerImpactCoeff`) — same intent as before, just confirm it feels right.

Tune `penetrationSpeedLoss` / `targetPushCoeff` to taste. Should it (a) blow clean through small/medium asteroids losing little speed, (b) bog down and shatter inside big tough ones, and (c) only lightly shove what it hits?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:07 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:08 UTC

I traced the full path (`AsteroidPrefab.BuildProceduralAsteroid` → `ScatterSeedsUniform` → `VoronoiTessellator.BuildWithSeeds`). Here's the verdict.

## Seeds: uniformly distributed — ✓ correct

[ScatterSeedsUniform](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/AsteroidPrefab.cs#L204):
```csharp
float θ = rng.NextDouble() * Tau;
float r = maxR * MathF.Sqrt(rng.NextDouble());   // uniform by area
if (ProcPointInPolygon(p, convex)) seeds.Add(p);
```
`r = R·√U` with uniform θ is the textbook uniform-by-area disk sampling — without the `√`, points clump at the center; with it, density is flat. Then it rejection-tests against the polygon. Since `maxR` is computed *after* roughness ([:103](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/AsteroidPrefab.cs#L103)) the polygon is always ⊆ the sampling disk, so rejection stays unbiased. Result is genuinely uniform over the asteroid area. The `tries < count*50` cap is generous (acceptance ~60-70%). No bug.

(Minor nit, not a uniformity issue: `seedCount` is derived from nominal `radius` but seeds are scattered out to the larger roughened `maxR`, so effective density runs slightly below what `grainArea` implies. Cosmetic.)

## Concavity bias: works *structurally*, but has two real weaknesses

The mechanism is sound: [BuildWithSeeds](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L114) computes the full Voronoi over **all** seeds, then drops cells whose seed fails `membership` — leaving real gaps in the boundary (not redistributing). That's the correct way to carve concavity. But the predicate:

```csharp
membership = s => rng.NextDouble() > concavity * (r*r);   // r = |s|/maxR ∈ [0,1]
```
keep-probability = `1 − concavity·r²`. Two problems:

**1. It erodes the interior, not just the rim.** Removal probability is `concavity·r²`, which is > 0 for *every* cell with r > 0. At the one type set to `concavityBias: 0.7` (the r=80 asteroid), a mid-body cell at r=0.5 has a ~17% chance of deletion, r=0.7 ~34%. So you get **interior holes/voids**, not boundary bites. "Concavity" should be a boundary effect; the current curve doesn't confine it there. The low-bias types (0.02–0.15) are essentially unaffected, so this only bites the 0.7 type.

**2. No connectivity guard → floating cells / islands.** Bonds are built purely from shared-edge adjacency ([BuildBondsWeighted](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L350)); nothing checks that the surviving cells form one connected graph. Random removal can leave a cell whose neighbors were all deleted (0 bonds → a free-floating cell), or a rim clump severed from the core (a disconnected island inside one body). Such cells render and move as part of the rigid body, but in the fracture graph they're *already detached* — so the first hit anywhere pops them off for free, and you can get visible gaps. Again, rare at low bias, plausible at 0.7.

## Fixes I'd suggest (not applied yet — this was a review)

- **Confine erosion to the rim:** make the curve zero in the interior, e.g. keep-prob `1 − concavity·smoothstep(0.6, 1, r)` (or gate `r > 0.6`). Concavity then only eats the outer shell, no interior voids — and you can push the bias higher without artifacts.
- **Largest-connected-component prune:** after dropping cells, flood-fill over bonds and keep only the biggest component (discard orphans/islands). Guarantees every asteroid is one connected body. Cheap, and it also hardens the explicit-seed path.

Want me to implement either/both? They're small, localized changes in `VoronoiTessellator` + the `membership` lambda. I'd recommend doing both — the connectivity prune is good insurance regardless of the bias curve.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:16 UTC

All four projects build clean. The connectivity fix is in [VoronoiTessellator.BuildWithSeeds](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L117).

**What it now does** (membership curve left untouched, as you asked):

1. **Full Voronoi over all seeds** — each area-valid cell records its seed index, whether it passed `membership`, and whether it's a **hull cell** (shares an edge with the outline, via `SharedEdgeLength(poly, bound)`).
2. **One adjacency build** over all cells (shared Voronoi edges), reused for both connectivity and bonds — so no extra O(n²) cost versus before.
3. **Largest-connected-component prune** — flood-fill the membership-passed cells over that adjacency, keep only the biggest component. Orphaned cells and severed rim clumps (islands) are discarded.
4. **Hole-fill pass** — flood the *empty* cells; any empty region that never reaches a hull cell is an enclosed void → filled back in. Boundary concavities survive because their empty cells *do* reach the hull. So you get: solid interior, ragged/concave outline preserved.
5. Materialize kept cells + bonds straight from the adjacency (kept↔kept only), with the same seed-mult geometric-mean bond strengths as before.

**Net effect:** every asteroid is now a single connected body with no interior voids, while the concavity bias still carves the rim exactly as configured — including the `0.7` type, which can now use that high value without punching internal holes or spawning free-floating cells. Cost is unchanged in order (runs once per asteroid spawn, n ≤ 600).

Two notes:
- The degenerate fallback (no cells survive) yields a single bound-shaped cell with no bonds — safe.
- This only touches the procedural-asteroid path; the explicit-seed path (player ship, piercing round) is unaffected since it never carves.

Worth a quick visual playtest on the `0.7` asteroid type to confirm the rim still looks irregular but the body's now solid.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:32 UTC

Two things — the range, and something more important I noticed answering it:

**Range:** the field is a plain `float` with no clamping in the model, but it's only ever *meant* to be 0–1 (the demo slider clamps it there). Semantically: `0` = crack direction follows the pure contact normal, `1` = pure relative velocity (including spin), with linear blend in between. So 0–1 is the intended range.

**But it's currently a dead parameter — nothing reads it.** `AsteroidDirSpin` appears in exactly two places: the config model and the demo slider. No fracture code consumes it:

```
GameConfig/Models/FractureGlobalConfig.cs:44   (declaration)
Demos/AsteroidDemo/ConfigEditorDefs.cs:54       (slider)
```

The collision path ([OnCollision](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs#L229-L241)) passes the **pure contact normal** `n` as the crack direction — there's no blend toward relative velocity. So moving the slider does nothing right now.

This is almost certainly a casualty of the Task 0 energy refactor: `BeginFracture` used to take an `impactorVelocity` **vector** (which carried the relative-velocity direction `AsteroidDirSpin` would blend in), and we changed it to take a scalar `normalSpeed` + an explicit direction. When the direction became "just the contact normal," the blend — and the only consumer of `AsteroidDirSpin` — was dropped.

So you have a choice:
- **Re-wire it** — in `OnCollision`, blend the crack direction as `dir = normalize(lerp(n, relVelDir, AsteroidDirSpin))` (computing `relVelDir` at the contact from the two bodies' velocities + spin·lever), and pass `dir` to each `BeginFracture` instead of raw `±n`. Restores the intended behavior.
- **Remove it** — drop the field + slider to avoid a misleading knob.

Want me to re-wire it (and if so, should the per-body direction use that body's outward normal blended with the relative-velocity direction), or just remove it?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 19:33 UTC

<ide_opened_file>The user opened the file /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json in the IDE. This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_opened_file>
re-wire it

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:34 UTC

Re-wiring it. I'll blend each body's crack direction between the contact normal and the relative-velocity direction (including spin·lever) by `AsteroidDirSpin`. Into A is the direction B moves relative to A; B gets the mirror.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 19:34 UTC

`AsteroidDirSpin` is now live. In [OnCollision](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs#L229):

- Computes the relative velocity of B w.r.t. A **at the contact point**, including each body's spin (`ω × r`) via the new `VelAtPoint` helper.
- Blends the crack direction: `dir = normalize( n·(1−dirSpin) + relVelDir·dirSpin )`, clamped to [0,1], with zero-velocity and degenerate-blend fallbacks to the pure normal `n`.
- Body A fractures along `dir`, body B along `−dir` (the mirror — `vB−vA = −(vA−vB)` and `−n`, so it stays consistent with the old `n`/`−n` structure).

So `0` = pure contact normal (the old effective behavior), `1` = pure relative-velocity direction, linear in between. The demo slider already drives it, and Save persists it.

**Heads-up on the default:** your `game_config.json` has `asteroidDirSpin: 1`, which until now did nothing. Now that it's wired, the default genuinely switches collision cracks to channel along the **relative velocity** instead of the contact normal — a real behavior change (most visible on glancing/spinning impacts, where the two directions diverge most). If you want to preserve the prior feel as a baseline, set it to `0` and tune up from there; otherwise leave it at `1` and playtest. All four projects build clean.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 19:58 UTC

I'm still not conviced of the seed distribution, there are lots of elongated, unnatural looking cells and lots of size variation among cells of the same asteroid.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 20:00 UTC

That's the classic signature of a pure-random (white-noise) Voronoi: uniformly-random seeds cluster and leave gaps, so you get slivers, big/small neighbors, and elongated cells. Sampling "uniformly by area" is correct but it's *white* noise — it has no spacing constraint. The standard fix is **Lloyd relaxation** (centroidal Voronoi): nudge each seed to its cell's centroid a few times and the cells even out into rounded, similar-sized chunks while staying organic.

Let me check the config model and demo editor so I can wire it as a tunable knob.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 20:02 UTC

All four build clean. The seed distribution now gets **Lloyd relaxation** before tessellation:

- **[LloydRelax](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L421)** — each pass recomputes every seed's bound-clipped Voronoi cell and moves the seed to that cell's centroid. After a couple of passes the point set converges toward a *centroidal Voronoi tessellation*: cells become evenly sized and rounded, slivers and elongated cells disappear, but it still looks organic rather than a regular honeycomb. Centroids of bound-clipped cells stay inside the body, so seeds never escape.
- Runs **before** membership is evaluated, so concavity acts on the relaxed positions, and it composes cleanly with the LCC-prune/hole-fill you added earlier.
- **Tunable** via `proc.RelaxIterations` (default **2**): `0` = the old raw-random lumpiness, `2–3` = natural and uniform, higher = increasingly honeycomb-regular. Passed through [BuildWithSeeds](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs#L123), wired in [AsteroidPrefab](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/AsteroidPrefab.cs#L119), and exposed as a **"Relax Iters" (0–6)** slider in the demo's procedural-shape editor.

Cost is negligible — asteroids carry only ~10–60 cells in practice (the 600 cap is rarely near), and relaxation is a few O(n²) passes done once at spawn.

Since the default is 2, asteroids improve immediately with no JSON edits. Try the demo's **Relax Iters** slider on the worst-looking type — 2 should clean up the slivers; if you still want more uniformity, bump to 3–4. Want me to bake an explicit `relaxIterations` into the JSON per type, or leave it on the default?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 20:06 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 20:06 UTC

Engine builds clean. Quick check on the downstream projects (no signature change, but to be safe):

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 20:06 UTC

**Task 8 done** — all four projects build clean. [FractureService.BeginFracture](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L76) now applies recoil as a mass-scaled impulse:

```csharp
Vector2 kick = dir * (impactorMass * normalSpeed * weapon.Knockback);  // J = fraction of impactor momentum
vKick.Linear += kick / MathF.Max(1e-3f, rb.Mass);                       // Δv = J / bodyMass
```

Previously it added a raw velocity, so a tiny fragment and a giant asteroid both lurched the same amount. Now Δv scales as `impactorMass / bodyMass` — heavy asteroids barely budge, light fragments get genuinely shoved, which is the physically correct momentum transfer.

**Retuning note:** the meaning of `knockback` changed — it's now multiplied by `impactorMass` (the bullet/impactor mass), so the same numeric value produces a much larger raw impulse than before. Most player weapons are already at `knockback: 0` so they're unaffected; the ones that will visibly change are the **grenade** (`0.0074`) and **alien shots** (`0.01`/`0.005`). You'll likely want to bump those up to feel the same, then tune to taste. Asteroid-on-asteroid recoil stays at `0` (handled by the collision solver, as before).

Worth a quick playtest: shoot a knockback weapon at a small fragment vs. a huge asteroid and confirm the size-dependent reaction.

- **[VortexSystem](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/GameSystems.cs#L240)** now takes the world dimensions and each frame computes `centre = mapCentre + (ampX·sin(τt/Px), ampY·sin(τt/Py + φ))`. | knob | default (JSON) | meaning |
|---|---|---|
| `moveAmpX` / `moveAmpY` | 1400 / 700 | orbit amplitude px (auto-clamped); 0 = stationary on that axis |
| `movePeriodX` / `movePeriodY` | 40 / 31 | seconds per oscillation (distinct → open Lissajous) |
| `movePhase` | π/2 | Y phase offset (shapes the figure) |
| `borderMargin` | 700 | hard keep-out from borders |

Map is 5760×3240, so the clamp ceilings are ampX ≤ 2180, ampY ≤ 920 — the 1400/700 defaults sit comfortably inside, drifting the eye of the storm around the central area over ~30–40 s without ever hugging an edge.

**Engine** ([CompoundShape](GameEngine/Engine/Collision/CompoundShape.cs)) — added a per-part `_disabled` flag with `DisablePart(int)` / `IsPartDisabled(int)`. Part index == cell index (guaranteed by `BuildShape`), and pulverized cells stay in the body, so the mapping is exact. I folded the existing player-cockpit game-over check into the same lookup (it reuses the resolved cell index now instead of a separate scan).

**Effect:** once a cell is gone, the next bullet's raycast passes *through* the hole and either strikes the live cell behind it (normal fracture) or misses the body entirely and flies on — instead of being stopped and consumed by the empty crater. Physics collisions ignore the craters too, so bodies no longer catch on holes.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 22:36 UTC

What if, say, 10 bullets collide with the same cell in the exact same frame that gets pulverized after the first 2 hits? Wille the remaining 8 bullets be consumed?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 22:37 UTC

Good question — it gets at the limit of the Task 7 fix. Let me verify the exact ordering in the raycast system before answering definitively.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 22:37 UTC

Yes — in that exact-same-frame case all 10 would be consumed, and Task 7 doesn't change that. It only fixes the *cross-frame* case. Two compounding reasons, from the code:

**1. All raycasts are computed before any hit is processed.** [RaycastBulletSystem.Update](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/GameSystems.cs#L446) snapshots every bullet into `_seg`, raycasts them all against the *current* collider state, and only `_bus.Publish(...)`es `BulletHitEvent`s — which are **deferred**. So all 10 rays see the cell still enabled and all 10 lock in a hit on it. The hits aren't handled until `EventBus.Flush` later in the frame, by which point the ray results are already decided.

**2. Pulverization isn't instant — it's multi-frame.** Your premise "pulverized after the first 2 hits" can't actually complete within the frame. When `OnBulletHit` runs for each of the 10 events, `BeginFracture` just *seeds/accumulates energy* into the body's `FractureProcess`; the cell is actually removed later by `FractureCrackSystem` over subsequent frames. The `CellPulverizedEvent` → `DisablePart` therefore fires in a *later* frame. So the cell stays a live target through the entire flush, and every bullet that hit it deposits energy and is destroyed.

So `DisablePart` only suppresses hits on a crater that pulverized on a **previous** frame — exactly the sustained-fire "drill deeper" case. It can't help bullets that already raycast this frame.

**Does it matter?** For a single cannon (15/s) you can't get 10 bullets in one frame. It's the shotgun (17 pellets) or grenade shrapnel (45) converging on one small cell at close range. There, all pellets depositing into one cell reads as *concentrated damage*, which is arguably fine/desired — the only "waste" is that pellets which might have penetrated deeper instead all stop at the front cell.

If you do want the excess pellets to **punch through** in the same frame rather than pile onto the front cell, the fix is a per-frame `(body, cell)` hit-dedup: when a second pellet's ray lands on a cell already claimed this frame, re-cast it past that cell (a skip-list in `PhysicsQueries.Raycast`) so it strikes the next live cell behind. It's a moderate change (the raycast needs a "ignore these parts" set) and a real behavior shift, so I didn't do it as part of Task 7.

Want me to add that same-frame penetration, or is concentrated close-range fire acceptable as-is?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 23:14 UTC

<ide_opened_file>The user opened the file /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json in the IDE. This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_opened_file>
I'm noticing that sometimes things don't collide and phase through each other, happens a lot with the custom shapes (aliens, piercing rounds) but sometimes with asteroids too.
I'm having some ideas, give me some honest feedback on this and tell me if it's doable/makes sense.
The CollisionSystem could use the previous position of all the objects (not only bullets), so it can more precisely trace the segment of movement and measure point of impact/relative speeds. It should also emit *all* the other intercepted entities, with some kind of way to recognize the order in which they happened. That way the systems could choose to handle more than one collision according to their needs and logic.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 23:16 UTC

Honest feedback: the instinct is sound and the technique is real (this is essentially continuous collision detection with time-of-impact ordering — Box2D, PhysX, etc. all do versions of it). But I'd push back on the *maximal* form ("for all objects"), and I think the asteroid case is a different problem than the custom-shape case. Let me break it down.

## First, the symptom probably has two causes, not one

- **Fast + thin (aliens, piercing rounds):** classic speed-tunneling. At the 1/120 s fixed step a piercing round (1300 px/s ≈ 11 px/step) or a dashing bruiser can jump clean across a thin custom-shape cell that's only ~10–20 px thick, so no frame ever sees an overlap. This is exactly what CCD fixes, and it's why **bullets already don't tunnel** — `RaycastBulletSystem` sweeps `PreviousPosition → Position` as a ray.
- **Big slow asteroids phasing through each other:** this one I'm skeptical is tunneling — they're large and slow, so they shouldn't move more than a fraction of their size per step. If *they* phase through, that smells like a **bug** (broad-phase grid miss, a layer/mask gap, or compound-vs-compound contact generation failing for certain geometries), and CCD wouldn't necessarily fix a bug. I'd want to confirm before building anything.

So: **diagnose first.** It's cheap, and it tells us whether we're building CCD or fixing a broad-phase/contact bug. I can instrument the candidate pairs and missed overlaps and watch a phasing asteroid.

## On the specific proposal

**"Use previous positions for all objects"** — good instinct, and the data's already there (`Transform.PreviousPosition`, used today by bullet raycast + render interpolation). The catch: a single **segment** only describes a *point's* motion. An extended, rotating body doesn't sweep a segment — every part traces a different arc, so you can't just raycast one line. Generalizing means one of:
- **swept-shape / conservative advancement** (true CCD for polygons — the genuinely hard, fiddly part), or
- **sub-stepping** fast bodies (split the step so nothing moves more than ~half its thickness — simple, robust, just N× cost), or
- **speculative contacts** (expand AABBs by motion, let the solver resolve a contact *before* penetration — Box2D's default anti-tunneling, far less code than TOI).

**"Emit all intercepted entities, ordered"** — partly already true and partly very valuable:
- The current solver *already* emits every overlapping **pair** (one `CollisionEvent` each, not just the deepest single one), so multi-body contact is handled today for the discrete case.
- What's missing is **swept hits ordered by time-of-impact** — and that's genuinely useful, especially for the sensor/piercing case (a round should register *each* cell along its path, in order — which is exactly what `ProjectileSystem` wants). But: resolving *physical* collisions in TOI order means an iterative TOI solver (advance to first impact, re-solve, repeat), which is a real complexity jump for the impulse solver. Ordering is cheap to *report*; ordering to *resolve* is not.

## What I'd actually recommend (tiered, by value/risk)

1. **Diagnose the asteroid phasing first** — likely a bug, not tunneling. Don't pay for CCD to mask it.
2. **Swept-AABB broad phase** — expand each body's broad-phase AABB by its motion since `PreviousPosition`. Cheap, no solver changes, and it stops fast bodies from being culled before they're even considered. Often removes a big chunk of tunneling on its own.
3. **CCD only for flagged "fast/small" bodies** (piercing rounds, small fast fragments, maybe dashing aliens) — sweep + clamp to first TOI, leave big slow asteroids on the discrete path. This is what real engines do; full CCD-for-everything is mostly wasted cost.
4. **Sensors/piercing are the easy, high-value win** — they only need *detection*, not impulse response. Treating the piercing round as a swept shape that reports every cell it crosses (TOI-ordered) drops straight into the per-cell pierce logic `ProjectileSystem` already has, with none of the solver complexity. I'd do this one first after diagnosis.

So: **makes sense, doable, but don't build the maximal version.** The full "TOI-ordered swept resolution for all bodies" is a large, bug-prone rewrite of a working solver for marginal benefit on the 95% of slow contacts. The 80/20 is swept-AABB + targeted CCD for the few fast/thin offenders, with sensors as the first slice.

Want me to start by **instrumenting the collision system to confirm what's actually happening** (tunneling vs. a broad-phase/contact bug), especially on the phasing asteroids? That'll tell us which of the above is even worth building.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-30 23:29 UTC

Another thing I've noticed is that if an objects is inside another body and they don't have much velocity (doesn't happen often, sometimes with piercing rounds or with asteroids spawning on top of alien/asteroid cells) it gets stuck inside and rapidly twitches. This may be related, in any case it is a real bug

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 23:31 UTC

Yes, that's a real bug, and it's a **cousin** of the tunneling issue, not the same thing: tunneling is *missed* detection (the bodies never see each other), this is *penetration recovery* going unstable once they're already deeply overlapped. Same subsystem, opposite failure mode. Let me give you the grounded mechanism and where I'd actually fix it.

## Why it twitches (from the CollisionSystem code)

When two bodies are deeply overlapped at low speed, two things fight each other every frame:

1. **The separation normal flips.** Compound-vs-compound builds a manifold from each overlapping *cell*, and `TrySeparate` corrects along the **deepest contact's** normal ([CollisionSystem.cs:110](GameEngine/Engine/Systems/CollisionSystem.cs#L110)). For a body sitting deep inside, *which* cell is deepest changes frame-to-frame, and each cell's normal points outward from itself — so the push direction alternates (left cell says "go right", right cell says "go left"). Baumgarte correction (`0.4·(depth−slop)`, capped 16px) physically moves the body that way, and next frame it flips back. That's the twitch.
2. **Opposing impulses in the solver.** The iterative velocity solver gets contacts with conflicting normals from cells on opposite sides; satisfying non-penetration for all of them at once oscillates the velocity. The body never gets below the sleep threshold (`LinSleepTol = 6`), so it never settles.

Notably, **restitution is probably *not* the driver here** — at low approach speed `vn0` is under `RestitutionVelThreshold (30)`, so the bounce bias is already 0 ([:293](GameEngine/Engine/Systems/CollisionSystem.cs#L293)). So this isn't the `DeepNoBounce` thing from Task 13; it's normal/manifold instability under deep penetration.

One flag worth raising: **piercing rounds are now sensors** — they skip both `TrySeparate` and the impulse solve — so a piercing round physically *can't* twitch via the solver anymore. If you still see it after Task 3, that's a separate thing (possibly its self-fracture fragments, which aren't sensors, or a pre-Task-3 memory). Worth confirming which.

## Where I'd fix it (cheapest → deepest)

1. **Prevent the deep overlap at spawn** — for the "asteroid spawns on top of an alien/asteroid" case, the right fix isn't to make the solver untangle a deep overlap; it's to **not create it**. A spawn-time overlap check (reject or nudge the spawn position if its AABB/shape overlaps an existing body) kills that whole class cleanly and cheaply. This is the highest-value, lowest-risk change and I'd do it first.
2. **Stabilize deep-penetration separation** for the unavoidable cases — when penetration exceeds a threshold (roughly a cell's size), stop using the flippy per-cell deepest normal and push out along a **stable** direction instead (center-to-center, or a persisted/averaged normal). Monotonic push-out → no oscillation → the body can actually reach sleep.
3. **Speculative contacts** (from the earlier discussion) would prevent deep penetration forming in the first place — which is why the anti-tunneling and anti-jitter work share a root: *don't let deep overlap exist*. If we go that route, both bugs shrink together.

## Honest bottom line

Real bug, well worth fixing, and **mostly independent of the big CCD question** — you can fix the jitter without building continuous collision. I'd sequence it as: (1) spawn-overlap rejection now (small, contained, kills the most common trigger), then (2) stable deep-separation if piercing/dynamic cases still misbehave.

Want me to start with the spawn-overlap check? It's a self-contained change in the spawn paths (`AsteroidPrefab` / wave spawner / `AlienPrefab`) plus a small `PhysicsQueries` overlap helper — and I can instrument the solver at the same time to confirm the normal-flip diagnosis on a live twitch before touching the solver itself.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-30 23:40 UTC

All build clean. **Spawn-overlap rejection is in.**

- **[PhysicsQueries.OverlapsCircle](GameEngine/Engine/Systems/PhysicsQueries.cs#L72)** — tests a spawn circle (centre + radius) against every existing collider's AABB on a layer mask. Conservative (AABB-based, so it rejects near-misses too) and skips disabled parts. For spawn placement that bias is exactly right: a wasted retry is far cheaper than a stuck/jittering body.
- **[FindSpawnPosition](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs#L337)** now rejects any candidate that overlaps a body already in the world (`Asteroid | Alien | Player`), on top of its existing checks (off-screen, player-clear, same-wave `placed` list). The old code only avoided bodies placed *in the same wave call*, so a new asteroid could (and did) land on a drifter from a prior wave or an alien — that path is closed. This also covers the mothership spawn (line 400), which uses the same function.

**What this fixes:** the reported "asteroid spawns on top of an alien/asteroid cell → stuck + twitch" case, by preventing the deep overlap from ever being created — the cheapest, most robust slice, no solver changes.

**What it doesn't cover (deliberately, for now):**
- The **boss drone-spawner** (line 643) spawns drones right at the mothership's hull by design; if those overlap, the fix would need an outward-nudge rather than rejection. Separate, less-common case — flagged, not touched.
- **Piercing rounds** ending up embedded: they're sensors now (no separation/impulse), so they shouldn't twitch via the solver at all. If you still see it, it's likely their non-sensor *self-fracture fragments* — a different path.

**On confirming the normal-flip diagnosis:** you don't need new instrumentation — the existing `ForceLog` already prints the separation normal per frame (the `…along n{…}` line in [CollisionSystem.TrySeparate](GameEngine/Engine/Systems/CollisionSystem.cs#L188)). If any twitch survives the spawn fix, enable `ForceLog` (the `L` key) for that body and you'll see `n` flipping frame-to-frame — that confirms we need step 2 (stable deep-penetration separation).

So: playtest this first. If spawn-on-top jitter is gone and you don't hit residual cases, we can skip the solver surgery entirely. If a non-spawn twitch remains (e.g. fracture fragments overlapping), tell me and I'll do the stable-separation pass with the `ForceLog` evidence. Want to move on to **Task 9 (mothership)** or the visual bugs **11/12** meanwhile?

All build clean. Piercing-round shards now inherit the round's behaviour, via a new `TagPiercingFragment` applied in both fracture handlers (`OnFractureCompleted` and `OnFractureSplit`) when the parent body carries a `PiercingRoundTag`:

- **Sensor** — the shard's collider is flagged `Sensor = true`, so it passes through bodies with no separation/impulse. This directly kills the residual twitch we discussed (the old non-sensor shards collided and jittered).
- **PiercingRoundTag** — inherits the parent's `Direction` and `LateralClamp` (with `PlayerGrace = 0`, `LastPiercePos = ` the shard's centroid). - **Bullet layer** — [GhostSystem](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/GameSystems.cs#L361) now promotes piercing shards to the `Bullet` layer with an `Asteroid | Alien` mask (instead of the default Asteroid layer), exactly like the round — so they pierce the same targets.
- **Material, mass, TTL** — already inherited: the shard body carries `piercing_material` from the parent's cells, and the existing `ephemeral` path gives it the fade-out `TimeToLive`.

It's also **recursive**: because a shard now has its own `PiercingRoundTag`, if it fractures further its children are detected as piercing too and inherit the same properties down the chain.

Net effect: a shattering piercing round sprays sensor shards that fly through everything, keep cutting per `ProjectileSystem`, and fade out — no more colliding/twitching debris. Worth a playtest: fire piercing into a heavy/tough asteroid so it shatters inside, and confirm the shards pass through cleanly instead of sticking and vibrating.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 00:21 UTC

Now the game-design brainstorm. I'll organize by area, flag the **highest impact-for-effort** (marked ⭐), and tie each to systems you already have (ECS, `EventBus`, `ParticleSystem`, `IRenderer`, config-driven tuning).

## 🎮 Game feel / "juice" — the biggest satisfaction-per-line wins
- ⭐ **Hitstop / frame-freeze** — on a big fracture or kill, freeze `FixedDt` for 30–80 ms. Trivial (scale/skip the timestep for N ms), and it makes every hit feel like it *lands*.
- ⭐ **Screen shake** — a decaying trauma value on the `Camera`, driven by `CollisionEvent`/`CellPulverizedEvent` magnitude. ~30 lines, huge impact. Add a settings toggle/intensity.
- ⭐ **Impact flash + spark burst** — you already emit dust/flash; add a brief white rim-flash on the struck cell and a directional spark cone along the impact normal. Scale particle count with impact energy.
- **Hit-freeze on the projectile** (micro-stutter the bullet at contact) + **muzzle flash** on fire.
- **Chromatic aberration / shockwave ring** on grenade + mothership skills (a cheap expanding ring in `IRenderer`).
- **Floating score popups** at kill location (small, fading, color by value).

## 🎨 Ships & coloring
- **Player ship**: distinct silhouette color (cool cyan/blue) with an **engine thrust plume** particle when accelerating, brightening with thrust. Cockpit cell glows.
- **Aliens by role/threat**: drones a cold teal, bruisers an aggressive red-orange, mothership a menacing purple with emissive spawner/weapon cells. Color *cells by role* (weapon cells tinted, propellers darker) so the ship reads at a glance — and it makes the fracture damage visually meaningful.
- **Material-driven asteroid palettes** (you already map material→color; push contrast: ice bluish-translucent, metal steel-specular sheen via a lighter outline, glass emissive edges).
- **Emissive cracks** — tint cracks by accumulated damage (you now have `Bond.Broken` + `Stress`), so a stressed body glows hot along its fault lines before it shatters.

## 🌌 Background & environment
- ⭐ **Parallax starfield** — 2–3 layers of stars scrolling at fractions of camera speed. Cheap, instantly makes the 10× map feel like space.
- **Nebula gradient / vignette** — a soft large-scale color gradient + dark vignette at screen edges for depth.
- **Visualize the vortex** — you exposed `VortexSystem.Centre`; draw a subtle swirling gradient / rotating faint particles at the eye so the (now-moving) pull is readable.
- **Border indicator** — a faint boundary glow when near the map edge.

## 🧮 Score system
- **Combo/multiplier**: chained kills/fractures within a time window ramp a multiplier; decays if you stop. Rewards aggression.
- **Style points**: bonus for piercing multi-kills, grenade cluster kills, destroying a body in one hit, near-miss dodges.
- **Score = area × density × multiplier** (you already score by area×density) + a visible running multiplier and a **high-score** persisted to a file.

## 📋 Menus, difficulty & settings
- **Main menu** polish: animated background (asteroids drifting + fracturing on their own as a "demo reel"), title, Play / Difficulty / Settings / Quit.
- ⭐ **Difficulty presets** (config-driven, easy to add): scale `waveSystem` budget/cap growth, alien `aggroRadius`/`shootCooldown`/`dash`, `playerImpactCoeff`, vortex strength. Easy/Normal/Hard/Nightmare as named `game_config` profiles.
- **Pause menu** (Esc) with resume/restart/settings/quit.
- **Settings**: master/SFX volume (if audio added), screen-shake intensity, difficulty, show-damage-numbers toggle, maybe colorblind-safe palette.

## 🔊 Audio (note)
- If there's no audio yet, even minimal SFX (fire, impact thud, fracture crunch, low-health warning) + a driving ambient track is the single biggest perceived-quality jump in this genre. Flagging it as a possible sub-task since it may need a backend addition.

**Score popups** — aggregated exactly as you wanted: `QueueScorePopup` accumulates value (area×density) and only emits when it crosses `PopupMinValue` **or** after `PopupFlushWindow` of idle, merging a burst of hits into one `+320`. Size **and** TTL scale with the amount (`PopupRefValue` maps to max size). They rise, fade, and are drawn world→screen. So it's never per-hit spam.

All tunables live in `VfxConfig` (spark/hitstop/popup blocks) — editable in `game_config.json`.

**On triggers** (your call): right now popups fire from **non-player cell pulverization**, aggregated. Tell me which feels right and I'll rewire the trigger — the aggregation stays regardless. Same for hitstop if you want it on more/fewer events.

---

## Coloring ideas (asteroids + ships)

You already have the data to drive all of this: cells carry `Role` and `DensityMult`, bonds carry `Broken`/`Stress`.

**Asteroids**
- **Density → darkness/saturation**: map each cell's `DensityMult` to lightness — denser cells (cluster cores) render darker and more saturated, so a body reads as a hard heavy core with a lighter crust. Instant "gradient" with zero new data.
- **Fake directional light**: shade each cell by its centroid vs. a fixed light direction (dot product) for cheap volume — turns flat fills into rounded rock.
- **Material identity**: metal steely-desaturated with a bright rim outline (specular feel); ice bluish + translucent; glass dark fill with emissive edges. Push contrast between materials.
- **Stress glow**: tint cells adjacent to high-`Stress`/`Broken` bonds warm (ember) so a body visibly "heats up" along fault lines before shattering.

**Ships (player + aliens)**
- **Role-based cell tint** — the big readability win: cockpit bright/emissive (player = cyan glow), propellers dark engine-tone (+ a thrust plume when accelerating), weapon cells accent-colored per weapon (cannon-yellow / shotgun-orange / piercing-white / grenade-green), spawner cells pulsing (mothership), hull the base body color. Damage then means something visually.
- **Faction palettes**: player cool blue/cyan, drones teal, bruisers red-orange, mothership deep purple with emissive spawner/weapon cells.
- **Density darkening on armor cells** too (heavier hull = darker), same as asteroids.
- **Low-health tell**: cockpit reddens as adjacent bonds stress (you already have the signal via the HUD gradient work).

**How I'd implement it (when you're ready):** compute a **per-cell fill color at spawn** (base material/faction color → role tint → density lightness → optional light shading) and store it per cell, then render bodies **per-cell** (`FillPolygon` per cell, like the HUD widget) instead of one flat `FillPath`. Precomputing at spawn keeps per-frame cost low. It's a meaty visual sub-task — I'd slot it as its own item (it overlaps the "Ships & coloring" area you'd deprioritized, but you clearly want it now).

Want me to (a) fold coloring in as the next 14 sub-task after you tune the juice, and (b) tell me your preferred popup/hitstop triggers so I can lock those in?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 12:02 UTC

All four build clean. **Task 14.D — per-cell coloring — is implemented:**

- **[CellColorizer](GameEngine/Gameplay/CellColorizer.cs)** computes each cell's fill from three layers: **role tint** (cockpit=bright glow, propeller=dark engine, cannon=yellow, shotgun=orange, piercing=white, grenade=green, spawner=magenta), **density darkening** (denser cells → darker, exactly your "darker where density is higher"), and a **rotation-invariant rim light** for volume. Asteroid cells have no ship role, so they just get density + rim shading of their material color.
- **[CellColors](GameEngine/Gameplay/Components/GameComponents.cs) component** holds the per-cell array, baked once in **[FractureBodyFactory.Spawn](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureBodyFactory.cs#L58)** — the single chokepoint, so **every** body is covered: asteroids, ships, fragments, piercing rounds. Fragments recolor correctly from their retained roles/densities.
- **[WorldRenderer](GameEngine/Gameplay/WorldRenderer.cs#L79)** now fills **per-cell** (`FillPolygon` with `CellColors[ci]`) when present, falling back to the old flat `FillPath` otherwise. Cracks/outline unchanged.
- **Faction palettes**: drones **teal**, bruisers **red-orange**, mothership **deep purple**; player stays **blue**; asteroids keep material colors — role tints layer on top of each.

Net: ships now read at a glance (weapon/cockpit/propeller cells are distinct, and damage is visible as those colored cells vanish), and asteroids show a shaded "heavy dark core, lit rim" look.

Two notes:
- The shading strengths (`DensityDarken`, `RimLight`) and the role/faction palette are constants in `CellColorizer`/`AlienPrefab` for now. If you want to tune them live, I can lift them into a `colors` config block (the plan's "config-driven palette") — say the word.
- Per-cell fills are a bit more draw calls than the flat path; fine at current counts, and it's on the list to revisit in the Task 10 perf pass if needed.

Playtest the look. Want the palette moved to config for tuning, or shall I move on to **14.B (score system)** or **14.C (menus)** next?

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-01 17:35 UTC

Looks very nice, one thing that bothers me is that now that we have slight variety in the colors of the cells their borders become very obvious, I would like them to blend better so it's not obvious which are the cells an asteroid/ship is composed of. Is it possible to do cheaply? Also maybe the cracks should be a bit thicker.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:36 UTC

Cheap fix, yes: the borders show because each cell is a flat fill and the density/rim shading makes adjacent cells step in color. I'll **smooth the base shading across bonded neighbors** (a couple of Laplacian passes over the bond graph, done once at spawn — free per frame) so the body reads as a smooth gradient rather than tiles. Key detail: I'll smooth the base shading *first*, then apply the **role accents on top** — so asteroid/hull borders blend away, but ship weapon/cockpit cells stay crisp and readable.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:36 UTC

Now thicker cracks — let me bump the crack line width in both draw paths:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:37 UTC

Both build clean.

**Cell-border blending** ([CellColorizer](GameEngine/Gameplay/CellColorizer.cs)) — restructured into three stages:
1. Compute the **base shading** (density darken + rim light) per cell, no role tint.
2. **Blend it across bonded neighbors** — a couple of Jacobi Laplacian passes over the bond graph (`SmoothPasses=2`, `SmoothBlend=0.55`). This pulls each cell toward its neighbors' average, so the low-frequency gradient (dark core → lit rim) survives but the per-cell steps at shared edges disappear — the body reads as a smooth shaded shape, not visible tiles.
3. Apply **role accents on top of the blend** — so ship weapon/cockpit/propeller cells stay crisp and readable while asteroid/hull borders melt away.

It's fully at-spawn (O(passes × bonds)), zero per-frame cost.

**Thicker cracks** — bumped the crack line width `1f → 2.2f` in both draw paths ([WorldRenderer](GameEngine/Gameplay/WorldRenderer.cs#L115)).

Playtest it. If asteroids still show borders, nudge `SmoothPasses` to 3 or `SmoothBlend` up; if ship role cells now look too soft-edged, lower `SmoothBlend` (they're accented post-blend, so they should still pop). Cracks are `2.2` — easy to dial. Want me to lift these blend/crack constants into the `vfx`/a `colors` config block so you can tune them live, or move on to **14.B (score)** / **14.C (menus)**?

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-01 17:43 UTC

The borders are still visible and it's not because of the color changing, it might be because cells don't perfectly overlap and the borders need to be filled?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:45 UTC

That's exactly it — this isn't color, it's **anti-aliasing seams**: each cell is filled as a separate AA'd polygon, and along a shared edge both cells' edges fade to transparent, leaving a ~1px gap that shows the dark background. Even identical colors would show it. The cheap fix is to **fill the whole body as one solid union first (which has no internal seams), then draw the per-cell colors on top** — any hairline gap then reveals body color, not the background.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:45 UTC

Now add the `CellPad` constant:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-01 17:46 UTC

All build clean. I attacked the seam two ways so it's robustly gone:

1. **Solid union underlay** — the whole body is filled once as a single multi-cell `FillPath` (no internal seams) in `col.Fill`, *then* the per-cell colors draw on top. Any sub-pixel AA gap between cells now reveals body color, not the black background.
2. **Slight per-cell overdraw** — each cell polygon is inflated `CellPad` (0.75 world-px) outward from its centroid, so neighbors physically overlap and cover the seam outright.

Together these eliminate both the "gap shows background" and the "edges don't quite meet" cases. Cost is one extra `FillPath` per body plus a tiny per-vertex push — negligible.

Playtest — the borders should be gone now. Knobs if needed: `CellPad` in [WorldRenderer](GameEngine/Gameplay/WorldRenderer.cs#L23) (bump to ~1.0 if any hairline survives, though the underlay alone should cover it), and the crack width is at `2.2`. If it looks clean, I'll move on to **14.B (score)** or **14.C (menus)** — your call.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-02 12:03 UTC

Confirmed the key facts (mothership is skipped by the AI so it never rotates; dash uses `aim.Dir`; aim turn = `RotSpeed·dt`). Here's the answer to your question, then the refined plan + recap.

## The color/relax question

That coloring is the **HUD ship widget** (`DrawShipWidget`), which tints each cell by `Broken ? 1 : Stress/Strength` → green→orange→red. Two different lifetimes are in play:

- **`relaxRate`** (per material, in `StressRelaxSystem`) decays each bond's `Stress` toward 0 at `relaxRate` units/second. So *sub-threshold* damage heals over time and the cell fades back toward green.
- **`Broken`** is **permanent** — once a bond's stress crosses its (spin-adjusted) strength it's flagged broken forever, and relax *skips broken bonds* (you asked for exactly that earlier). The HUD treats a broken-adjacent cell as fully damaged (red) permanently.

So "different color on first hit, never changes back" = **that first hit broke bonds** there (permanent), not just stressed them. If a hit only stresses without breaking, it *does* fade back at `relaxRate`. So it's working as designed given the permanent-break model — but if you want light first hits to be recoverable, that's a tuning lever (player material `toughness`/`cellToughness` so early hits stay sub-threshold), **or** we change the HUD to show live `Stress` only (not the permanent `Broken`). Your call — flagging it, not changing it.

## Refined plan items (to resolve before implementing)

**P1 — Dash in movement/keys direction** *(small, clear)*
Dash currently uses `aim.Dir` (mouse). Change to the **pressed-keys (WASD) direction** when any is held, falling back to current velocity direction, then aim. Lets you dash sideways to dodge without rotating. Need to compute the WASD dir before the dash block (it's currently computed later).

**P2 — Slow-mo boosts rotation** *(small, clear)*
During slow-mo, multiply the player's aim `RotSpeed` by a new `slowmo.rotSpeedBoost` so you can whip your aim around while the world crawls. Add the config knob.

**P3 — Boss faces the player; ram along facing** *(medium)*
The mothership never rotates (the AI skips it). Add a kinematic turn-to-face in the boss update, and make the **ram lunge along the nose** (facing) instead of homing to the player's position — consistent with how alien dash/fire now work. *Decision:* for a multi-fragment boss, rotate/ram **each fragment** by its own facing (which pairs with P5). Need to confirm the mothership shape's forward axis (I'll verify from the shape file).

**P4 — Skills tied to a new `skill` cell role** *(large; couples with P5)*
Add a `"skill"` cell role. A boss can only cast skills it has alive `skill` cells for, so a bare cockpit can't spam everything. **Ambiguity to resolve:** you wrote "cooldowns should **scale down** as these cells are vaporised." Two readings:
- (a) *Weaken* — fewer skill cells → **longer** cooldowns (destroying skill cells cripples the boss). This is the natural "shoot its weapons off" mechanic.
- (b) *Enrage* — fewer cells → **shorter** cooldowns (desperation).
I read your intent as **(a) weaken** (matches "so a cockpit alone doesn't use all the skills"), e.g. `effectiveCooldown = base · maxSkillCells / aliveSkillCells`. Confirm which.
Also to decide: does *each* skill map to its own role (`skill_shockwave`, `skill_barrage`, …) or one generic `skill` role that powers all skills collectively? I'd suggest **one generic `skill` role** for simplicity, count-scaled — but per-skill roles give richer "disable a specific attack" play. Your call.

**P5 — Separated cockpits act independently** *(large; the boss refactor)*
Today the boss is one global controller (cooldown fields on `PlayingState`, `msCenter` average). To make each cockpit fragment its own boss keyed off *its* cells, I'd move boss state into a **per-fragment component** (`BossBrain { cooldowns… }`) and a system that, for each cockpit-bearing fragment, casts from *its* alive skill cells at *its* position. This is the real refactor — and it's the same extraction that makes the boss **demo-spawnable (F)**. So P3+P4+P5+F become one coherent "boss controller v2" piece.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-02 12:50 UTC

All four build clean — **Boss v2 refactor is complete.** Summary of what changed:

**Architecture:** Boss control moved out of `PlayingState` into a shared, per-fragment system:
- **[BossBrain](GameEngine/Gameplay/Components/GameComponents.cs) component** — per-cockpit-fragment cooldowns + skill/spawner cell counts.
- **[BossSystem](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/BossSystem.cs)** — drives *each* cockpit fragment independently (careful about nested `ForEach`/ref-invalidation across spawns).
- **[MothershipPrefab](GameEngine/Gameplay/Prefabs/MothershipPrefab.cs)** — shared spawn + `AttachBossBrain`, used by game, demo, and the fracture split path.

**Behavior (your decisions):**
- **Per-cockpit independence** — every cockpit-bearing fragment is its own boss, acting only on *its* attached cells; a fragment that loses its cockpit **sheds its BossBrain and becomes inert tough debris**.
- **Face + nose-ram** — each fragment kinematically turns to face the player and **rams along its own nose**, moving only itself (no more global group movement).
- **Generic `skill` role** — the 7 former "generic" cells are now `skill` cells (cyan-tinted). A fragment casts skills only if it has alive skill cells, and **cooldowns lengthen (× maxSkillCells/alive)** as they're pulverized. Spawn rate weakens the same way with spawner cells.
- **Win** = no `BossBrain` remains.
- **Demo-spawnable (F)** — press **M** in the AsteroidDemo to spawn the mothership; `BossSystem` runs there too.

**Playtest flags:**
- The ram direction assumes the mothership shape's forward axis matches the ship convention (`cos(rot−π/2)`). If it rams *backwards*, that's the axis — easy flip.
- With 3 cockpits, you initially have **3 independent bosses** each running all skills — potentially intense; tune cooldowns/counts if it's too much.
- `SpawnerAccumulator` is now dead (harmless); I can remove it later.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-02 13:03 UTC

Confirmed both facts. Here's the analysis, answers, and how I'd fold these into the plan.

## Answers to your questions

**Weights & normalization** — good news: weights are **already absolute values normalized by the system**, not constrained to sum to 1. At selection time the wave system does `total = Σ weights; pick = rand·total` ([ChooseAsteroids](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs#L435), and the alien branch), so you can put any relative magnitudes and they're normalized on the fly. So that part is how you want it.

**But aliens really are spawned separately** — you're right. Asteroids go through a proper budget-packing loop (weighted pick → consume budget/cellcap → repeat, a real mix). Aliens are bolted on: it picks **one** alien type, spawns `clamp(budget/BaseCost, 1, 3)` of *just that type*, using the full budget independently of what asteroids consumed. So no alien mix, and their count is decoupled from the shared budget/cap.

**Player cell colors** — already satisfied for the world: `CellColors` is **baked once at spawn and never mutated** (only read by the renderer). The world ship's cell fills don't change on damage; only cracks (world) + the HUD widget show damage. So nothing recolors the world ship. If you were seeing a change, it was the HUD widget — which you're keeping. So: **no change needed** (I'll just confirm in-game with you), unless you actually want the HUD widget color-change removed too.

**Background parallax** — yes, strongly agree, it's the classic cheap depth trick and perfect here. With a 10× map and a camera that follows the player, draw 2–3 layers (far starfield, near starfield, optional nebula band) each offset by `cameraPos · parallaxFactor` (far ≈ 0.1, near ≈ 0.4), tiled/wrapped. Near-free (just points), and it makes motion read as depth. I'd make layer count/density/speed/color config-driven.

## New/refined tasks (adding to the plan)

- **T16 — Aliens as first-class wave spawns**: generalize `ChooseAsteroids` into one `ChooseSpawns` that packs **asteroids *and* aliens** from the same budget/cellcap by weight (each alien = a candidate with `BaseCost` + `CellCount`), so waves become a real mix. Weights stay absolute/normalized.
- **T17 — Special timed waves**: a config list of scripted waves that fire at given `gameTime`s, each with its own weights, budget, and banner text (e.g. "ELITE SWARM"). Checked alongside the normal wave trigger.
- **T18 — Alien turn speed in config**: expose the hardcoded `maxTurn` (drone 7 / bruiser 3.5 rad/s) as `EntityConfig.TurnSpeed`; wire into the AI kinematic turn.
- **T19 — Parallax background**: 2–3 config-driven star/nebula layers scrolling at fractions of camera position, drawn before the world.
- **P6 note**: world ship cells already static — no action (confirm the HUD is what you want).

Let me record these in the plan.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-02 17:40 UTC

All four build clean. **Color-change-on-hit bug fixed.**

Root cause: the fill colors lived in a separate `CellColors` component computed per-body, and every fracture (even a minor first hit that just sheds a cell) **destroys and respawns** the body as a fragment — which re-baked colors from scratch. Since the rim-light and neighbor-smoothing depend on the body's own `maxR` and adjacency, the retained cells came out a slightly different shade → the ship visibly recolored.

The fix bakes the color **onto the cell itself**:
- New `Cell.FillColor` ([Cell.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/Cell.cs#L24)), computed once for a fresh body by `CellColorizer.Apply` (alpha 0 = "not yet baked").
- `FractureBodyFactory.Spawn` only bakes if the body is fresh (`Cells[0].FillColor.A == 0`); fragments skip it.
- `FractureSimulator` copies `FillColor` into fragment cells, so the color **travels with the cell** through every split.
- `WorldRenderer` reads `Cell.FillColor`; the `CellColors` component is gone.

Net: a body's cells keep their exact colors no matter how it's damaged or fractured — the ship (and asteroids) no longer recolor on hit, while cracks + the HUD widget still show damage. Worth a quick playtest to confirm the ship holds its color through the first hit.

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-03 09:45 UTC

<ide_opened_file>The user opened the file /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json in the IDE. This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_opened_file>
There's a slight problem in the gameplay loop: asteroids split into atomic cells that accumulate in the center of the vortex and linger without ever vaporising but still taking up space and filling the cell global budget. The player then has to destroy piles of atomic cells, which is both hard and not very satisfying; the best thing about the game is handling fracturing asteroids, destroying them while dodging flying fragments.
Can you give some ideas to solve this problem?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-03 09:46 UTC

Good problem to solve — the atomic-cell pileup undercuts the core fun. Let me quickly check the actual mechanisms (there's already an `IsDebris` path and a `minFragmentArea`) so my ideas are grounded.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-03 09:47 UTC

Found the root cause. A fracture fragment only becomes fading "debris" when it's a **single cell AND its area is below `minFragmentArea`** ([FractureSimulator.cs:242](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs#L242)):

```csharp
IsDebris = idxs.Count == 1 && area < mat.MinFragmentArea,
```

So a single cell whose area is *above* the threshold (rock's `minFragmentArea` is 180) spawns as a **persistent single-cell body** — those are your atomic cells. They hold cell-budget, never vaporize on their own, and the vortex rakes them into a pile at the eye. Here are ways to fix it.

## Fix at the source (recommended)
**1. Single cells → fading flying debris, regardless of area.** Drop the area condition (or add a "min persistent cell count", e.g. treat ≤1–2 cells as debris). Instead of a persistent target, a lone cell becomes a `DebrisPiece` with velocity + a TTL — it still flies off (keeping the dodge-the-fragments feel) but fades in a couple seconds. This kills the pileup *and* the budget clog at the source, while preserving exactly the part you love (big asteroid → destroyable chunks + flying shards). Tunables: min-persistent-cell-count and debris TTL.

## Turn the vortex into an asset (great complement)
**2. Vortex core "drain".** Anything that reaches the vortex's inner radius gets vaporized with a nice implosion VFX. The eye of the storm *eats* junk instead of hoarding it — and it becomes a spatial hazard you must avoid drifting into. Very thematic, and it cleans up whatever still clumps (medium chunks too). Tunables: core radius, whether it also hurts the player.

## Cheap safety nets
**3. Age-out small fragments** — give any low-cell/small fragment a TTL so leftovers fade after ~10–20s even if ignored (a gentle janitor).
**4. Cap "junk" bodies** — when single-cell/tiny bodies exceed a cap, fade the oldest, so the budget can't be strangled.
**5. Exclude tiny fragments from the cell budget** (or discount them), so they never block new spawns even while visible.

## Tuning levers (no code)
**6.** Raise `minFragmentArea` and/or lower the vaporize threshold so hits on small pieces *pulverize* rather than shed atomic cells; give single-cell bodies low `cellToughness` so they pop in one shot.

---

**My recommendation:** the one-two of **#1 (single cells → fading debris)** + **#2 (vortex core drain)**. Together they remove the chore *and* enhance the core loop — fracturing yields destroyable chunks plus flying debris (no cleanup), and the vortex becomes a dramatic drain/hazard instead of a junk magnet. Add **#3** as insurance.

Want me to implement #1 + #2 (config-driven, so you can tune the thresholds and core radius)? I'd start with #1 since it addresses the root cause directly.

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-03 09:57 UTC

I was thinking of something else entilrely; change the minFragmentArea. Cells/bodies below the minFragmentArea don't just fade artificially, they become fragile bodies that completely vaporise completely the moment a beginFracture method is called on them. I'll raise the minFragmentArea to be ~grainArea, so 50% of the cells will fall in that category. This way even the slightest touch will be enough to vaporise them without introducing any new logic or artificially destroying them. If that won't be enough we could make the vortex have a dot radius around its center, so these bodies would instantly vaporise when reaching it. We could also raise the minFragmentArea so that most single cells would fall in the fragile fragment category. What do you think?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-03 09:59 UTC

I think it's a good approach — arguably better than my "auto-fade" idea, because it stays true to the physics model (no artificial destruction) and it fixes the *actual* pain point: those atomic cells aren't just cluttering, they're **hard to kill** (a single cell only vaporizes once `Cell.Damage` accumulates to `CellToughness·Area·Density`, so you have to chip each one repeatedly). Making them one-shot turns tedium into a satisfying pop. Two refinements and one caveat:

**Define "fragile" at the body level by total area.** Add a `Fragile` flag on the body, set at spawn when `Σ cell area < minFragmentArea`. Then a lone cell *and* a tiny 2–3 cell sliver are both one-shot, while a real chunk (total area over the threshold) stays a proper destroy-over-time target — so you keep the good part (medium chunks + dodging) and only trivialize the crumbs. `BeginFracture` checks the flag at the top: if fragile → pulverize all its cells (emit the normal `CellPulverizedEvent`s + debris + score) and destroy it, skipping the crack sim entirely. Zero new subsystems, reuses everything.

**Watch the budget, though — this is the one caveat.** Right now sub-threshold single cells become *dust* (`IsDebris`, they vanish and cost no budget). If they instead become persistent fragile *bodies*, you'll have **more** live bodies holding cell-budget, not fewer — you could trade "hard-to-kill pile" for "easy-to-kill pile that still clogs the budget until touched." Two easy guards:
- **Exclude fragile bodies from the cell budget** (they're ephemeral — one touch and gone), so they can never strangle spawns; and/or
- keep the **vortex core drain** as the janitor. I'd do the drain regardless — it auto-clears anything that clumps at the eye and doubles as a hazard.

**On the numbers:** setting `minFragmentArea ≈ grainArea` catching ~50% of cells is a sound heuristic (grainArea *is* the mean cell area, so ~half fall below). Just note it also affects the **initial** shatter — more small pieces will come off as fragile bodies (more flying debris to dodge, which is on-theme), so pair it with the budget exclusion so the first few frames of a big break don't spike the budget.

So: **fragile-flag + one-shot vaporize in `BeginFracture` + exclude-from-budget + vortex core drain.** That's fully in the spirit of what you proposed, just hardened against the budget side effect. Want me to implement it that way (all config-driven: the `minFragmentArea` threshold you'll tune, a `fragileExcludeFromBudget` toggle, and a `vortex.coreRadius`)?

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-03 10:07 UTC

I think the budget and coreRadius could wait and be implemented only if needed, for now the fragile flag + one-shot vaporise (also on asteroid-on-asteroid fractures) could be enough, I will playtest and see. One important thing to note: fragile bodies still apply normal force and fractures when impacting other entities, they just vaporise the moment it happens, but still potentially inflict heavy damage.
