## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-03 10:17 UTC

All four build clean. **Fragile one-shot mechanic implemented:**

- **`FracturableBody.Fragile`** flag, computed at spawn ([FractureBodyFactory.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureBodyFactory.cs)): `total cell area < material.MinFragmentArea` **and** no cockpit cell.
- **[BeginFracture](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L65):** a fragile body's own fracture floods enough omnidirectional, full-blast energy to pulverize every cell → **one-shot vaporize** (reuses the normal pulverize path, so you still get dust/debris/score). Works for bullet hits *and* asteroid-on-asteroid (each body runs its own `BeginFracture`).
- **Your note is honored:** the collision impulse and the fracture the fragile body inflicts on the *other* body are untouched — the target's `BeginFracture` still uses the fragile body's real mass, so a fast/heavy crumb still deals heavy damage; only the crumb's *own* response is "vaporize."
- **Exclusions:** cockpit bodies (live ships — so the player's cockpit fragment isn't one-shot); piercing (set `piercing_material.minFragmentArea: 0`, so it's never fragile and keeps its gradual self-fracture).

**One thing I had to change for this to actually work** (worth knowing): `IsDebris` previously turned any sub-`MinFragmentArea` single cell into **dust** (never a body), so it could never *be* a fragile body. I decoupled that — dust now only fires for genuinely degenerate slivers (`< 40 px²`), and everything else spawns as a body. So **`MinFragmentArea` is now the fragile threshold**, not the dust threshold, which is exactly what you want.

**Tuning you'll want to do:** raise the asteroid materials' `minFragmentArea` toward their `grainArea` (rock is `180` vs `grainArea 1500`, so right now almost nothing is fragile). Bump it to ~`grainArea` and ~half your single cells become one-shot crumbs, as you planned. Playtest and see if that alone clears the pileup, or if we then add the vortex core-drain.

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-07 14:45 UTC

<ide_opened_file>The user opened the file /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json in the IDE. This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_opened_file>
There is a small game design problem: the player can just camp in the corner of the map and stay relatively safe for a long time without ever needing to dodge asteroids, use skills and weapons. This strat should not be viable. How would you solve this?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-07 14:47 UTC

Good catch — let me diagnose *why* the corner is safe first, because it points straight at the fix.

## Why corner-camping works (grounded in your systems)
1. **Asteroids spawn at the edges and drift toward the world center** (`AsteroidPrefab` gives them velocity toward `worldCenter`), so they *converge away from the corners*.
2. **The vortex pulls bodies to the center too** — reinforcing a central "storm."
3. **The player has `vortexCentripetal/tangential = 0`**, so the vortex never tugs the player out of the corner.
4. A corner is inherently **defensible** — enemies can only approach through ~90°, so even aliens are easy to pick off one at a time.

Net: all the danger pools in the middle, and the corner sits outside it. So the fix is either *bring the storm to the player* or *make the corner itself unsafe*.

## Options

**A. Let the vortex be the enforcer (cheapest, most on-theme — my top pick)**
Give the player a **modest `vortexCentripetal`** again. Key insight: the vortex pull already **scales with distance from the center** (`excess = dist − deadzone`), so a corner-camper — who's maximally far out — gets pulled *hard* toward the action, while center play is barely affected. It's practically self-targeting against camping, and it's a one-value change. You zeroed it before (probably felt too strong everywhere); the trick is a *small* value + a healthy `deadzone` so the center is calm and only the fringes drag you in. Pair it with the vortex's existing Lissajous motion so the "safe center" isn't a fixed spot either.

**B. Border danger creep (the hard backstop)**
Make the outer margin actively hostile: hugging a border ramps up damage / stress and shoves you inward the longer you sit there. You already have `BorderDampSystem` damping velocity near edges — extend it into a soft inward push + escalating hazard. This makes the literal corner an uncomfortable place to sit, independent of the vortex.

**C. Bring asteroids to the player**
Have a **fraction of each wave drift loosely toward the *player's* position** instead of the world center, so wherever you hide, some rocks come to you → the dodge-and-destroy loop is restored anywhere. (Small homing steer, config'd fraction.)

**D. Shrinking safe zone (boldest)**
Battle-royale style: a lethal zone creeps in from the edges over time, so the survivable area shrinks toward the center. The most *reliable* anti-camp fix, but it's a real new subsystem + VFX, and it changes the arena feel.

**E. Hunter pressure (supporting only)**
Aliens that relentlessly hunt a stationary player (aggro scaling with how long you've been still, or a ram-type that ignores standoff). On its own it's weak (corners are defensible), but it's a good multiplier on A/B.

## Recommendation
Start with **A (player vortex pull) + B (border danger creep)** — together they're cheap, need no big new system, and stay true to the "central storm" identity: the vortex gently but inexorably drags you off the walls (harder the farther out you are), and the extreme border is a place that hurts to sit in. If that isn't enough after playtesting, add **C** (player-homing asteroids) or escalate to **D** (shrink zone).

Want me to implement **A** first (re-enable a small player `vortexCentripetal`/`tangential`, tune the deadzone so the center stays calm), and prototype **B** as a config-driven border hazard?

## 🧑 User · 2026-07-07 14:53 UTC

Option A + B sound great, I can do Option A myself by tuning parameters, we should plan option B and lay out a specification for it. What did you have in mind?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-07 14:55 UTC

Here's a full spec for **Option B — Border Danger Creep**. It has two coupled effects: a continuous **inward push** (nudges you off the wall) and an **escalating erosion** that damages the ship the longer you linger — with a grace window so normal edge-brushing during play is safe.

## Border Hazard — Specification

### Behavior
1. **Inward push (soft, immediate).** Within `pushZone` px of any border, the player gets an inward acceleration that grows as you get closer to the edge: `push = pushStrength · (1 − dist/pushZone)`, summed per axis — so a corner pushes diagonally toward center. Complements the existing `BorderDampSystem` (which only *damps outward* velocity) and pairs with your Option-A vortex pull.
2. **Erosion (escalating, delayed).** Track `borderTime` = seconds the player has been continuously inside `hazardZone` of any border.
   - Below `hazardGrace` (e.g. 2s): nothing — normal play that brushes the edge is safe.
   - Above grace: every `hazardTick` seconds, apply a fracture hit to an **exposed edge cell**, with energy ramping: `energy = hazardBase · (1 + (borderTime − grace) · hazardRamp)`. The storm progressively rips cells off the wall-facing side; sit there long enough and the ship is destroyed.
   - **Leaving decays, not resets:** `borderTime` recovers at `decayRate·dt` when you're out of the zone (a bit slower than it builds), so dipping in/out to cheese it doesn't work, but a genuine escape recovers.
3. **Feedback (juice).** Intensity ∝ `borderTime`: a red screen-edge vignette that brightens as it ramps, a warning line (e.g. "HULL ERODING") once past grace, and a shake/flash on each erosion tick. Without this the damage feels like an unfair invisible wall.

### Scope & state
- Applies to **PlayerTag** entities only (aliens/asteroids handled by `BorderDampSystem` as now).
- New `BorderHazardSystem : ISystem`, added to the game (and demo) system lists after `MovementSystem`, alongside `BorderDampSystem`. Takes `GameContext` (config) + world.
- `borderTime` lives on the player as a `BorderExposure { float Time; }` component (survives normal frames; reset on player death/respawn since a new ship spawns fresh). Single-player, so a system field also works — component is cleaner if control transfers to a cockpit fragment.

### Damage mechanism (implementation choice)
Reuse the fracture pipeline: each tick call `FractureService.BeginFracture` on the player at the cell nearest the exposed border, inward direction, with the ramped energy (control energy via a synthetic `impactorMass · normalSpeed`). This makes erosion look/feel identical to combat damage (cracks, HUD reddening, the fragile/pulverize path, dust) — no new damage model. It ignores dash i-frames (the storm is environmental).

### Config (`world.borderHazard`, all tunable)
```
enabled        : true
hazardZone     : 320     // px from a border where erosion timing runs
pushZone       : 380     // px where the inward push applies
pushStrength   : 900     // px/s² inward at the very edge, → 0 at pushZone
hazardGrace    : 2.0     // s inside the zone before erosion begins
hazardTick     : 0.45    // s between erosion hits
hazardBase     : <energy>// first-tick fracture energy (small chip)
hazardRamp     : 0.6     // energy multiplier growth per extra second camped
decayRate      : 0.6     // borderTime recovery rate when clear (×dt)
```

### Interactions / edge cases
- **With Option A:** the vortex drags you off the wall; the hazard erodes you if you resist — mutually reinforcing.
- **Map is 10× screen**, so `hazardZone`/`pushZone` (~300–400px) are a thin rim, invisible during normal center play.
- **Spawns:** `FindSpawnPosition` already spawns at the border strip — make sure new asteroids/aliens aren't instantly eroded. They shouldn't be (hazard is player-only), so fine.
- **Death by erosion** flows through the normal game-over path (player cockpit lost).

### Open decisions for you
- **Push-only vs push+erosion:** the inward push alone might be enough with Option A — erosion is the "hard backstop." Ship push first, add erosion if camping still survives?
- **Erode exposed cells vs whole-ship stress:** I spec'd hitting the wall-facing cell (directional, thematic). Alternative: uniform hull stress.
- **Should it also gently apply to aliens** (so they can't wall-hug either)? Probably unnecessary.

I'd add this to the plan as **Task B** and, when you're ready, implement it push-first (cheap, testable) then layer erosion + the vignette. Want me to record it in the plan file and hold for your Option-A tuning, or should I start on the push half now?

## What landed

**`BorderHazardSystem`** (replaces `BorderDampSystem`, fully config-driven, applies to **all** entities):
- **Damp** — the old hard-coded edge damping, now exposed as `dampZone`/`dampStrength`.
- **Push** — inward acceleration that grows toward the edge (`pushZone`/`pushStrength`), summed per axis so a corner shoves diagonally toward center.
- **Erosion** — a per-entity exposure timer; after `grace` seconds in the `hazardZone` rim, every `tick` it fractures the **most-exposed cell** (the one furthest along the nearest border's outward normal, hit inward with a tight environmental impactor), energy ramping via `baseMass·(1 + ramp·extra)`. Exposure decays at `decayRate` once you leave, so dip-in/dip-out doesn't cheese it. Player, aliens, and asteroids are all subject to it — the corner is never safe for anyone.

**Visuals** (`WorldRenderer.DrawEnvironment`, drawn over the field in world space):
- **Border** — translucent red rim strips + a pulsing red warning line right at the erosion boundary, so you can see exactly where the danger starts.
- **Vortex** — rotating spiral arms + a bright core at the live `VortexSystem.Centre`, so the (moving) eye is finally readable.

**Config** — new `borderHazard` block in [game_config.json](GameEngine/Assets/game_config.json#L926), all 12 knobs including the previously hard-coded damp params, modeled in [BorderHazardConfig](GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/WaveSystemConfig.cs#L75). Wired into both the game and demo system lists.

## One thing to tune
The erosion energy defaults (`baseMass: 8`, `impactSpeed: 1000`) are a blind first guess against `fracture.energyScale: 0.0005` — I couldn't calibrate the actual chip rate without playtesting. A bullet deposits ~5–6k energy; a base erosion tick lands ~1.5k, ramping. Watch whether it chips too slow/fast and adjust `baseMass`/`impactSpeed`/`ramp`; `grace`/`tick`/`pushStrength` are the feel dials. This dovetails with your Option-A vortex-pull tuning — the pull drags you off the wall, the rim erodes you if you resist.

## Game over as a live overlay

Death no longer swaps states. When the player's last cockpit goes, [PlayingState](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs) latches `_gameOverActive`, submits the score once (so `NEW BEST!` still persists), and keeps running the full system list — asteroids, aliens, the boss, the vortex and the border rim all keep simulating underneath. What freezes:

- **Score** — new `Score.Frozen` flag; `AddKill`/`Add`/`AddBonus` and the kill-chain decay all early-out, so wreckage grinding itself down after you die awards nothing.
- **Clock & wave director** — `_gameTime` stops advancing, so the HUD timer holds and no further waves, special waves, or mothership spawn.
- **Player control** — `PlayerControlSystem` is skipped, so the hulk just drifts instead of still steering and firing (the ship entity survives its cockpit's death, so this was a real hazard).

The verdict fades in over the live playfield: a scrim darkens over 1.6s, then the headline/score/best fade in over 0.6s. `SPACE`/`ENTER` (only once the overlay is fully up, so you can't skip it by mashing during death) resets and returns to the main menu. `GameOverState` is still used by `WaveCompleteState` for the boss-win path, so I left it in place.

## Sand material

Added `sand` to `materials` and a `"sand"` case to `AsteroidPrefab.MaterialColor` — fill `rgb(150,118,58)` with a `rgb(224,190,110)` outline, so it reads as dark-yellow ochre with a bright sandy rim. The per-cell colorizer's density-darkening and fake-light shading do the rest.

One thing you should know I decided for you: a material with no asteroid referencing it never spawns, so I also added a **`dune`** procedural asteroid using it plus a `spawnBias` entry (`w0: 0.10 → w1: 0.06`) so you can actually see it in game. Its parameters and sand's are placeholders leaning "crumbly" (high brittleness, low toughness, low cell toughness, small grain) — tune or delete `dune` as you like.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 12:40 UTC

Good pushback — reading the kernel properly, **two of my four points were wrong**. Let me correct the record.

## How a front actually propagates

A front is a **greedy best-first flood** over the bond graph, not a path. `StepFront` ([FractureKernel.cs:74](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L74)) is *one pop*: it takes the **highest-energy cell in the frontier** ([:82-87](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L82)) and splits its energy `e` into named channels that sum back to `e`:

- `transmit = tf·e` where `tf = lerp(ReachMin 0.1, ReachMax 0.96, brittleness)` — rock (brittleness 0.5) → **53%**
- `dump = e − transmit` → **47%**, which splits again into
  - `flingE[i] += (1−blast)·dump` — cannon `blastFraction 0.1` → **42%** becomes fling
  - `vaporiseEnergy = blast·dump` → **4.7%** is the *only* part that becomes `Cell.Damage` at the impact site

**How many nodes channel outward:** *every* intact bond of the popped cell ([:139-153](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L139)) — broken bonds and bonds to pulverized neighbours are skipped. `transmit` is divided into two pools by the per-bond weights: a **damage pool** `Σwd/W` (breaks bonds, `wd` = perpendicularity) and a **conduct pool** `Σwc/W` (`wc` = alignment with the flow direction, sharpened by `Directionality` and `AlignExponent`). Whatever the damage pool over-delivers past a bond's `Strength − Stress` is `recovered` and added to the forward pool ([:172-175](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L172)). Neighbours take `energy[j] = max(energy[j], fwd)` — a **max, not a sum**; the losing delivery becomes fling.

## I was wrong about the "pure conduit"

You're right to be suspicious. For a **single front, energy never enters a pulverized cell** — [:143](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L143) (`if (pulverized[j]) continue;`) skips them when routing. The `transmit = e` conduit branch at [:97](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L97) only fires in a narrow **cross-front** window: cell X was queued into front A's frontier while intact, then front B pulverized it before A popped it. It exists to conserve energy, because `RouteFling` **drops** energy on a pulverized cell ([:192](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs#L192)). So it's not a systemic free-ride down the crater, and I'll drop that from the plan. (Your model instinct — pulverize ⇒ break its bonds — is defensible, but note it would make that queued energy vanish instead of pass through. That's a deliberate conservation-vs-simplicity call, not a bug fix.)

## I was also wrong that fronts don't advance independently

They already do. `FractureCrackSystem` steps **every active front** `StepsPerIteration` times per iteration ([FractureCrackSystem.cs:84-95](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureCrackSystem.cs#L84)) — equal budgets, separate `Energy`/`Processed`/`Parent`/`Frontier` arrays. The only shared pacing is `fp.FrameCounter`, and I checked `FromCrackSpeed` ([FractureProcess.cs:18-24](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureProcess.cs#L18)): at 120 Hz, `popsPerStep = crackSpeed/120`, and **every shipped material is ≥ 150** (rock 240, metal 180, titanium 150) → `popsPerStep ≥ 1` → **`FramesPerIteration = 1` for all of them**. The idle-before-first-pop bug can't even fire with your config. So no — making fronts independent would fix nothing, because they aren't the problem.

## What is actually making new hits feel weightless

The numbers above: **only ~4.7% of a hit's energy craters the cell it landed on**, while **53% immediately transmits outward** into a graph where the alignment weighting (`Directionality` 0.65 effective, `AlignExponent` 1.6) funnels it into a narrow forward cone — and where already-broken bonds are skipped, so it routes *around* and *along* the existing crack network. The visible result is the old crack growing, not a new crater where you just shot. It's not a scheduling bug; it's an **energy-budget** issue: the impact site is the one place the model spends almost nothing.

So the core feel fix is the **guaranteed impact bite**: in `BeginFracture`, before seeding the flood, deposit a configurable fraction of `E` *directly* into the struck cell's `Damage` and its incident bonds' `Stress`. Every hit then visibly craters where it lands, regardless of what any other front is doing.

Alongside it, one **real** bug survives scrutiny: if `fp.Done` is already set this frame (the split/finalise frame), `BeginFracture` appends the new front to a process that `FractureCrackSystem` skips ([:74](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureCrackSystem.cs#L74)) — **that shot does literally nothing**. It must start a fresh process instead.

Want me to rewrite Task 3 down to just those two — the impact bite (feel) and the `Done` hit-dropping bug (correctness) — dropping the pacing, conduit, and relax points, and optionally adding the `recovered` attenuation knob as tuning?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 13:54 UTC

**Tasks 1–3 done, all four projects build clean.** Here's what changed, and it's a good point to playtest since these three all affect how hits land.

**Task 1 — fracture seeds on the surface.** The narrow phase now carries the struck cell through to the fracture. `ContactInfo` gained `PartA`/`PartB`, filled in [CompoundShape.CollectContacts](GameEngine/Engine/Collision/CompoundShape.cs#L143) (which already knew the index and threw it away — and the *other* body's index comes free from `LastHitPartIndex`). `CollectPairContacts` swaps them back in the two branches where B is the reference body. `OnCollision` now seeds each body at its true contacted cell instead of `-1`. The `-1` fallback also got fixed: [NearestCell](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs#L179) now prefers the cell that *contains* the point, then nearest by **distance to the polygon** — never by centroid, which is what was seeding cracks inside intact rock.

**Task 2 — piercing pays its way.** New engine query [`CompoundShape.SegmentParts`](GameEngine/Engine/Collision/CompoundShape.cs#L193) returns *every* cell a swept segment crosses, ordered entry-first. `ProjectileSystem` now walks that list and charges the round for each cell (its pulverise threshold plus the residual strength of its intact bonds), cracking each one as it goes. Run out of budget and it craters the face it stopped on and shatters there. It leaves with whatever it didn't spend (`v ∝ √E`), so it decelerates through rock it *can* pierce. The old 20 px throttle keyed on a drifting contact point is gone — that was what left whole slabs on the penetration line untouched. New knob: `weapons.piercing.penetrationCostScale` (currently `1.0` — this is your main dial for how wall-like titanium feels).

Also worth knowing: I use the round's closing speed **along its own axis**, not `ev.ApproachSpeed`. The contact normal is a cell *face* normal, often near-perpendicular to travel, so the old value was the wrong quantity for something tunnelling rather than bouncing.

**Task 3 — the dropped-hit bug only** (impact bite held back as you asked). The no-op finalise path set `Done` and queued a *deferred* component removal. Since `FractureCrackSystem` runs before the event flush, any hit landing later in that same frame found a still-present but already-`Done` process, appended its front to it, and then had the whole thing deleted by `FlushDeferred` — that shot did **literally nothing**. That removal is now immediate, so the hit starts a fresh process instead. I'd expect this to matter most exactly where you noticed it: sustained fire on one asteroid.

Next up is Task 4 (crack speed ∝ impact velocity), which needs pacing moved onto the front. Want me to continue, or would you rather playtest 1–3 first?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 14:26 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 14:26 UTC

Found it — and it's an **ordering bug**, not the `Done` flag.

`RaycastBulletSystem` publishes `BulletHitEvent` early in the frame, but `EventFlushSystem` runs **last** — after `FractureCrackSystem`. So on any frame where the asteroid splits or finalises, the sequence is:

1. Bullet raycast hits → event queued.
2. `FractureCrackSystem` splits the body → sets `Done`, publishes the split.
3. `EventFlushSystem` finally dispatches the bullet hit → `BeginFracture` on a body that is now `Done` and about to be destroyed → **the hit evaporates**, but the bullet is still consumed.

And `OnFractureCompleted` destroys+respawns the body even for a crater-only finalise ([FractureGameplay.cs:415](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs#L415)) — so sand (`crackSpeed 80`, `grainArea 300` → constant detachment) is in that state almost every frame. That's exactly your symptom, and it hits bullets, piercing, and body-vs-body alike. My `Done` guard made the loss explicit instead of silent, but the hit was already being thrown away.

The fix is to flush hit events **before** the crack system, so a hit always seeds a front on a live body and gets stepped that same frame.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 14:27 UTC

Same ordering exists in the demo — let me fix it there too.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 14:28 UTC

`Flush()` is a drain-until-empty loop, so handlers that publish during a flush still get dispatched in the same pass — safe to call twice. All four projects build clean.

## What was actually wrong

The `Done` guard I added last round was treating a symptom. The real defect is that **impacts were flushed too late in the frame**:

```
RaycastBulletSystem  → publishes BulletHitEvent  (queued)
CollisionSystem      → publishes CollisionEvent  (queued)
FractureCrackSystem  → splits the body, sets Done, destroys it
EventFlushSystem     → NOW dispatches the bullet hit … onto a corpse
```

So on every frame where a body split or finalised, each hit that landed on it that frame was dispatched to a body already marked `Done` and queued for destruction — the fracture never happened, though the bullet was still consumed. And because `OnFractureCompleted` destroys and respawns the body even for a *crater-only* finalise, sand (`crackSpeed 80`, `grainArea 300`) is in that state nearly every frame, which is why it's so blatant there. It was never piercing-specific — bullets, piercing, and body-vs-body all went through the same queue.

Now there are two flushes: impacts drain **before** `FractureCrackSystem` (so every hit seeds its front on a live body and is stepped that same frame), and the crack system's own output — pulverise/split/complete — drains **after**, so fragments still spawn as before. Applied to both `PlayingState` and the demo.

One thing this does *not* address, which is worth knowing before you test sand: at `crackSpeed 80`, `FromCrackSpeed` yields `FramesPerIteration = 2`, so sand's fronts genuinely advance at half rate. That's the material behaving as tuned, not a dropped hit — and Task 4 (per-front pacing, crack speed scaling with impact velocity) is where a fast bullet would start cracking it faster than a slow drift. Want me to carry on into Task 4, or playtest this first?

All four build clean. This third layer was the structural one:

**Every fracture fragment spawns as a ghost** — `Layer = Ghost, Mask = 0` for its first 0.04 s, so newborn siblings don't physically explode apart ([FractureGameplay.cs:380](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs#L380) spawns *everything*, even the big continuer, with `ghost: true`). - the bullet raycast mask was `Asteroid | Player | Alien` — ghosts simply weren't raycast against, so **bullets flew through fresh fragments unconsumed**;
- the piercing round's collider mask was `Asteroid | Alien` — the layer gate in `CollisionSystem` failed both directions against a ghost, so **no contact ever fired** and my swept-segment walk never even ran on those pieces.

A body that splits continuously — sand above all, with `crackSpeed 80` and `grainArea 300` — re-ghosts its pieces every few frames, so a large part of it was untargetable at any given moment. That's why your two symptoms tracked each other: same window, two weapon paths.

The fix keeps ghosts exempt from *physics* but visible to *weapons*: the bullet raycast mask now includes `Ghost` (this also fixes grenade shrapnel and alien fire for free, since they share `RaycastBulletSystem`), and the piercing round + its shards carry `Ghost` in their masks so the contact fires (they're sensors, so no physics side-effects follow).

Worth a sand playtest now — the three fixes stack: hits land on live fragments (this fix), on the frame they arrive (flush ordering), at the cell they actually struck (Task 1). If sand still feels spongy after this, what remains is its genuine tuning (`crackSpeed 80` halves front advance rate) rather than lost hits — and that's Task 4's territory, where impact velocity scales the crack rate. It works fine now, however we need to tune it down a little, it's too powerful right now. The formula used for the speed loss doesn't feel right and doesn't leave much space for tuning. How would you refactor the piercing round?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 17:13 UTC

The current model's core problem: **the budget refreshes every frame**. `E` is recomputed from the round's current speed each frame, and it only has to afford the one or two cells crossed *that* frame — so it never really "runs out", it just decays multiplicatively. Worse, everything is coupled: the same `E` is both the penetration gate *and* the fracture energy dumped into each cell (via `ImpactEnergy`'s reduced-mass physics, shared with `energyScale` tuning for all weapons). So "how far it goes", "how much it wrecks around the tunnel", and "how fast it slows" are all one knob wearing three hats — that's why it feels untunable and too strong at once.

## Proposed refactor: an explicit, lifetime penetration budget

Terminal-ballistics style — the round carries **PenetrationPower `P`**, set once at fire from config, spent over its whole life:

```
at fire:            P = penetrationPower                     (weapon config)
per cell crossed:   cost = penetrationCostScale × (cell pulverise threshold
                                                   + Σ residual intact-bond strength)
                    if P < cost → crater the face with what's left, SHATTER, stop
                    else        → P -= cost, crack the cell
speed:              v = v₀ · (P / P₀) ^ speedExponent        (pure feel, no physics coupling)
```

And **damage is its own dial**: each crossed cell is fractured with energy `pierceDamageScale × cost` — at `1.0` that's "just enough to carve the tunnel cell with modest spillover"; raise it for collateral shatter around the line, lower it for a clean needle. `BeginFracture` still does the cracking, so the crack model/visuals stay consistent — we just stop feeding it the full reduced-mass impact energy per cell.

That gives four orthogonal knobs, each mapping to one sentence of feel:

| Knob | What it tunes |
|---|---|
| `penetrationPower` | Tunnel length — total material (thresholds + bonds) one round can chew through |
| `penetrationCostScale` | Exchange rate per material — makes titanium a wall without touching power |
| `pierceDamageScale` | Collateral — needle (< 1) vs shredder (> 1) around the tunnel |
| `speedExponent` | How the round visually decelerates as it spends power (0 = constant speed until it dies, 1 = linear fade) |

The failed-pierce shatter, the self-fracture, and TTL all stay as they are. "Too powerful" then gets fixed by lowering `penetrationPower` and `pierceDamageScale` independently, rather than fighting the physics.

Two genuine decision points before I build it:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-14 17:21 UTC

Done — all four projects build clean, and the plan records the revision. Here's the shape of the refactor:

## What changed

**The old model's flaw:** the budget was recomputed from the round's speed *every frame*, so it only ever had to afford the one or two cells crossed that frame — it never genuinely ran out, and the same number was simultaneously the penetration gate and the fracture energy dumped per cell. One number, three jobs.

**The new model** — terminal ballistics with a lifetime budget:

- At fire, the round gets `Power = penetrationPower`, and the tag stores the KE→power exchange rate (`PowerPerKE = penetrationPower / ½m₀v₀²`). Per your decisions: power derives from mass·velocity², so **shards recompute their own budget** from their own mass and fling speed at spawn — a big fast shard stays mean, slivers arrive nearly spent. No extra knob needed.
- Each cell crossed charges `cost = penetrationCostScale × (pulverise threshold + residual intact-bond strength)`, deducted from `Power` permanently. Can't pay → dumps what's left into that face and **shatters there** (unchanged).
- **Damage decoupled:** each crossed cell is fractured with `pierceDamageScale × cost` via a new engine entry, [`FractureService.DepositEnergy`](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureService.cs) — an exact-energy seed with no impulse physics (the fragile one-shot override still applies). No more full reduced-mass impact per cell, which is where most of the excess power was coming from.
- **Speed is pure feel:** `v = v₀·(P/P₀)^pierceSpeedExponent`, applied incrementally (the steps compose to exactly that power law).

## Your four dials (in `weapons.piercing`)

- `penetrationPower: 60000` — tunnel length. With your `costScale 3.0`, a rock cell costs ~22k → **~2–3 rock cells per round**; metal ~2 cells at scale 1 (≈1 at yours); titanium shatters on the face. Raise this if it now feels too weak.
- `penetrationCostScale: 3.0` (kept your value) — the material exchange rate.
- `pierceDamageScale: 1.0` — collateral: 1 carves the tunnel, >1 shreds around it, <1 leaves a cracked needle.
- `pierceSpeedExponent: 0.5` — deceleration curve (0 = full speed till it dies, 1 = linear fade).

`penetrationSpeedLoss` is gone from the JSON (the model property remains so old configs still load). Knobs are JSON-only — the demo's weapon tab intentionally holds only fields shared by all weapons, so I followed that convention.

Playtest when ready; `penetrationPower` and `pierceDamageScale` are the two you'll want to touch first. Then I'll pick up Task 4 (crack speed ∝ impact velocity).

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-16 08:54 UTC

**Task 4 done — all four projects build clean.** Crack speed now depends on impact velocity, not just material.

## How it works

Each hit's crack pace is `material.CrackSpeed × factor(normalSpeed)`, where the factor is `(normalSpeed / crackSpeedRefVelocity) ^ crackSpeedVelExponent`, clamped to ×0.25…×4 ([FractureTuning.CrackSpeedFactor](GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureKernel.cs)). At the defaults (`ref 600`, `exp 0.5`): a 2500 px/s cannon round cracks at ~2× the material rate, a 150 px/s drifting-asteroid grind at ~0.5× — same energy, visibly different tempo. A speed of 0 (unknown) means "material base pace", so nothing else changes behaviour.

The structural change that makes it visible: **pacing moved off `FractureProcess` onto each `CrackFront`** — every hit's front now carries its own `StepsPerIteration`/`FramesPerIteration`/`FrameCounter` and advances on its own clock in `FractureCrackSystem`. Without this, a second faster hit on an already-cracking body would have inherited the first hit's pace and the feature would be invisible. A subtlety I preserved: when all live fronts are merely waiting on their frame counters the process skips the split/finalise checks (as before), but when *no* front is active it falls through so finalise still fires.

Wired end to end:

- `BeginFracture` passes its `normalSpeed` through; `DepositEnergy` gained an optional `normalSpeed`, and the piercing round passes its closing speed — so tunnel cells crack at the round's pace.
- `PartitionFront` carries each front's pacing across a mid-fracture split, so a fast-cracking front stays fast on the fragment it lands in.
- Config: `fracture.crackSpeedRefVelocity: 600` and `crackSpeedVelExponent: 0.5` in `game_config.json`, applied via `ApplyFractureTuning`, plus two sliders in the demo's Fracture tab (which pushes changes live). The ×0.25/×4 clamp band lives in `FractureTuning` statics if you ever want to widen it.

**To verify in the demo:** shoot a big `metal` or `sand` asteroid (slow crack speeds) with the cannon and compare against a slow heavy body colliding with it — the bullet's crack should race, the collision's creep. `crackSpeedVelExponent 0` reverts to the old behaviour if you want an A/B.

Next in the plan is Task 5 — fragments inheriting `Cell.Damage`/`Bond.Stress` across splits. Continue?

## Task 5 — fragments inherit damage
`FractureSimulator.BuildComponentSpec` now copies `Cell.Damage` and surviving-bond `Stress` into fragments, scaled by `fracture.splitStressInherit` (default 1.0; 0 restores the old full-heal; slider in the demo's Fracture tab). - `pattern`: `scattered` (classic) · `burst` (tight cluster around one anchor) · `wall` (a line along one side) · `pincer` (alternating opposite sides).

- **`spawnDuration`** — your addition: the wave's bodies are queued at fire time and released evenly across the window. Crucially, **position and aim are resolved at release time**, so `atPlayer` tracks the live player and overlap rejection sees the world as it is then. Both prefabs took an optional `aimDir`/`speedMult` override (default behaviour unchanged).

Defaults I set for playtesting: normal waves stay `scattered/inward` but now trickle in over 4s; DRONE SWARM is a `burst` aimed `atPlayer` over 3s; ELITE ASSAULT is a 5s `pincer`; DEBRIS RAIN is a 6s fast `wall`. All tunable in `game_config.json`.

## #1 — Derelict game over (done)

A new `PlayerIsDerelict()` check in [FractureGameplay.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/FractureGameplay.cs): the run ends when the ship has **no propeller and no weapon cell left alive** — only cockpit and generic hull. It's checked at both places the ship loses cells: after any player cell pulverizes, and after a break-up transfers control to the surviving cockpit fragment (so a fragment born as cockpit+hull ends the run immediately). Since the game-over overlay from earlier keeps the world running, you'll watch your dead hull drift while the verdict fades in — fitting, I think. Note dash already requires propellers and all weapons require their cells, so this only ends runs that were genuinely unwinnable (slow-mo alone can't save you).

## #2 — Corner-camping, round two: ideas

The rim hazard + vortex pull made the *literal* border unsafe, but sitting just **inside** the rim still works: threats pool toward the centre/vortex, normal waves aim `inward` (away from a corner camper), and nothing follows you. So the remaining hole is *danger doesn't seek the player*. Options, cheapest first:

**A. Aim the waves at the camper — config-only, already built.** Task 7's machinery does this today: set normal waves' `direction: "atPlayer"` (with generous `aimJitter` so it's pressure, not a firing squad). I could also add a `side: "nearPlayer"` option so burst/wall waves enter from the player's side of the map. Zero new systems.

**B. Camping-pressure system — the targeted fix.** Track time spent within a radius (~600 px) of a trailing anchor position. Past a grace (~20 s), enqueue escalating hunter bursts (`burst` + `atPlayer`, drones first, then bruisers) every N seconds until the player relocates. It punishes *the behaviour*, not the location — works for any camp spot, not just corners — and it's mostly plumbing on top of `EnqueueWave`.

**C. Storm-chaser scoring — the carrot.** Scale kill points by proximity to the vortex eye (or recent movement): camping starves your score (combo already decays), playing inside the storm multiplies it. One factor in `Score.AddKill`, HUD shows the bonus. Makes camping *pointless* rather than fatal.

**D. The eye seeks the idle.** Blend the vortex's Lissajous centre slowly toward a player who hasn't moved in a while — the storm (and everything it drags) wanders to you. Most thematic, pairs beautifully with Task 8's vortex visuals, medium effort.

**E. Rim grows over the run.** `hazardZone` creeps outward (+~15 px / 30 s), slowly squeezing the playfield. Global, simple, but punishes everyone equally rather than campers specifically.

My recommendation: **A immediately** (it's a config edit), **B as the real fix**, and **C** if you want optimal play to *chase* danger rather than merely not flee it. Which combination do you want in the sprint?

## A — nearPlayer waves + bigger world

- **World extended to 7680×4320** (was 5760×3240 — one extra screen per axis), `BorderZone` and the hazard rim untouched. With the longer sides, there's always off-screen border strip on every side of the player, corner included — the viewport rejection in spawn placement keeps working, it just never runs out of room anymore.

## B — camping response

New `waveSystem.campingResponse` block, tracked in [PlayingState.UpdateCampingResponse](GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs):

- The **camping band** is `borderHazard.hazardZone + zoneDepth (200 px)` from any edge — exactly your "200 px from the erosion zone".
- Time inside accrues `_campTime`; outside it **decays at `decayRate` (0.5×/s) instead of resetting**, so dipping in and out doesn't cheese it.
- At `triggerSeconds` (20 s) a hunter wave fires: `burst` + `atPlayer` + `nearPlayer` side, drone-weighted, budget 90, trickling in over 2 s, with a red **"HUNTERS INBOUND"** banner. The timer re-arms to `trigger − repeat`, so staying camped brings the next squad every `repeatSeconds` (12 s).
- It reuses the whole Task 7 pipeline (`ChooseSpawns` → `EnqueueWave`), so budget/cell-cap accounting and release-time positioning all apply. Everything is tunable in the JSON, including the hunter composition (`weights` accepts asteroids too, if you ever want a rock avalanche instead).

Worth playtesting alongside: whether 20 s / 12 s feels right, and whether drones alone are threatening enough in a corner — bruisers at weight ~0.3 would raise the stakes.

That leaves **Task 8** (the environment VFX/PAL rework) as the last sprint item before the deferred grenade perf pass. Ready when you are.

Fixed — the playable field is back to 5760×3240, and the extra space is now a proper **spawn ring outside it**.

## How it works now

- `world.spawnMargin: 500` defines a ring beyond the playable bounds (negative coordinates and past width/height). **All wave spawning moved out there**: `SidePoint` (patterns), `FindSpawnPosition` (scattered + fallback), and the mothership. Since the camera clamps to the playable field, anything in the ring is off-screen *by construction* — which is exactly what makes nearPlayer corner entries work.
- The subtle problem this created: `BorderHazardSystem` damps, pushes, and hard-clamps every moving body into `[0,W]×[0,H]` — a ring spawn would be teleported to the edge on its first frame. So ring spawns get an **`InboundSpawn` tag** that exempts them from both hazard passes (containment *and* erosion — without the erosion skip, the depth math would read "outside" as "deep in the rim" and eat them before they arrive). The tag is removed the moment the body crosses into the field, after which it's contained like everything else. The player never gets the tag, so they can't wander out.
- Two loose ends covered: fragments of a body shattered while still inbound inherit the tag (bullets can reach the ring, and untagged fragments would have snapped to the edge), and `AlienPrefab.Spawn` now returns its entity so the tagging works for aliens too.

Nothing else moved: border zone, hazard rim, camping band, camera, and the vortex all still work off the same 5760×3240 field as before. The demo is untouched (it spawns inside its own bounds and never tags anything).

One tunable to be aware of: `spawnMargin: 500` comfortably fits the largest asteroids (boulder ~200 px radius × size mult), but if you ever add something bigger, the ring needs to grow with it. Bodies enter visibly crossing the border — natural-looking, since they're moving inward at spawn speed.

Ready to pick up **Task 8** (environment VFX: PAL warp, vortex gusts, rim rework + projectile eating) whenever you say go.

**Task 8 is complete — all four projects build clean.** This was the big one; here's what landed across its three parts.

## 8a — PAL warp capability
New optional `IPostEffects` interface in the engine ([IPostEffects.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IPostEffects.cs)) with a single `Distort(regionMin, regionMax, gridX, gridY, sourceOf)` — "the pixel at p is resampled from `sourceOf(p)`". `SkiaRenderer` implements it by snapshotting the region and redrawing it as a warped triangle mesh (`DrawVertices` with an image shader, `SKBlendMode.Src`) — no SKSL, which is the safe path on the pinned SkiaSharp 2.88.7. The renderer now receives the `SKSurface` (needed for `Snapshot`) instead of just its canvas. Callers feature-detect with `renderer as IPostEffects` and no-op if unsupported, so the engine keeps its zero-toolkit-dependency rule.

## 8b — vortex gusts + swirl
`VortexSystem.FieldVelocity(pos)` exposes the *live* terminal drift (reusing the sim's own math, so the visual can't lie about the field). New `VortexFx` owns sporadic gust motes advected along it, drawn as fading streaks — genuinely sparse/slow at the calm eye, dense/fast further out — plus a bright eye core and an `IPostEffects` swirl warp on the eye. The old static spiral-arm `DrawEnvironment` is deleted.

## 8c — border rim
- **Red strips gone.** Primary cue is now a full-screen **red tint that deepens with the player's depth into the rim** (screen-space, no PAL — the signal you actually read).
- **Secondary:** a subtle heat-haze `Distort` shimmer on whichever world edges are on-screen — self-gating, since edges are only visible when you're near a border.
- **Rim eats projectiles:** `BorderHazardSystem` now skips bullets/piercing in the damp/push/clamp *and* erosion passes, and destroys any projectile crossing the world bounds with a fizzle (took a `ParticleEffects` dep). No more bullets piling against an invisible wall.

All new knobs are in `game_config.json` under `vortexFx` and the extended `borderHazard`.

## Two things to check when you playtest
1. **Warp orientation (the real risk):** the GL surface is `GRSurfaceOrigin.BottomLeft`. If `Snapshot` round-trips vertically flipped, warp regions will look upside-down. I can't verify without a display — it's the first thing to eyeball. If flipped, the fix is a one-line Y-flip on the texcoords in `SkiaRenderer.Distort`.
2. **Frame time:** the vortex warp snapshots a ~1240px region every frame, and the rim adds up to 4 edge strips near a wall. Worth watching — it feeds directly into the deferred grenade FPS task, which is now the only remaining item in the sprint.

All four build clean. Both parts done:

## Wider at corners
`CampZoneDepth(p)` now computes exposure from distance to the nearest *vertical* edge (`dx`) and nearest *horizontal* edge (`dy`) separately. It's the max of two terms:
- **Edge band** — `min(dx,dy) < band` (the old uniform strip, `band = hazardZone + zoneDepth`).
- **Corner square** — when *both* `dx` and `dy` are within `band × cornerScale`, an extra region keyed on `max(dx,dy)`. So a diagonal spot like "1.3×band from both walls" — which the flat edge band misses entirely — now registers as camping, deepening toward the actual corner.

`cornerScale: 1.8` means the corner reaches ~80% further in than a flat wall. Both the trigger (`inZone = depth > 0`) and the visual read from this same function, so they can't disagree.

## Exposure indicator
`DrawCampCue` draws a **grey full-screen filter** — deliberately a different color from the red erosion tint — that appears the instant you enter the zone (floor 30% intensity) and **deepens as the hunter timer fills** (`campTime / triggerSeconds`), then eases back out as the timer decays when you leave. Alongside it, a top-center **countdown**: `EXPOSED — HUNTERS 3s` ticking toward the next wave. Both fade with the same intensity, and the whole cue is gated off during game-over so it doesn't freeze on-screen.

New knobs in `campingResponse`: `cornerScale: 1.8` and `tintMaxAlpha: 70`. Your live-tuned values (trigger 3s, the richer weight mix) are untouched — though heads up, at `triggerSeconds: 3` the countdown will read "3s… 2s… 1s" fast, and the grey filter ramps to full in 3 seconds; if that feels too twitchy, `triggerSeconds` is the dial. Your call whether to keep the deferred grenade-perf task next or playtest this first.

## The ram
Root cause was a config interaction: the boss holds at `preferredRange: 750`, but the ram gate required `dist ≥ ramChargeMinDist: 900`. The boss is *never* that far (it actively cruises inward to 750), so the gate never passed — and each time it failed, the code reset the full 6s cooldown anyway, so the ram was permanently dead.

Two-part fix:
- **Logic** ([BossSystem.cs](GameEngine/Gameplay/Systems/BossSystem.cs)): when the ram is off cooldown but the player is *too close* for a run-up, it now retries in 0.4s instead of burning the whole cooldown on a no-op. So the ram fires the moment there's runway, rather than waiting a fresh 6s.
- **Config**: lowered `ramChargeMinDist` to `350` (below `preferredRange`), so from its standoff the boss reliably lunges. It'll now ram roughly every 6s (weakened as skill cells die). If that's too aggressive, raise `ramChargeMinDist` back up — but keep it **under** `preferredRange` or you'll reintroduce the dead-ram bug.

## barrageRayMass
The barrage reused the `cannon_alien` weapon for visuals/TTL, so its rays inherited that weapon's `mass: 500` — no independent damage dial. Now:
- New `BulletData.MassOverride` (nullable) threads a per-bullet impact mass through `SpawnBullet` → `OnBulletHit`, which prefers it over the weapon's `Mass`.
- New `boss.barrageRayMass` config (defaulted to `500` to match today's behaviour). Tune it to make the barrage hit harder or softer without touching the alien cannon that drones/bruisers fire.

Both are live-tunable, and neither touches anything outside the boss/bullet path.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-17 14:28 UTC

Fixed — all four build clean.

The cooldown widgets were stepping by a fixed `HudBarGap = 96px`, but labels like "SHOTGUN [RMB]" and "SLOW-MO [R]" are wider than that, so adjacent widgets ran into each other. Now the column pitch is **computed from the widest label**:

- `HudColumnWidth(r)` measures every `NAME [KEY]` label (weapons *and* skills) at their actual fonts and returns `max(barWidth, widestLabel) + 16px` padding. Both rows use that same pitch, so the HUD reads as one consistent grid and no two labels can overlap regardless of wording — if you rename a weapon or rebind a key, the spacing adjusts automatically.
- The weapon row lays out left-to-right from `HudWeapX`; the skill row is **right-aligned** to the same pitch (`ScreenW − pad − 3·col`), so it stays anchored to the screen's right edge.
- The two label fonts are now shared statics (`HudLabelFont`/`HudKeyFont`) so the measurement that drives spacing is exactly the one used to draw — they can't drift apart.

One thing worth a glance when you playtest at your actual window size: the weapon row grows rightward from x=200 and the skill row grows leftward from the right edge. On a wide window they sit comfortably apart; if you ever run a narrow window they could meet in the middle. If that happens, shrink the label font or the widget set — but at normal widths it's clear.

That plus `IRenderer` (+ optional `IPostEffects`) is the entire surface a backend must satisfy.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-07-17 15:09 UTC

I have the structural backbone already. Let me answer your conceptual questions now from confirmed facts, then I'll fold in the agents' mapping (dormant WinForms backend, input enums, loop) before writing the plan.

## Are you right that the UI has only two responsibilities?

Almost — it's **four small ones**, but "drawing + input" are the two big ones. A backend that implements `IGameWindow` + `IRenderer` owns:

1. **Window lifecycle** — create/size/title the OS window; expose `Width`/`Height`; flip `ShouldClose` when the user closes it; `Dispose` cleanup.
2. **Input forwarding** — `PollEvents()` drains OS events and fires the five callbacks (`KeyDown/KeyUp/MouseMoved/MouseButtonChanged/TextInput`), mapping platform keys → engine `KeyCode`.
3. **Drawing** — execute the immediate-mode `IRenderer` calls onto a surface.
4. **Presentation** — `Present()` shows the finished frame.

And critically, **what the UI is *not* responsible for**: the game loop and timing. `Program.cs` owns a hand-written loop and *calls* `PollEvents()`/`Present()` each frame — the window is a passive service. This is the one real friction point for WinForms, which normally runs its own message loop via `Application.Run`; your backend must instead pump messages on demand (`Application.DoEvents()`) inside `PollEvents()`. No audio, no textures, no asset loading — correct, none of that is in the PAL.

## Does GDI+ have all the necessary tools?

**For `IRenderer` + `IGameWindow`: yes, completely.** Every primitive maps cleanly to `System.Drawing.Graphics`:

| Our API | GDI+ |
|---|---|
| `Begin(clear)` | `Graphics.Clear` |
| `Push/PopTransform` | matrix stack via `Graphics.Save/Restore` (or a `Matrix` stack) |
| `DrawLine` / `DrawPolygon` / `FillPolygon` | `Pen`/`Brush` + `DrawLine`/`DrawPolygon`/`FillPolygon` |
| `FillPath` (multi-contour, nonzero) | `GraphicsPath` (multiple figures) + `FillMode.Winding` |
| `DrawCircle` / `FillCircle` | `DrawEllipse` / `FillEllipse` |
| `DrawText` / `MeasureText` | `DrawString` / `MeasureString` (+ `StringFormat.GenericTypographic` to match top-left) |
| input events | Form `KeyDown/KeyUp/MouseMove/MouseDown/MouseUp/KeyPress` |
| present | blit a back-buffer `Bitmap` |

**The one gap is `IPostEffects.Distort`** — the vortex/rim swirl warp. It snapshots the framebuffer and remaps it through a *triangle mesh*, which GDI+ has no native equivalent for (Skia does it via `DrawVertices`). But I deliberately made `IPostEffects` **optional and feature-detected** (`renderer as IPostEffects`): a backend that doesn't implement it just returns null, and the warp is silently skipped. The gust streaks and the red/grey screen tints are plain `DrawLine`/`FillRect` and work fine. So a WinForms backend can **omit `IPostEffects` entirely** and lose nothing but the swirl-warp polish. (Interesting bonus: the WinForms back-buffer is already a CPU `Bitmap`, so if you ever want the warp, `Graphics.DrawImage` with per-cell 3-point affine parallelograms can *approximate* the mesh cheaply — no GPU readback needed. Worth deferring, not doing now.)

## The one structural wrinkle I've already confirmed

Every project targets `net8.0` (cross-platform). **WinForms requires `net8.0-windows`** and only runs on Windows. So the new backend must be its own project (`net8.0-windows`, `<UseWindowsForms>`), and the `Game` executable that references it must also target `net8.0-windows` for the Windows build. The dormant `Engine/Rendering/GameWindow.cs` is currently just `<Compile Remove>`'d from the UI-free engine — it should **move out** into the new platform project (it doesn't belong in the toolkit-free engine anyway). How `Program.cs` picks SDL-vs-WinForms (compile-time `#if WINDOWS` vs. runtime flag vs. a separate entry project) is the main design decision I want to pin down.

I'm waiting on the codebase mapping (the dormant `GameWindow.cs` contents, the `KeyCode`/`MouseButton` enums, and the exact `Program.cs` construction site) to ground the plan and the backend-selection recommendation. I'll write the plan once that lands.

---

# How the game's main loop drives the Platform Abstraction Layer (PAL)

The engine is **engine-driven** (its own `while` loop calls `PollEvents`/`Present` each frame) — NOT message-pump driven. Everything routes through two PAL interfaces in the UI-free engine library: `IGameWindow` and `IRenderer`. The SDL backend is a separate assembly. A dormant WinForms scaffold already exists, and the whole codebase is written in anticipation of exactly the backend you're planning.

---

## 1. `Game/Program.cs` — entry point + hand-written main loop

File: `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Game/Program.cs` (top-level statements, 86 lines).

**Backend construction is direct, not via a factory or interface.** It hard-references the concrete SDL type (`using AsteroidsEngine.Platform.Sdl;` at line 14):

- Line 26: `var (W, H) = SdlGameWindow.QueryDisplaySize();` — static probe of the display before the window exists.
- Line 27: `using var window = new SdlGameWindow("Asteroids on Steroids", W, H, fullscreen: true);` — the window is constructed by directly `new`-ing the concrete `SdlGameWindow`. There is **no factory, no `IGameWindow` variable, no WINDOWS/SDL conditional selection.** The local `window` is statically typed as `SdlGameWindow`.

**Input wiring** (lines 28-33) — the window's C# events are subscribed to an `InputSystem`:
```csharp
var input = new InputSystem();
window.KeyDown += k =&gt; input.OnKeyDown(k);
window.KeyUp += k =&gt; input.OnKeyUp(k);
window.MouseMoved += p =&gt; input.OnMouseMove(p);
window.MouseButtonChanged += (b, pr) =&gt; input.OnMouseButton(b, pr);
window.TextInput += s =&gt; input.OnTextInput(s);
```

**Screen size**: `W`/`H` come from `SdlGameWindow.QueryDisplaySize()` (line 26) and are passed into `GameContext` (line 37: `new GameContext(config, shapes, input, W, H)`).

**Timing** (lines 43-46): `const double FixedDt = 1.0 / 120.0;`, `var fixedStep = new FixedTimestep(FixedDt);`, and a `Stopwatch`.

**The main loop verbatim** (lines 50-83):
```csharp
while (!window.ShouldClose)
{
    window.PollEvents();

    long now = sw.ElapsedTicks;
    double frameTime = (double)(now - lastTicks) / Stopwatch.Frequency;
    lastTicks = now;

    input.BeginFrame();

    // Fixed-step updates. Esc is handled by the states (menu quits, PlayingState pauses); a state
    // sets ctx.QuitRequested to exit.
    int steps = fixedStep.Advance(frameTime);
    for (int i = 0; i &lt; steps; i++)
    {
        IGameState? next = state.Update(FixedDt);
        if (next is not null)
        {
            state.Exit();
            state = next;
            state.Enter();
        }
    }
    if (ctx.QuitRequested) break;

    // Render at the sub-step alpha position.
    state.Draw(window.Renderer, fixedStep.Alpha);
    window.Present();

    // Soft frame cap: sleep until the next 120 Hz slot if we finished early.
    double elapsed = (double)(sw.ElapsedTicks - now) / Stopwatch.Frequency;
    int sleepMs = (int)((1.0 / 120.0 - elapsed) * 1000);
    if (sleepMs &gt; 1) Thread.Sleep(sleepMs);
}

state.Exit();
```

Per-frame sequence confirming your expected order: `window.PollEvents()` (line 52) → `input.BeginFrame()` (58) → `fixedStep.Advance(frameTime)` (62) → `state.Update(FixedDt)` in a step loop (65) → `state.Draw(window.Renderer, fixedStep.Alpha)` (76) → `window.Present()` (77).

- **`IRenderer` is obtained from the window** via the `window.Renderer` property (line 76), passed into `state.Draw`. The loop never touches a concrete renderer.
- **Loop termination**: `while (!window.ShouldClose)` (line 50), plus an internal `if (ctx.QuitRequested) break;` (73) — a game state sets `ctx.QuitRequested` to exit, and the window sets `ShouldClose` on an OS quit event.

---

## 2. `Platform/Sdl/SdlGameWindow.cs` — the reference backend to mirror

File: `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/SdlGameWindow.cs` (257 lines). `public sealed unsafe class SdlGameWindow : IGameWindow` (line 26).

**Public PAL surface** (lines 38-47):
```csharp
public int  Width       { get; }
public int  Height      { get; }
public bool ShouldClose =&gt; _shouldClose;
public IRenderer Renderer =&gt; _skiaRenderer;

public event Action&lt;EngineKey&gt;?         KeyDown;
public event Action&lt;EngineKey&gt;?         KeyUp;
public event Action&lt;Vector2&gt;?           MouseMoved;
public event Action&lt;EngineMouse, bool&gt;? MouseButtonChanged;
public event Action&lt;string&gt;?            TextInput;
```
`Renderer` returns the private `SkiaRenderer` field (line 41) — this is exactly the `window.Renderer` the loop reads.

**Constructor wiring** (lines 59-116, quoting the load-bearing tail). Init order: SDL init → optional fullscreen mode probe → set GL attributes → create window → create GL context → make current → create `GRGlInterface` → `GRContext.CreateGl` → describe default framebuffer → create `SKSurface` → `new SkiaRenderer(...)`:
```csharp
_grContext = GRContext.CreateGl(glInterface)
    ?? throw new InvalidOperationException("GRContext.CreateGl returned null");

// Describe the default framebuffer: id=0, internal format GL_RGBA8 (0x8058).
var fbInfo = new GRGlFramebufferInfo(0, 0x8058);
var rt     = new GRBackendRenderTarget(width, height, sampleCount: 0, stencilBits: 8, fbInfo);

// BottomLeft: OpenGL's origin is bottom-left; Skia's is top-left.
_surface = SKSurface.Create(_grContext, rt, GRSurfaceOrigin.BottomLeft, SKColorType.Rgba8888)
    ?? throw new InvalidOperationException("SKSurface.Create returned null");

_skiaRenderer = new SkiaRenderer(_surface, width, height);   // needs the surface for snapshot-based post FX
```
The renderer is thus bound to the `SKSurface` at construction time. GL attribute setup is at lines 78-82 (OpenGL 3.3 core + 8-bit stencil + double buffer); vsync is disabled at line 96 (`_sdl.GLSetSwapInterval(0)` — the loop does its own frame cap).

**`QueryDisplaySize`** (static, lines 50-57): inits SDL video and reads `GetCurrentDisplayMode`, returning `(1920,1080)` as a fallback. A WinForms backend would replace this with `Screen.PrimaryScreen.Bounds`.

**`PollEvents()`** (lines 118-162) drains SDL events in a `while (_sdl.PollEvent(ref ev) != 0)` loop and switches on `EventType`, invoking the callbacks:
- `Quit` → `_shouldClose = true;` (line 126) — this is the only place `ShouldClose` is set.
- `Keydown` (128-143): maps sym via `MapKey`, fires `KeyDown?.Invoke(...)` when not a repeat; also derives a printable char via `SdlSymToChar` and fires `TextInput` (suppressed when Ctrl/Alt held).
- `Keyup` (144-147): `KeyUp?.Invoke(...)`.
- `Mousemotion` (148-149): `MouseMoved?.Invoke(new Vector2(ev.Motion.X, ev.Motion.Y));`.
- `Mousebuttondown`/`up` (151-158): button 1→`EngineMouse.Left`, button 3→`EngineMouse.Right`, firing `MouseButtonChanged` with a pressed bool.

**`Present()`** (lines 164-169):
```csharp
public void Present()
{
    _surface.Canvas.Flush();
    _grContext.Flush();
    _sdl.GLSwapWindow(_window);
}
```

**`MapKey`** (SDL sym → `KeyCode`, lines 184-206): lowercase `a-z` (97-122) are up-cased to the engine's uppercase codes via `(EngineKey)(sym - 32)`; digits map straight through; arrows/space/escape/enter/tab/backspace/brackets and Ctrl/Shift/Alt (both sides) are mapped explicitly; everything else → `null`. (Note: this exists precisely because SDL syms don't line up with the engine enum — WinForms `Keys` **do** line up, see section 6.)

**`Dispose()`** (lines 241-255): disposes `_skiaRenderer`, `_surface`, `_grContext`, then deletes the GL context, destroys the window, and quits SDL.

## 3. Project / assembly layout

The SDL backend is a **separate project that references the engine**, and both `Game` and the demo reference that backend project. Everything targets **`net8.0`** (plain, no `-windows`). There is **no `&lt;UseWindowsForms&gt;` and no OS-specific TargetFramework anywhere.**

- **Engine** `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/AsteroidsEngine.csproj`: `net8.0`, `AllowUnsafeBlocks`, no external UI packages. Its `&lt;ItemGroup&gt;` explicitly *excludes* `Platform/**`, `Demos/**`, `GameConfig/**`, `Game/**`, `Gameplay/**`, and specifically `Engine/Rendering/GameWindow.cs` (line 30, comment: "Dormant future WinForms backend; compiled only under the WINDOWS symbol."). Header comment (lines 4-6) literally states: *"Platform backends (SDL/Skia now, WinForms/GDI+ later) live in separate assemblies and implement the PAL interfaces."*
- **SDL backend** `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/Engine.Platform.Sdl.csproj`: `net8.0`, `AllowUnsafeBlocks=true`, `RootNamespace=AsteroidsEngine.Platform.Sdl`. `ProjectReference` → `../../AsteroidsEngine.csproj`. `PackageReference` → `Silk.NET.SDL` 2.21.0 and `SkiaSharp` 2.88.7. Comment (lines 4-6): *"The engine itself depends on neither SDL nor Skia; only this assembly does."*
- **Game** `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Game/AsteroidsGame.csproj`: `OutputType=Exe`, `net8.0`. `ProjectReference`s to `AsteroidsEngine.csproj`, `Platform/Sdl/Engine.Platform.Sdl.csproj`, `GameConfig/GameConfig.csproj`, `Gameplay/AsteroidsGameplay.csproj`. `PackageReference` → `SkiaSharp.NativeAssets.Linux.NoDependencies` 2.88.7 (the runtime native Skia lib).

**Where a `Engine.Platform.WinForms` project slots in**: a new `net8.0-windows` project with `&lt;UseWindowsForms&gt;true&lt;/UseWindowsForms&gt;`, `ProjectReference` → `AsteroidsEngine.csproj`, implementing `IGameWindow` + `IRenderer` (GDI+). `Game` would then reference it, and `Program.cs` line 27 would need a way to pick a backend (today it hard-codes `new SdlGameWindow(...)`; there's currently no factory/DI seam, so backend selection would be a new decision point). Note the native-asset package in Game is Linux-specific — a Windows target would swap it.

---

## 4. `FixedTimestep` and the "who owns the loop" question

File: `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Core/FixedTimestep.cs` (44 lines). Plain accumulator:
- `Advance(realDelta)` (lines 31-39): adds elapsed time, clamps `_acc` to `_maxAccum` (default 0.25s, anti "spiral of death"), then `while (_acc &gt;= Step) { _acc -= Step; steps++; }` and returns `steps`.
- `Alpha` (line 42): `(float)(_acc / Step)` — the render interpolation factor passed to `state.Draw(..., fixedStep.Alpha)`.

**The loop is external-`while`, engine-driven.** `Game/Program.cs` owns a `while (!window.ShouldClose)` loop that explicitly calls `window.PollEvents()` and `window.Present()` every iteration. This is the critical mismatch for your plan: **WinForms normally owns its own message loop via `Application.Run`**, but here nothing calls `Application.Run`. A WinForms `IGameWindow.PollEvents()` implementation would need to pump the message queue manually (e.g. `Application.DoEvents()`, or drain messages via `PeekMessage`) rather than yielding control to `Application.Run`, so the engine keeps driving.

**Two dormant precedents for the WinForms model already exist** (both compile-excluded from the engine build):
- `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Core/GameLoop.cs` — a **thread-based** loop (`Start()` spins a background `Thread` running `Loop()`) with an `OnDraw` callback and `Stop()`. Its per-frame body (lines 90-118) mirrors `Program.cs` but has no `PollEvents`/`Present` (WinForms would pump on the UI thread). It is referenced only by the dormant `GameWindow`.
- `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/GameWindow.cs` — a full **`#if WINDOWS` WinForms `Form`** scaffold (entire file wrapped in `#if WINDOWS ... #endif`, lines 1/141). It owns front/back `Bitmap` double-buffers swapped via `Interlocked.Exchange` (lines 91-92), wires WinForms `KeyDown`/`KeyUp`/`MouseMove`/`MouseDown`/`MouseUp` to `InputSystem` (lines 64-68), blits the front buffer in `OnPaint` (line 113), suppresses background erase (line 117), and calls `_loop.Stop()` on `FormClosing` (line 71). **Note**: this scaffold uses the *thread + `Invalidate`* model and registers `_loop.OnDraw`, which is architecturally different from the current SDL/`Program.cs` synchronous `PollEvents → Draw → Present` model. It is not wired to `IGameWindow` and predates the current PAL — treat it as a reference for GDI+ buffer mechanics, not as the integration contract. The live contract to implement is `IGameWindow` (`/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IGameWindow.cs`, lines 17-38) + `IRenderer` (`/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IRenderer.cs`, lines 22-54).

## 5. The demo entry — a second direct consumer

File: `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs` (687 lines; top-level statements + `DemoSession`/`DemoRenderer` classes).

**Yes — it ALSO constructs `SdlGameWindow` directly.** Line 31: `var (W, H) = SdlGameWindow.QueryDisplaySize();` and line 33: `using var window = new SdlGameWindow("Asteroids — Destruction Sandbox", W, H, fullscreen: true);`. Same input wiring (lines 35-39) and same `using AsteroidsEngine.Platform.Sdl;` (line 29).

Its loop (lines 74-134) is the same shape as the game's: `window.PollEvents()` → `input.BeginFrame()` → `fixedStep.Advance` / `session.Update` → draw via `window.Renderer` (e.g. line 120 `window.Renderer.Begin(...)`, line 126 `renderer.Draw(window.Renderer, ...)`, line 128 `editor.Draw(window.Renderer, ...)`) → `window.Present()` (line 129). It exits on `input.IsPressed(KeyCode.Escape)` → `break` (line 93) rather than `window.ShouldClose` alone. `Demos/AsteroidDemo/AsteroidDemo.csproj` references the same four projects incl. `Engine.Platform.Sdl.csproj` (line 13), `net8.0`, `SkiaSharp.NativeAssets.Linux.NoDependencies`.

So there are **two** consumers that hard-`new` `SdlGameWindow` (`Game/Program.cs:27` and `Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs:33`). Any backend-selection seam you introduce must account for both, or the demo stays SDL-only.

## Bonus — `KeyCode` alignment (relevant to WinForms mapping)

File: `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Input/KeyCode.cs`. The enum values are deliberately set to match `System.Windows.Forms.Keys`. The header comment (lines 3-6) says: *"Values intentionally match System.Windows.Forms.Keys so GameWindow can cast directly: `inputSystem.OnKeyDown((KeyCode)e.KeyCode)`."* The dormant WinForms `GameWindow.cs` does exactly this (line 64: `_input.OnKeyDown((KeyCode)(int)e.KeyCode)`). So a WinForms backend needs no `MapKey` switch — a direct cast suffices, unlike the SDL backend's `MapKey` (SdlGameWindow.cs:184-206). `MouseButton` (KeyCode.cs:51-56) values (Left=1, Right=2, Middle=4) match `System.Windows.Forms.MouseButtons`.

**Summary of the seams a WinForms backend must satisfy**: implement `IGameWindow` (`Width`/`Height`/`ShouldClose`/`Renderer` + 5 input events + `PollEvents`/`Present` + `Dispose`) and `IRenderer` (Begin/PushTransform/PopTransform/DrawLine/DrawPolygon/FillPolygon/FillPath/DrawCircle/FillCircle/DrawText/MeasureText/End) with GDI+, provide a static display-size probe analogous to `QueryDisplaySize`, pump the Win32 message queue inside `PollEvents` instead of calling `Application.Run`, and add a backend-selection seam at `Game/Program.cs:27` (and optionally `Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs:33`), since today both hard-code `new SdlGameWindow(...)`.</result>

# Platform Abstraction Layer (PAL) — Exploration Report

All paths absolute. The engine library (`AsteroidsEngine.csproj`, net8.0) is deliberately UI-toolkit-free; backends live in separate assemblies (`Platform/Sdl/`). A GDI+/WinForms backend would either be a new sibling assembly or (as the dormant file shows) compiled into the engine under a `WINDOWS` symbol.

---

## 1. `IGameWindow` — `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IGameWindow.cs`

Full interface verbatim (lines 17-38):

```csharp
public interface IGameWindow : IDisposable
{
    int  Width       { get; }
    int  Height      { get; }
    bool ShouldClose { get; }

    /// &lt;summary&gt;Immediate-mode renderer backed by this window's drawing surface.&lt;/summary&gt;
    IRenderer Renderer { get; }

    event Action&lt;KeyCode&gt;?           KeyDown;
    event Action&lt;KeyCode&gt;?           KeyUp;
    event Action&lt;Vector2&gt;?           MouseMoved;
    event Action&lt;MouseButton, bool&gt;? MouseButtonChanged;
    /// &lt;summary&gt;Fired for each SDL_TEXTINPUT event (UTF-8 characters typed).&lt;/summary&gt;
    event Action&lt;string&gt;?            TextInput;

    /// &lt;summary&gt;Drain pending OS events and fire input callbacks.&lt;/summary&gt;
    void PollEvents();

    /// &lt;summary&gt;Flush GPU commands and swap the front/back buffers.&lt;/summary&gt;
    void Present();
}
```

Notes for a new backend:
- Extends `IDisposable`.
- There is **no** `Title` property and **no** settable size — `Width`/`Height`/`ShouldClose` are get-only. Title is passed to the concrete constructor (SDL takes `string title` in its ctor); it is not part of the interface.
- No `Show()`/`Run()` on the interface; lifecycle is ctor + `PollEvents`/`Present`/`Dispose`.
- Event payload types: `KeyCode` and `MouseButton` are from `AsteroidsEngine.Engine.Input` (imported at line 2). `Vector2` is `System.Numerics`.

---

## 2. `IRenderer` and `IPostEffects`

### `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IRenderer.cs`

Full interface (lines 22-54) and the `FontSpec` struct (lines 60-70):

```csharp
public interface IRenderer
{
    void Begin(Color clear);

    void PushTransform(in Matrix3x2 transform);
    void PopTransform();

    void DrawLine(Vector2 a, Vector2 b, Color color, float width = 1f);

    void DrawPolygon(ReadOnlySpan&lt;Vector2&gt; verts, Color color, float width = 1f);
    void FillPolygon(ReadOnlySpan&lt;Vector2&gt; verts, Color color);

    void FillPath(ReadOnlySpan&lt;Vector2&gt; verts, ReadOnlySpan&lt;int&gt; contourLengths, Color color);

    void DrawCircle(Vector2 center, float radius, Color color, float width = 1f);
    void FillCircle(Vector2 center, float radius, Color color);

    void DrawText(string text, Vector2 topLeft, Color color, in FontSpec font);

    Vector2 MeasureText(string text, in FontSpec font);

    void End();
}

public readonly struct FontSpec
{
    public readonly string Family;
    public readonly float  Size;
    public readonly bool   Bold;

    public FontSpec(string family, float size, bool bold = false)
    {
        Family = family; Size = size; Bold = bold;
    }
}
```

Key conventions documented in the file header: Y-down screen space; `Fill/DrawPolygon` take **convex** polygons; `FillPath` fills a multi-contour path as ONE region with nonzero winding (no AA seams between adjacent contours); antialiasing is a backend concern (on by default); `DrawText` positions by TOP-LEFT (backend handles baseline). No `DrawImage` yet.

The active Skia implementation confirms the exact same signature set — `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/SkiaRenderer.cs`:
`class SkiaRenderer : IRenderer, IPostEffects, IDisposable` (line 12), with `Begin` (34), `End` (40), `PushTransform` (42), `PopTransform` (49), `DrawLine` (51), `DrawPolygon` (57), `FillPolygon` (65), `FillPath` (73), `DrawCircle` (91), `FillCircle` (97), `DrawText` (103), `MeasureText` (112), `Distort` (145), `Dispose` (207).

### `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Rendering/IPostEffects.cs`

Full interface (lines 11-21):

```csharp
public interface IPostEffects
{
    void Distort(Vector2 regionMin, Vector2 regionMax, int gridX, int gridY, Func&lt;Vector2, Vector2&gt; sourceOf);
}
```

Behavior per the doc comment: it is optional/feature-detected via `renderer as IPostEffects` (callers skip when null, preserving the zero-toolkit rule and headless backends). `Distort` warps the frame drawn so far within screen-space rect `[regionMin, regionMax]`: the pixel at screen point `p` is resampled from `sourceOf(p)` (also screen space). `gridX`×`gridY` is the warp-mesh resolution. Must be called in screen space (no camera transform pushed); no-op for a degenerate region. Skia implements it via a framebuffer snapshot warped over a triangle mesh (implementation at `SkiaRenderer.cs:145`; needs the `SKSurface` for the snapshot, per `SdlGameWindow.cs:115`). A GDI+ backend can implement `IPostEffects` optionally — omitting it is legal and the effect is simply skipped.

---

## 3. Input — KeyCode, MouseButton, InputSystem

### `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Input/KeyCode.cs`

Full `KeyCode` enum (lines 8-49). Critically, the header comment (lines 3-7) states values **intentionally match `System.Windows.Forms.Keys`** so a WinForms window can cast directly: `inputSystem.OnKeyDown((KeyCode)e.KeyCode)`.

```csharp
public enum KeyCode
{
    // Alphabet
    A = 65, B = 66, C = 67, D = 68, E = 69, F = 70,
    G = 71, H = 72, I = 73, J = 74, K = 75, L = 76,
    M = 77, N = 78, O = 79, P = 80, Q = 81, R = 82,
    S = 83, T = 84, U = 85, V = 86, W = 87, X = 88,
    Y = 89, Z = 90,

    // Digits
    D0 = 48, D1 = 49, D2 = 50, D3 = 51, D4 = 52,
    D5 = 53, D6 = 54, D7 = 55, D8 = 56, D9 = 57,

    // Navigation
    Left  = 37, Up = 38, Right = 39, Down = 40,

    // Common
    Space = 32, Enter = 13, Escape = 27, Tab = 9, Back = 8,

    // Brackets / punctuation (SDL sym = ASCII)
    LeftBracket = 91, RightBracket = 93,

    // Modifiers
    Shift = 16, Control = 17, Alt = 18,
    ShiftLeft = 160, ShiftRight = 161,

    // Function keys
    F1 = 112, ... F12 = 123,
}
```

`MouseButton` enum (same file, lines 51-56) — its values also match `System.Windows.Forms.MouseButtons`-style bit values:

```csharp
public enum MouseButton
{
    Left   = 1,
    Right  = 2,
    Middle = 4,
}
```

**"EngineMouse"** is not a separate type — it is a `using` alias for `MouseButton` used only inside the SDL backend: `using EngineMouse = AsteroidsEngine.Engine.Input.MouseButton;` (`SdlGameWindow.cs:7`; also `EngineKey = ...KeyCode` at line 6). The `IGameWindow.MouseButtonChanged` event carries `MouseButton`.

### `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Input/InputSystem.cs`

`sealed class InputSystem` (line 13). Two-thread design: platform/UI thread writes `_pending` under a lock; the game thread calls `BeginFrame()` once per frame to commit and compute press/release deltas.

Ingest methods (called from the window's event callbacks):
- `void OnKeyDown(KeyCode key)` (32) — `_pending.Add`
- `void OnKeyUp(KeyCode key)` (33) — `_pending.Remove`
- `void OnMouseMove(Vector2 screenPosition)` (35)
- `void OnMouseButton(MouseButton button, bool pressed)` (37) — handles Left/Right only (Middle ignored)
- `void OnTextInput(string chars)` (47) — appends to `_textPending`

Frame commit:
- `void BeginFrame()` (51) — clears per-frame press/release sets; diffs `_pending` vs `_committed` to fill `_pressedThisFrame`/`_releasedThisFrame`; copies `_committed = _pending`; commits mouse position/buttons; commits `_textThisFrame` and clears `_textPending`.

Polling API:
- `bool SuppressKeyboard { get; set; }` (82) — blocks WASD/hotkeys while a text widget is active; Back/Enter/Escape always pass (`IsEditingKey`, 84); modifiers always pass (`IsModifier`, 87).
- `bool IsHeld(KeyCode)` (93)
- `bool IsPressed(KeyCode)` (97) — edge, one frame
- `bool ConsumePress(KeyCode)` (102) — like IsPressed but removes from `_pressedThisFrame`
- `bool IsReleased(KeyCode)` (110)
- `bool IsPressedThisFrame(params KeyCode[] keys)` (113)
- `Vector2 MouseScreen` (116) — committed mouse position in pixels
- `bool IsMouseLeft` (122) — committed AND not `SuppressMouseLeft`
- `bool IsMouseLeftRaw` (128) — ignores suppression (for UI layer)
- `bool IsMouseRight` (130)
- `bool SuppressMouseLeft { get; set; }` (137)
- `string TextThisFrame` (143)

**Wiring** (window events → InputSystem) is done in application code, not in the window or engine. Reference wiring in `/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Game/Program.cs:29-33` (identical block in `Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs:35-39`):

```csharp
window.KeyDown            += k =&gt; input.OnKeyDown(k);
window.KeyUp              += k =&gt; input.OnKeyUp(k);
window.MouseMoved         += p =&gt; input.OnMouseMove(p);
window.MouseButtonChanged += (b, pr) =&gt; input.OnMouseButton(b, pr);
window.TextInput          += s =&gt; input.OnTextInput(s);
```

So a new backend only needs to raise the five `IGameWindow` events with the correct payloads; the app-level glue already routes them into `InputSystem`.
